Deinde resupinetur infirmus super dorsum suum, aut super latus sanum.	Then lay the patient on his back, or on his healthy side.
Deinde eleua cutim, quae est in interiori Titillici ad superiora cum digitis manus tuae sinistrae: et si iunctura dislocatur ad interiora.	Then lift the skin on the inner shoulder upward with the fingers of your left hand if the joint is dislocated inward.
Deinde igni Cauterium habens duo uerua.	Then heat a cautery iron with two prongs.
Cuius forma est haec.	In this shape.
Deinde cauteriza cutim, donec penetret eam usque ad latus aliud, et ueniet figura cauterizationis cum quatuor cauteriis.	Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates through to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will appear with four cauteries.
Et quandoque fit cauterizatio cum cauterio habente tria uerua, quare fit figura cauterizationis tunc sex cauteriorum: et sunt uerua secundum subtilitatem tentae.	Sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery iron having three prongs, and thus the figure of the cauterization will have six cauterizations; the prongs are as thin as a stretched thread.
Et haec est forma cauterii habentis tria uerua.	And this is the shape of the cautery iron with three prongs.
Et quandoque additur super hunc modum unum, quare sunt cauteria octo.	Sometimes one more is added to this method, so that there are eight cauteries.
Deinde pone super cauterium porros contritos cum sale.	Then apply crushed leeks with salt over the cauterized area.
Deinde fac adhaerere infirmum tranquillitati, ut non moueatur membrum tempore aliquo, donec confortetur.	Then keep the patient in stillness, so the limb does not move for a while, until it is strengthened.
Et si dislocatio est ad superiora, et raro fit illud, tunc cauteriza ipsum super humerum cauterio clauili, aut cauteriis multis punctando.	And if the dislocation is upward, which rarely happens, then cauterize the shoulder with a nail-shaped cautery or with many puncturing cauteries.
Nam iunctura firmatur, et remouetur humiditas: et sanatur infirmus.	For the joint is strengthened, the humor is removed, and the patient is healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Stomachum.	On the method of cauterizing the stomach.
Caput XXVIII.	Chapter 28.
Quando accidunt in Stomacho frigus et humiditates multae, donec extrahant ipsum a complexione sua, et multiplicentur catarri ad ipsum, et assiduas modos curationis, et non confert: tunc oportet ut resupinetur infirmus super dorsum suum, et extendat crura sua, et manus suas.	When cold and excessive humors occur in the stomach, to the extent that they disrupt its temperament, and phlegm increases, and regular treatments are ineffective, then the patient should be placed on his back, with his legs and arms extended.
Deinde cauteriza cum tribus cauteriis, cauterio sub cochleari pectoris quantitate digiti unius cum cauterio clauili, et duobus cauteriis inferius a duobus lateribus cauterii unius, donec ueniat figura cauteriorum triangulata.	Then cauterize with three cauteries: one under the breastbone the size of a single finger with a nail-shaped cautery, and two cauteries below on both sides of this cautery, until a triangular shape is formed by the cauteries.
Et elonga inter utraque ut non coniungantur, quando facient pus.	And leave space between each so that they do not merge when they form pus.
Et sit profunditas cauterii quantitas duarum tertiarum grossitudinis cutis.	Let the depth of the cautery be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
Et sit figura cauteriorum secundum hanc formam sine additione: et si uis cauteriza cauterio magno in medio stomachi secundum hanc formam: et sit cauterium quo fit hoc cauterium unum secundum figuram circuli secundum hanc formam.	Let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition; and if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach in this form, and let the cautery be circular in shape.
Et cauterizatur stomachus punctando ei qui terretur ab hoc cauterio: et est, ut signes super stomachum punctum secundum quantitatem, quam uis cum encaustro: deinde cauteriza ipsum cum cauterio puncti: deinde cura ipsum cum curatione, quae praecessit donec sanetur.	The stomach can be cauterized by puncturing for those who fear this cautery: mark a point on the stomach according to the desired size with ink, then cauterize with a pointed cautery, then treat it with the previous remedy until healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Epar frigidum.	On the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
Caput XXIX.	Chapter 29.
Quando accidit in Epate dolor ex frigiditate et humiditate, aut ex uentositate grossa, donec egrediatur a complexione sua naturali egressione superflua, et curatur infirmus, cum eo quod diximus, et non proficit in illo: tunc oportet ut resupinetur infirmus super ceruicem suam, et signes cum encaustro tria cauteria secundum hanc figuram, et hanc quantitatem eandem super Epar inferius ab hypocundriis, ubi peruenit cubitus hominis: et sit spacium quod est inter omne cauterium secundum grossitudinem digiti: et sit cauterium secundum longitudinem corporis rectum: et non comprimas manum tuam cum cauterio multum.	When pain occurs in the liver due to cold and moisture, or from thick winds, disrupting its natural balance by excess, and treatment as prescribed does not help, then the patient should lie on his back, and mark with ink three cauteries in this shape and this same size below the hypochondria, at the point where the elbow meets: allow space between each cautery the width of a finger, and let the cautery be straight in the length of the body; do not press your hand too hard with the cautery.
Et sit quantitas eius quod aduritur ex spissitudine cutis, quantitas medietatis eius non additum: et sit infirmus stans super pedes suos.	Let the amount burned be half the thickness of the skin, not more; and let the patient be standing on his feet.
Si autem non est stans, tunc sit iacens, qui iam extendit crura sua, et eleuauit brachia sua.	If he is not standing, then he should be lying down, with his legs extended and arms raised.
Haec est forma cauterii.	This is the shape of the cautery.
Et tibi quidem possibile est, ut cauterizes ista cauteria cum cauterio cultellari, quando tecum est subtilitas et prudentia in arte.	Indeed, it is possible to perform these cauterizations with a knife-like cautery, provided you possess skill and precision in the art.
Et custodi te, ut non ultime procedas in cauterizatione, et aduratur spissitudo cutis totius, quare aduratur corpus totum, et perueniat ad intestina: quoniam cutis illic est subtilis, scias ergo illud.	Be cautious not to go too deeply with the cauterization, so as not to burn the full thickness of the skin, for this would burn the entire body and reach the intestines, as the skin there is thin; know this well.
¶ De modo cauterizandi apostemata Epatis.	On the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
Caput XXX.	Chapter 30.
Quando accidit exitura, et uis scire, si illud apostema est in carne Epatis, aut in tunica eius: tunc si est in carne Epatis, inuadit infirmum dolor, et grauitas absque acuitate: et si est in tunica Epatis, cum dolore est acuitas uehemens: et uides iam, quia fatigauit medicos eius curatio.	When an abscess occurs and you wish to know if it is in the liver's flesh or its covering: if it is in the liver's flesh, the patient suffers dull pain and heaviness; if in the liver's covering, there is sharp, intense pain; and you see that its treatment has wearied the physicians.
Oportet ergo ut resupinet infirmus super ceruicem suam.	Thus, the patient should lie on his back.
Deinde figura locum apostematis cum encaustro: deinde ignias cauterium quod assimilatur radio.	Then mark the site of the abscess with ink, and heat a cautery shaped like a ray.
Et haec est forma eius.	And this is its shape.
Et cauteriza cum eo cauterium unum, donec comburatur cutis tota, et perueniat ad siphac, donec egrediatur sanies tota: deinde cura ipsum curatione exiturarum, donec sanetur.	Cauterize with it once, until the entire skin is burned and reaches the membrane, until all discharge is released; then treat it with the abscess remedy until healed.
Et non oportet ut hac cauterii specie utatur, nisi cuius studium in arte medicinae prolongatur: et per cuius manus concurrunt aegritudines istae cum experimento aliquotiens: tunc enim audeat super huiusmodi operationem.	And this type of cautery should not be used except by one experienced in the art of medicine and who has often encountered such illnesses; only then should he dare this procedure.
At uero dimittere ipsam, apud me est melius.	But truly, leaving it alone is, in my view, better.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Pleuresi.	On the method of cauterizing in cases of pleurisy.
Caput XXXI.	Chapter 31.
Dixerunt antiqui, cauterium cum radicibus aristolochiae ad Pleuresim frigidam secundum hunc modum.	The ancients said to use cautery with roots of aristolochia for cold pleurisy in the following manner.
Et est, ut recipias ex radicibus aristolochiae siccae longae, radicem unam longiorem, quae ex ea inuenitur, et sit sicut grossitudo digiti.	Take a long, dry root of aristolochia, selecting the longest available, approximately the thickness of a finger.
Deinde submerge eam in oleo: et accende ipsam in igne.	Then immerse it in oil and ignite it in fire.
Deinde cauteriza cauterio uno in eo quod est inter continuationem furculae cum collo, et duobus cauteriis paruis sub guidezi parum decliuibus ad partem, quae est sub barba.	Then apply one cautery at the point where the furcula meets the neck, and two smaller cauteries slightly downward below the chin.
Et duobus cauteriis etiam in eo, quod est inter costam quintam et sextam decliuibus ad posteriora parumper: et cauterio alio in medio pectoris, et alio supra stomachum.	And also apply two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, slanting slightly towards the back; one cautery at the center of the chest and another over the stomach.
Et tribus cauteriis a posterioribus: uno in eo quod est inter duas spatulas: et duobus cauteriis a duobus lateribus pectoris, inferius cauterio quod est inter duas spatulas.	And apply three cauteries on the back: one between the shoulder blades, and two on each side of the chest, below the cautery placed between the shoulder blades.
Et non oportet ut comprimas manum tuam cum cauterio, imo sit in manifesto cutis odorando.	Do not press your hand too hard with the cautery; instead, it should only be obvious enough by the smell of the burning skin.
Et iam dixerunt quidam antiqui, quod ex hominibus sunt qui utuntur cauterio ex ferro simili radio: et igniunt, et intus mittunt ipsum in eo quod est inter costas, donec perueniatur cum eo ad ipsum apostema, et egrediatur sanies: sicut diximus in apostemate Epatis.	Some of the ancients have said that certain practitioners use an iron cautery similar to a rod; they heat it, insert it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess, and let the discharge exit, as we mentioned in the case of a liver abscess.
Sed in hac perforatione cum cauterio est ex timore, quod aut moritur infirmus statim, aut accidit in loco fistula, cui non est sanatio.	But with this procedure there is a risk: either the patient dies immediately, or a fistula develops at the site, which is incurable.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Splenem Caput XXXII.	On the method of cauterizing the spleen. Chapter 32.
Quando tu curas aegritudinem splenis, cum eo quod diximus ex curatione in diuisione aegritudinum, et non confert curatio tua, tunc cauterium in ea est secundum tres modos, qui omnes sunt recti.	When you treat a disease of the spleen with the treatments we discussed in the division of diseases, and it does not yield to these treatments, cautery can be used in three ways, all of which are effective.
Quorum unus est, ut facias tria cauteria, aut quatuor lineando secundum longitudinem splenis secundum figuram cauteriorum Epatis, quorum praecessit figura.	One method is to create three or four cauteries in a line along the length of the spleen, in the same manner as the cauteries for the liver, as we previously described.
Et sit inter omne cauterium quantitas grossitudinis digiti, aut plus parum.	Let the space between each cautery be about the thickness of a finger, or a little more.
Et sit modus cauterii, quem diximus in cauterio epatis aequaliter.	Let the method of the cautery be exactly as we described in cauterizing the liver.
Et non comprimas manum tuam cum cauterio: et sit infirmus resupinus super dorsum suum.	Do not press your hand hard with the cautery, and have the patient lying on his back.
Et modus alius de cauterizatione est: ut ignias cauterium habens duo uerua, quod diximus in capitulo dislocationis humeri: et eleua cutem, quae est in directo splenis, ubi peruenit cubitus infirmi sinister: et sit eleuatio tua qua eleuas cutem secundum latitudinem corporis, ut cadant cauteria secundum longitudinem corporis.	Another method of cauterization is to heat a double-pronged cautery, as we discussed in the chapter on shoulder dislocation; lift the skin directly over the spleen, where the patient’s left elbow reaches, lifting it along the body’s width, so the cauteries fall along the body’s length.
Deinde intromitte duo uerua ignita ualde, donec cum eis penetres cutem a parte altera: deinde extrahe cauterium: fiunt ergo cauteria quatuor.	Then insert the two highly heated prongs until they pierce through to the other side of the skin; then remove the cautery, creating four cauteries.
Et si uis cauteriza cum cauterio alio habente tria uerua.	If you wish, you may cauterize with another cautery that has three prongs.
Deinde cura cauterium postquam dimittis ipsum emittere pus diebus multis: est enim magis conferens quamque reliqua quae praecesserunt ex curatione.	Then care for the cautery site, allowing it to discharge pus over many days, as it is more effective than other preceding treatments.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Hydropisi.	On the method of cauterizing for dropsy.
Caput XXXIII.	Chapter 33.
Cauterium non cadit in Hydropisi, nisi ascliti proprie.	Cautery is only applied in cases of ascitic dropsy specifically.
Quando tu curas Hydropicum cum modis curationis, quos diximus in diuisione, et non confert curatio, tunc oportet ut cauterizes ipsum quatuor cauteriis in circumitu umbilici, et cauterio uno super stomachum, et cauterio alio super epar, et cauterio super splenem, et cauteriis duobus post dorsum inter spondiles, et uno in directo pectoris, et alio in directo stomachi: et sit quantitas profunditatis cauterii propinqua spissitudini cutis.	When treating a dropsical patient with the previously described treatments and they prove ineffective, you should then cauterize with four cauteries around the navel, one cautery on the stomach, another over the liver, one on the spleen, two on the back between the vertebrae, one opposite the chest, and another opposite the stomach. The depth of the cautery should be close to the thickness of the skin.
Deinde dimitte cauterium apertum, ut emittat pus tempore longo.	Then leave the cautery site open so it may discharge pus over a long period.
Et non euacues infirmum a curatione post cauterium cum eo: quod oportet ut aggregentur ei duae intentiones: et festinabit ad ipsum sanatio cum auxilio Dei.	And do not abandon treatment for the patient after the cautery; it is necessary to combine two aims, and healing will hasten with God’s help.
Forma uero cauterii cum quo cauterizatur uenter, sit clauilis: secundum quod praecessit forma eius: et illius cum quo cauterizatur dorsum, sit oliuaris secundum quod praecessit eius forma.	The shape of the cautery used for the abdomen should be nail-like, as previously described, and the one used for the back should be olive-shaped, as previously specified.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Pedes, et Crura.	On the Method of Cauterizing Feet and Legs
Caput XXXIIII.	Chapter 34.
Quando apostemantur in Hydropico, et replentur aqua citrina: oportet ut cauterizes super dorsum Pedis in nocrati, quae est inter auricularem et anularem: et eleua manum tuam cum cauterio, et non torqueas ipsum: deinde eleua manum tuam: et non iteres ipsum omnino.	When swelling occurs in the dropsical person, and yellowish water fills the feet, it is necessary to cauterize the top of the foot, specifically on the area between the little toe and the ring toe. Raise your hand with the cautery tool, do not twist it, and then lift your hand; do not repeat the procedure at all.
Resudet enim aqua citrina, et sit cauterium secundum hanc formam.	This will cause the yellow water to sweat out, and the cautery should be applied as described.
Deinde fac super duo crura duo cauteria in omni crure, et fiat cauterium cum extremitate cultellari cauterii: et fiat cauterium secundum longitudinem cruris, unum sub genu, et alterum inferius eo, circiter medium cruris: et super omnem coxam cauteria duo: et dimitte cauterium apertum absque curatione tempore longo: ut resudet ex eo aliquod aquae: deinde cura ipsum cum reliquis quae diximus.	Then, apply two cauteries on each leg. Use the blade-like end of the cautery tool, applying it lengthwise along the leg, one below the knee and the other slightly lower, around the middle of the leg. Apply two cauteries on each thigh. Leave the cautery sites open without treatment for an extended time so that water may exude from them. Afterward, treat the area with the remedies previously mentioned.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in solutione Ventris.	On the Method of Cauterizing for Looseness of the Bowels
Caput XXXV.	Chapter 35.
Quando est solutio uentris ex frigore et humiditatibus, donec debilitet uirtutes retentiuam et digestiuam, quae sunt in stomacho et intestinis: et curatur illud cum modis curationis, et non sanatur: et uides infirmum tolerantem cauterium exuberantis uirtutis, tunc cauteriza ipsum cauterio magno super stomachum suum, secundum quod praecessit in cauterizatione stomachi cum cauterio circuli, et quatuor cauteriis in circumitu umbilici subtilibus, cum cauterio clauili subtili: et cauterio super alcatin supra alhosos magno, aut duobus cauteriis.	When there is looseness of the bowels due to cold and moisture, which weakens the stomach and intestinal retention and digestive functions, and if usual treatments fail, and the patient is strong enough to tolerate cauterization, apply a large cautery to the stomach, as previously described in stomach cauterization using a circular cautery. Apply four delicate cauteries around the navel, using a fine nail-like cautery tool, and another on the alcatin (just above the pubic bone), using a large cautery or two smaller ones.
Et si uides humiditates exuberantes, et infirmum tolerantem illud, tunc cauteriza ipsum cauterio super pectinem, et cauterio super omne ilium: et fortasse addes duo cauteria parua super stomachum prope magnum.	If you see an excess of moisture and the patient can tolerate it, cauterize over the pubic area and over each iliac crest. You may add two small cauteries on the stomach, close to the larger one.
Est enim curatio proficiens, cuius iuuamentum non errat.	This treatment is effective, providing reliable relief.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Hemorroidas.	On the Method of Cauterizing Hemorrhoids
Caput XXXVI.	Chapter 36.
Quando in ano sunt Hemorroides antiquae multae, aut una, et sunt ex humoribus grossis, frigidis, aut humiditatibus corruptis, et curantur cum eo, quod diximus in diuisione, et non confert curatio: tunc cauteriza tribus cauteriis super inferiorem spondilem dorsi sub almeidati parumper triangulatim, et cauterio sub umbilico quasi duobus digitis.	When there are old, multiple hemorrhoids in the anus, or even a single one, caused by thick, cold humors or corrupt moisture, and treatments have proven ineffective, cauterize with three cauteries on the lower vertebra of the back just below the waist in a triangular shape, and one cautery just two finger-widths below the navel.
Et si cogitas, quod stomachus eius infrigidatus sit, et cibus eius non digeratur, et faciem eius uides apostemari, tunc cauteriza eum super stomachum cauterio magno, secundum quod praecessit: et cauterio super Epar eius, et alio super Splenem ipsius, cum cauterio clauili: et dimitte cauterium apertum tempore aliquo: deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	If you suspect the patient's stomach is chilled and food is undigested, and you notice swelling in the face, then cauterize over the stomach with a large cautery as previously described, and also over the liver and spleen using a nail-like cautery. Leave the cautery site open for a while, then treat it until healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi althelul post abscisionem eorum.	On the Method of Cauterizing Althelul (Lesions or Ulcers) after Their Removal
Caput XXXVII.	Chapter 37.
Quando tu abscindis althelul, tunc ignias cauterium quod assimilatur radio.	When you remove althelul (lesions or ulcers), heat a cautery shaped like a rod.
Deinde intromittite ipsum ignitum in ipsum althelul abscisum: et ultima manum tuam, donec perueniat cauterium ad orificium uenae, ex qua currit sanguis: fac illud semel, aut bis.	Then insert the heated cautery into the cut althelul, pressing until it reaches the mouth of the vein from which blood flows; do this once or twice.
Si ergo althelul fuerint multa, tunc cauteriza unumquodque cauterio secundum quod narrauimus.	If there are multiple althelul, cauterize each one as described.
Deinde cura ea, cum eo quod confert eis ex unguentis, donec sanentur.	Then treat them with appropriate ointments until they heal.
Et si cauterizas eum cauterio magno super alcatin, est magis ultimum in iuuamento.	If you cauterize with a large cautery over the alcatin, this is the most beneficial method.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Fistulam in ano.	On the Method of Cauterizing a Fistula in the Anus
Caput XXXVIII.	Chapter 38.
Quando non obedit infirmus sectioni et operi quod narrauimus in loco suo, et terretur ab illo, fortasse sanatur cum cauterio.	When a patient is unwilling to undergo surgery and the procedure we discussed earlier, and if they are afraid of it, perhaps they can be cured with cauterization.
Cum ergo accidit alicui Fistula, et antiquatur, currit pus ex ea, et humiditates corruptae.	When someone has a fistula that has persisted for a long time, and pus and corrupted humors flow from it.
Dignius ergo quod oportet est, ut probes eam cum tenta subtili.	First, it is necessary to examine the fistula carefully with a fine probe.
Deinde cognosce quantitatem profunditatis eius cum tenta.	Then, assess its depth with the probe.
Deinde ignias cauterium, quod est simile radio.	Afterward, heat a rod-like cautery.
Deinde intromitte ipsum ignitum in ipsam Fistulam et quantitatem in qua intrauit clauus.	Then insert the heated cautery into the fistula to the depth of the insertion mark.
Et itera super eam cauterium, donec comburantur illa omnia corpora corrupta, semel, aut bis, aut ter, secundum quantitatem necessitatis tuae.	Repeat the cauterization over the affected area until all the corrupted tissue is burned, doing this once, twice, or thrice, depending on the need.
Et custodi te ab adustione nerui, si est illic, aut uenae magnae: aut si Fistula uadit ad corpus uesicae, aut ad corpus intestini, tunc custodi te ab istis locis omnibus.	Be cautious not to burn any nerves, if present, or major veins. If the fistula is near the bladder or intestines, take care to avoid these areas entirely.
Et non facias illud, nisi quando fistula est in loco carnoso: et cogitas, quia non est penetrans.	Only perform this procedure when the fistula is in fleshy tissue and you believe it does not penetrate deeply.
Deinde cura locum usquequo sanetur.	Then treat the area until it is fully healed.
Si autem sigillatur locus, et abscinduntur ab eo materiae, et remanet sic tempore longo: tunc scias, quia iam sanatus est integre.	If the area seals and discharges material for an extended period, this indicates complete healing.
Et si non abscindunt ab eo materiae, tunc scias quia est penetrans, aut in profundo eius est os corruptum, aut quasi illud ex illis: quorum rememoratio ueniet in loco suo.	If it fails to discharge material, then know that the fistula may be deep, possibly involving decayed bone or similar structures, which will be discussed later.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Renes.	On the Method of Cauterizing the Kidneys
Caput XXXIX.	Chapter 39.
Quando accidit in Renibus dolor ex frigore, aut ex uentositate grossa, et minuitur propter illud coitus infirmi, tunc oportet ut cauterizes ipsum super almethenem super ipsos renes, cauterio super omnem renem cum cauterio clauili, cuius praecessit rememoratio.	When kidney pain arises due to cold or thickened wind (gas), and this reduces the patient’s virility, it is necessary to cauterize over the kidneys on the area called the almethen. Apply a nail-shaped cautery to each kidney, as previously described.
Et fortasse cauterizamus ipsum secundo in ipso almeidatu.	You may also cauterize again on the lower back (almeidatu).
Quare uenient tria lineata.	Thus, three linear cauterizations will be done.
Ergo erunt magis ultima in iuuamento.	This will provide the best therapeutic outcome.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Vesicam.	On the Method of Cauterizing the Bladder
Caput XL.	Chapter 40.
Quando accidunt in Vesica debilitas, et mollificatio a frigore et humiditatibus, donec non retineat infirmus urinam, tunc cauteriza ipsum in inferiori parte suminis super Vesicam, ubi incipiunt pili pectinis, et cauterio a dextra suminis, et alio a sinistra illius: et sit longitudo illius cauterizationis lateris secundum quantitatem nodi pollicis: et cauteriza ipsum cauterio inferiori dorsi, aut duobus cauteriis, si indiges illo: et sit secundum quod praecessit cauterium clauile.	When there is weakness and relaxation in the bladder due to cold and moisture, causing urinary incontinence, cauterize the lower part of the abdomen, above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins. Apply cauterization on both the right and left sides, with a length approximately that of the thumb joint. Additionally, cauterize the lower back, using one or two cauteries if necessary, following the nail-like cautery form previously described.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Matricem.	On the Method of Cauterizing the Uterus
Caput XLI.	Chapter 41.
Quando accidunt in Matrice frigus et humiditates, et prohibetur per illud ab impregnatione, et corrumpuntur menstrua eius, et tardatur prouocatio eorum, et accidit ei apud aduentum eorum dolor, tunc oportet ut cauterizetur tribus cauteriis in circumitu umbilici, sicut diximus in cauterizatione uesicae, et cauterio super alcatim inferius dorso, aut duobus cauteriis: et sit cauterium clauile.	When cold and moisture affect the uterus, preventing conception, causing menstrual irregularities, delays, and pain upon menstruation, it is necessary to cauterize with three cauteries around the navel, as described in bladder cauterization. Apply an additional cautery over the pubic region below the back, or use two cauteries, and use the nail-shaped cautery.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Ancham in dislocatione.	On the Method of Cauterizing the Hip in Dislocation
Caput XLII.	Chapter 42.
Quando effunduntur humiditates mucosae ad pixidem Anchae, et fiunt caussa exitus eius a loco suo: et signum illius est, quod prolongatur crus super alterum, quando comparantur adinuicem: et inuenitur locus dislocationis in eo uacuus.	When mucus-like humors flow into the hip socket, causing it to dislocate, one leg will appear longer than the other when compared, and there will be an empty space at the dislocation site.
Oportet ergo ut cauterizes infirmum super pixidem Anchae ipsius cauterio simili circulo: postquam tu signas cum encaustro in circumitu pixidis, sicut reuoluitur: et ut cadat ipsa pixis in medio circuli.	It is necessary to cauterize the patient over the hip socket using a circular cautery. First, mark around the hip with ink, following its contour, so that the hip joint falls within the center of the circle.
Et sit cauterium cuius forma praecessit in cauterizatione stomachi.	Use the same cautery form as used for the stomach.
Quod si tibi non est praesens hoc cauterium, tunc cauteriza ipsum tribus cauteriis, cum cauterio oliuari magno: et fiat cauterio profunditas secundum quantitatem spissitudinis cutis totius.	If this circular cautery is not available, then apply three cauteries using a large olive-shaped cautery, with a depth equal to the skin’s full thickness.
Deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	Then treat the area until it heals completely.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Sciatica.	On the Method of Cauterizing for Sciatica
Caput XLIII.	Chapter 43
Quando accidit dolor in pixide anchae, et sunt causa illius frigus et humiditates: et curatur infirmus cum eo, quod diximus in divisione, et non confert curatio, et antiquatur illud: tunc oportet ut soluas infirmum ab humoribus grossis cum pillulis foetidis, aut cum pillulis artificialibus, et similibus.	When pain occurs in the hip joint due to cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated with the methods described earlier, but no cure is achieved, and the pain becomes chronic, it is necessary to purge the patient of thick humors using fetid pills, artificial pills, or similar remedies.
Deinde cauteriza eum.	Then proceed to cauterize the patient.
Et modus cauterii in ea est secundum duos modos: aut cauterium cum medicinis adurentibus, aut cauterium cum igne.	There are two methods for cauterization in this case: cauterization with caustic medicines or cauterization with fire.
Cauterium cum igne, est secundum multos modos.	Cauterization with fire can be done in several ways.
Quorum unus est, ut cauterizes super pixidem anchae ipsius tribus cauteriis triangulatis, secundum hanc formam.	One method is to apply three triangular cauterizations over the hip joint, arranged in this form.
Et fac eis profunditatem bonam, vel malam.	Make the cauterizations either deep or shallow, as necessary.
Et sit spacium quod est inter omne cauterium quantitatis grossitudinis digiti: sitque cauterium oliuare.	Allow a finger’s width of space between each cauterization, and use an olive-shaped cautery.
Quandoque autem fit cauterium in medio super caput anchae ipsius.	Sometimes, a single cauterization is also applied in the center over the head of the hip joint.
Quare sunt quatuor cauteria.	Thus, there will be four cauterizations in total.
Et si vis cauteriza cum circulo, cuius praecessit forma in cauterizatione dislocationis anchae, uno: ut sit circulus continens ancham totam.	If you prefer, you may use a circular cautery as described in the treatment for hip dislocation, forming a circle around the entire hip joint.
Et combure spissitudinem cutis totius.	Burn through the entire thickness of the skin.
Iste est modus cauterii in Sciatica, quando dolor est adhaerens anchae ipsi, et non extenditur usque ad coxam et crus.	This is the method for cauterizing sciatica when the pain is localized in the hip and does not extend to the thigh or leg.
Si autem extenditur usque ad coxam et crus, tunc cauteriza ipsum duobus cauteriis super coxam, super locum ad quem innuit illic infirmus, in quo est dolor, et cauterio tuo super cauillam quatuor digitis ad partem syluestrem parumper: et sit cauterium cultellare.	If the pain extends to the thigh and leg, apply two cauterizations on the thigh at the point indicated by the patient where the pain is located, and place another cautery on the ankle, about four fingers’ width toward the outside. Use a knife-shaped cautery.
Et sit profunditas cauterii secundum profunditatem spissitudinis cutis.	Ensure the cautery penetrates to the full thickness of the skin.
Quod si infirmus innuit quod dolor extenditur usque prope digitos pedis, tunc cauteriza ipsum illic ubi innuit cum cauterio puncti, tribus, aut quatuor, aut pluribus, si indiget illo.	If the patient indicates that the pain extends to the toes, apply three, four, or more point cauterizations at the points indicated by the patient, if necessary.
Et si innuit dolorem esse sub genu versus crus, tunc cauteriza ipsum illic cauterio uno cultellari.	If the patient points to pain below the knee toward the leg, apply a single knife-shaped cautery there.
Et caue tibi in omni cauterizatione tua, ut non ultimes cum cauterio ad hoc ut comburas neruum, aut arteriam magnam, et attrahas per illud super infirmum nocumentum malum, aut contractionem.	In all cauterizations, be cautious not to apply the cautery too deeply to avoid burning any nerve or major artery, which could cause severe harm or lead to contraction in the patient.
Et ego quidem iam vidi unum et alium, ex eis qui cauterizaverunt supra cauillam, et ultimaverunt in cauterizatione, et inflatum est crus, donec tumor consecutus est pedem, et perforatus est totus, et corruptus est totus pes: deinde accidit solutio ventris, et mors post illud.	I have witnessed cases where practitioners cauterized above the ankle and applied the cautery too deeply, causing the leg to swell until the swelling reached the foot, leading to the entire foot becoming perforated and necrotic; following this, the patient experienced abdominal distress and ultimately died.
Quod si dolor est in duabus partibus simul, cauteriza utramque secundum hunc modum.	If the pain is present on both sides simultaneously, cauterize each side in this manner.
Et sapientes quidam dixerunt in cauterizatione anchae, cuius cauterii iste est modus.	Certain learned practitioners have suggested the following method for hip cauterization.
Fac simile samio ex ferro, cuius diametrus sit medietas palmi: et sit apud orificium suum secundum grossitudinem nuclei dactyli, aut minus parumper: et intra illud samium sit samium tertium.	Create a cautery tool from iron resembling a double samium. Its diameter should be half a palm's width, with an opening about the width of a date stone, or slightly less. Within it, place a third samium.
Et sit spacium quod est inter omne samium per quantitatem nodi pollicis: et sint samia aperta a duabus partibus: et sit altitudo eorum quasi nodus, aut duo nodi: et fac eis manubrium ex ferro decenter aptatum in samiis.	Ensure there is a space between each samium about the size of a thumb joint. These sami should be open on both ends, with a height of about one or two thumb joints. Attach an iron handle suitably fitted to the sami.
Et haec est forma eius.	This is the design of the cautery tool.
Deinde igniatur in igne, donec rubeat, et proiiciat scintillas: deinde ponatur super pixidem anchae infirmo accubitato super latus sanum.	Then, heat it in the fire until it becomes red-hot and emits sparks. Place it on the hip joint of the patient while they lie on their healthy side.
Cauteriza ergo eum tribus cauteriis rotundis in vice una.	Thus, cauterize with three round cauterizations in a single session.
Deinde dimitte ipsum tribus diebus.	Afterward, leave the wound undisturbed for three days.
Postea emplastra cum butyro: et dimitte vulnus apertum diebus multis.	Then apply a butter-based plaster and leave the wound open for several days.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento, donec sanetur.	Finally, treat the wound with ointment until it heals completely.
Inquit Albucasis, hac specie cauterii o filii, parum usi sumus, propter terrorem aspectus eius: et propterea, quod paucos invenimus qui expectent super ipsum.	Albucasis says, "My son, we have rarely used this type of cautery because of the intimidating appearance and the lack of patients willing to undergo it."
Verumtamen est ex bonis cauteriis ei qui suffert, et invenit cum eo locum eius.	Nevertheless, it is one of the most effective cauteries for those who can endure it and whose condition warrants its application.
Cauterium autem cum medicinis adurentibus est, ut tu facias duo samia habentia perforatam armillam, in quam descendit cardo portae eius ex aere, aut ferro, longitudo parietis: quorum in altitudinem eorum sint duo nodi, aut quasi ipsi.	For cauterization with caustic medicines, make two small devices with a perforated ring through which a pivot made of brass or iron passes, the length of which is about two thumb joints.
Et sit spacium quod est inter utraque quantitas grossitudinis digiti, et sint aperta inferius et superius: et sit quod contineant se adinvicem, secundum hanc formam.	There should be a space between the devices approximately the width of a finger, and they should be open at the top and bottom, aligning in this arrangement.
Deinde depone eam super pixidem anchae, infirmo iacente super latus sanum.	Place this over the hip joint of the patient as they lie on the healthy side.
Et comprime manum tuam super pixidem anchae multum.	Press firmly over the hip joint with your hand.
Deinde funde inter duos circulos ex aqua calida, quae sit calefacta cum igne parumper, et tene eam quantitate horae temporalis: et toleret infirmus mordicationem eius, et ipsius adustionem, nam ipse invenit mordicationem sicut ignis, donec quiescat mordicatio.	Then, pour warm water heated over a flame between the two rings, maintaining the heat for about an hour. The patient will feel a biting pain like fire, which they must endure until it subsides.
Deinde eleva manum tuam cum instrumento, et absterge aquam calidam ab ancha tota cum aqua dulci: deinde dimitte illud tribus diebus.	Afterward, remove your hand and the device, wipe away the hot water with fresh water, and leave the area undisturbed for three days.
Et pone super illud butyrum, donec removeatur nigredo adustionis: et dimitte illud diebus aliquot, et curret ex eo pus.	Apply butter to the area until the burned skin turns black, and allow it to rest for several days, during which pus will begin to flow.
Est enim ultimum in iuvamento.	This process provides the most lasting relief.
Deinde cura illud cum unguentis, donec sanetur.	Then, treat it with ointments until it fully heals.
Quod si extendatur dolor usque ad coxam, aut crus: fac ei statuam in eo quod continet aquam, secundum quod fecisti in ancha aequaliter.	If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, perform the same procedure with the water application on that area as you did on the hip.
Et iste est modus aquae calidae: et ego iam scripsi eam in tractatu rectificationis medicinarum.	This is the method of using hot water, as I have detailed in my treatise on refining medical treatments.
Sume alcali, et calcis non extinctae amborum ana partem unam: tere utraque, et pone ea in ollam nouam, cuius inferior pars sit perforata foramine uno paruo, secundum quantitatem quod ingrediatur ipsum radius: et pone sub fundo ollae ollam aliam uitreatam: et proiice super alcali et calcem ex aqua dulci, quod submergat utraque per digitum: post quam tu comprimas ea manu tua compressione bona: et dimite ollam, donec descendat aqua acuta inferiori parte ollae uitreatae.	Take equal parts of alkali and quicklime, grind them thoroughly, and place them in a new pot with a small hole at the bottom, just large enough for a rod to pass through. Place a glass vessel underneath, then pour fresh water over the alkali and lime to cover them by about a finger's width. Press down firmly with your hand and allow the liquid to drain into the glass vessel below.
Deinde aggrega illam aquam totam, et proiice eam super aliam calcem: et cola, donec renovetur.	Collect all this liquid, pour it over a new portion of lime, and filter it to renew its potency.
Ipsa enim erit tunc fortis acuitatis valde, quae administratur in multis operationibus medicinae, et in cauterizatione reliquorum membrorum.	This solution will be highly caustic and suitable for many medical applications, including cauterizing other parts of the body.
Quoniam efficit operationem ignis ipsius.	It effectively replicates the action of fire.
Et ex medicinis sunt, cum quibus cauterizantur ancha, etiam sicut tesisie, et mel anacardi, et calx cum sapone, ita quod utraque sint permixta.	Other medicinal substances used for cauterizing the hip include tesesi, cashew honey, and lime mixed with soap, all combined for maximum efficacy.
Et Galenus quidem narrando retulit, cuiusdam viri ex antiquis curationem, qua curatus est dolor anchae et venae sciaticae: et magnificavit esse eius valde.	Galen, recounting the treatment of an ancient man cured of hip pain and sciatica, highly praised this method.
Et dixit, quia non indiguit alia curatione, et quia sanatus est ex vice una, donec retulit, quia ipse fortasse intravit balneum delatus, et exivit ex eo iam sanus.	He said that the man needed no further treatment and was cured after a single session, even claiming that the patient entered the bath in pain and emerged fully healed.
Et est, ut accipiatur ex seitaragi viridi: et si non invenitur viride, sumatur siccum, recens: et teratur multum cum aliquanto adipe, et ponatur super ancham, ubi est dolor, aut crus, aut in coxa: et ligetur, et dimittatur quantitate trium horarum, aut per quantitatem quod sentiat infirmus sedationem adustionis.	The treatment involves using fresh seitaragi (a specific medicinal plant), or, if unavailable, a dried, recent sample. Grind it thoroughly with some fat, apply it to the hip, leg, or thigh where the pain is located, then bind and leave it in place for about three hours or until the patient feels relief from the burning.
Deinde intromitte eum in balneum.	Then, have the patient enter a bath.
Cum ergo roridum fit corpus eius, intromitte ipsum in solium.	Once their body is perspiring, immerse them in a basin.
Nam dolor recedit, et sanatur.	The pain will subside, and healing will occur.
Et scias, quia non oportet ut utatur aliquis cauterio cum istis medicinis, nisi post evacuationem corporis.	Be aware that cauterization should not be combined with these treatments until the body has been purged.
Et Dioscorides quidem dixit, quod stercus caprarum, quando cum eo cauterizatur vena sciatica, confert ei: et fit cauterium secundum hunc modum.	Dioscorides stated that goat dung, when used to cauterize the sciatic vein, provides relief. The cautery is applied as follows:
Sumatur lana, et imbibatur oleo antiquo, et ponatur super locum profundum, qui est inter pollicem pedis, et inter focile, et est propinquior focili.	Take some wool, soak it in old oil, and place it over the depression between the big toe and the arch, near the ankle.
Deinde accipe stercus caprarum siccum, et inflamma ipsum in igne, donec fiat carbo.	Then take dried goat dung, ignite it in fire until it turns to charcoal.
Deinde pone ipsum super lanam, et dimitte ipsum, donec extinguatur.	Place this charcoal on the wool and let it burn out.
Deinde itera illud.	Repeat this process.
Non cesses ergo facere illud, usquequo perveniat sensus super mediatione usque ad ancham, et quiescat dolor.	Continue this until the sensation extends along the pathway to the hip and the pain subsides.
Et iste modus cauterii nominatur cauterium Vaccinum.	This method is known as the "Cow Cautery."
¶ De cauterizatione doloris Dorsi.	On cauterization for back pain.
Caput XLIIII.	Chapter 44.
Quandoque accidit dolor in Dorso ex caussis multis, aut a casu, aut a percussione, aut euacuatione superflua, et illis similibus, ex infusione materiei frigidae, et humidae: et cauterium quidem non cadit, nisi in hac specie sola, quae fit ex infusione materiei frigidae.	Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from an accident, or from an impact, or excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and moist matter: and in fact, cauterization is only used in this specific case, which results from the infusion of cold matter.
Oportet ergo post euacuationem infirmi cum pillulis foetidis, et eis similibus, ut fiant super Dorsum, ubi est dolor, tres lineae secundum latitudinem almeidati ipsius, postquam signas cum encaustro in omni linea quinque cauteria, aut plura secundum quantitatem quae uenit ex tolerantia infirmi uirtute eius: et fiat cauterizatio cum cauteriopuncti.	Therefore, after evacuating the patient with stinking pills, and similar treatments, three lines should be made on the back, where the pain is, according to the width of the affected area itself, marking five cauterizations on each line with ink, or more according to the patient’s ability to endure it: and the cauterization is to be performed with a pointed cautery.
Et si uis, cauteriza tribus cauteriis, aut quatuor, cum cauterio clauili mediali, secundum hanc formam.	And if you wish, cauterize with three cauteries, or four, with the middle key-shaped cautery, in this manner.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in incaeptine Gibbositatis.	On the method of cauterizing in the initial stage of hunchback.
Caput XLV.	Chapter 45.
Multotiens accidit haec aegritudo infantibus paruis.	This disease often occurs in young children.
Et signum incaeptionis eius in pueris est: quod accidit super eum strictura in anhelitu apud eleuationem, et motum: et inuenis in ultima spondilium Dorsi et nodorum eius, quod iam incaepit eminere super reliquos spondiles.	And the sign of its onset in children is that they suffer tightness in breathing upon lifting and movement: and you find at the end of the spine and its joints, that one part has already started to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Cum ergo uides illud, et uis facere illud, tunc cauteriza ipsum cum cauterio quod sit circulus secundum hanc formam.	When you see that, and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cautery shaped like a circle, in this manner.
Et capiat cauterium super omnem partem spondilis aequaliter: et si uis cauteriza in circumitu spondilis cum cauterio puncti duas lineas, aut tres: et sint puncta propinqua adinuicem.	And let the cautery take hold evenly on every part of the vertebra: and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebra with a pointed cautery in two lines, or three, with the points close together.
Deinde cura locum, donec sanetur cum eo quod diximus.	Then treat the area until it heals with what we have prescribed.
Et caue, ne administres cauterium in gibbositate, quae fit in spasmo nerui.	And be careful not to apply cautery to a hump caused by nerve spasm.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Podagra, et doloribus iuncturarum.	On the method of cauterizing for gout and joint pains.
Caput XLVI.	Chapter 46.
Quando dolores iuncturarum sunt ab humiditatibus frigidis, quae effunduntur ad cuiuslibet membra corporis, tunc quando accidunt dolores in pedibus, de consuetudine medicorum est, ut nominent illud Podagram proprie.	When joint pains result from cold humors that spread to various body parts, then when pain occurs in the feet, it is customary among doctors to specifically call it gout.
Cum ergo curatur Podagra frigidae caussae cum modis curationis, et non remouentur dolores, tune cauterium remouet eos.	Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with various methods, and the pains are not relieved, then cauterization removes them.
Et est, ut cauterizes eum post euacuationem in circumitu iuncturae pedum, cauteriis multis: et sit cauterium Oliuare.	And this is done by cauterizing around the joints of the feet after evacuation, with multiple cauterizations: and the cautery should be olive-shaped.
Cuius haec est forma.	This is its form.
Et si indiges ut punctes super faciem pedis, tunc fac cum cauterio puncti.	And if you need to prick the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery.
Quod si ascendunt dolores usque ad genua, aut reliquas iuncturas, et multotiens accidit illud, tunc cauteriza ipsum super omne genu tribus cauteriis, aut quatuor ab omni parte, cum hoc eodem cauterio Clauili.	If the pains extend up to the knees or other joints, as often happens, then cauterize each knee with three or four cauteries on all sides, with this same key-shaped cautery.
Si autem necessaria sunt tibi plura hoc cauterio, tunc cauteriza ipsum.	And if more cauterizations with this cautery are necessary, then cauterize it.
Et non submergas manum tuam cum cauterio, imo sit circiter spissitudinem cutis tantum.	Do not sink your hand deeply with the cautery; rather, only to the thickness of the skin.
Si autem ascendunt dolores ad genua, et dorsum: tunc administra quod diximus ex cauterio in capitulo suo.	But if the pains rise to the knees and back, then apply what we mentioned in its section on cautery.
Quod si dolores sunt in manibus tantum, tunc puncta in circumitu focilium, sicut reuoluuntur duae lineae.	If the pains are in the hands only, then prick around the joints, as two lines are traced.
Si autem remanet ex doloribus in digitis, tunc puncta eos, super omnem nodum punctum, et super pectinem manus.	If any pain remains in the fingers, then prick each joint and along the ridge of the hand.
Si autem ascendunt dolores post dies ad cubitos, aut ad humeros, tunc cauteriza utrosque ab omni parte.	If the pains rise over time to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from all sides.
Et non euacues infirmum ex regimine bono, ex recaeptione medicinarum.	And do not evacuate the patient if they follow a good regimen and receive medicines.
Nam si bonum fiat regimen, et euacuetur phlegma, sanabitur auxilio Dei cum isto cauterio.	For if a good regimen is followed, and phlegm is evacuated, they will be healed by God’s help with this cautery.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Rupturis.	On the method of cauterizing for hernias.
Caput XLVII.	Chapter 47.
Quando accidit Ruptura in inguinibus, et descendit intestinum, aut zirbum ad testiculum, et est illud incipiens propinquum: tunc oportet ut praecipias infirmo dimittere comestionem in die suo.	When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine or fatty tissue descends to the testicle, and it is in the early stage, then you must instruct the patient to refrain from eating for a day.
Et utatur ex lenientibus, quo descendat stercus a uentre suo.	And he should use laxatives, so that stool may pass from his abdomen.
Deinde sedeat inter manus tuas super dorsum suum: et praecipe ei, ut teneat anhelitum suum, donec egrediatur, uel appareat zirbum, aut intestinum.	Then let him sit on his back in your hands, and instruct him to hold his breath until the fatty tissue or intestine emerges or becomes visible.
Deinde reduc ipsum digitis tuis, et signa cum encaustro sub Ruptura super os pectinis, cum signo cuius extremitas sit similis medietati circuli ad superiora corporis.	Then, reduce it with your fingers, and mark under the rupture over the pubic bone with ink, using a symbol whose end resembles half a circle facing the upper body.
Deinde igni cauterium, cuius haec est forma, donec ueniat album, et proiiciat seintillas.	Then heat the cautery in the fire, in this shape, until it turns white and sparks.
Deinde reduc intestinum, aut zirbum ad concauitatem suam.	Then return the intestine or fatty tissue to its cavity.
Deinde ponat minister manum suam super locum, ut non exeat intestinum: et tu iam aperuisti inter crura infirmi, et posuisti sub eo puluinar, et seruiens alius super crura eius, et alius super pectus eius qui tenet manus.	Then let the assistant place his hand over the area so the intestine does not exit: and now you spread the patient's legs, place a cushion under him, with one assistant holding his legs and another on his chest holding his hands.
Deinde depone cauterium super ipsum signum, manu tua cum cauterio stante recta.	Then place the cautery over the marked spot, holding your hand with the cautery upright.
Et tene ipsum, donec cum eo consequaris os: aut itera cum eo uice alia, si non consecutus fueris cum eo in prima usque ad os.	And hold it there until you reach the bone with it; or repeat another time, if you have not reached the bone on the first attempt.
Et prudenter obserua ab exitu intestini in hora cauterizationis tuae, ne comburas ipsum, et eueniat per illud super infirmum aut mors, aut malicia magna.	And carefully watch for the exit of the intestine at the time of your cauterization, lest you burn it, and cause either death or severe harm to the patient.
Et scias, quod quando tu non consequeris cum cauterio os, non confert operatio tua.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your procedure will not be effective.
Et oportet ut sit cauterium infantium subtile, secundum mensuram eorum.	And the cautery for children must be fine, according to their size.
Deinde cura cum reliquis unguentis, donec sanetur.	Then treat it with other ointments, until it heals.
Et sit infirmus iacens super dorsum suum quadraginta diebus, donec sigilletur uulnus.	And the patient should lie on his back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
Et oportet, ut ponas nutrimentum eius longitudine temporis curationis eius, quod leniat uentrem eius: ut non exeat intestinum apud conamen et egestionem.	And his nourishment should be regulated during his recovery period to keep his bowels soft, so the intestine does not exit during strain or evacuation.
Deinde quando uult surgere post quadraginta dies, tunc administra ligamentum decenter factum, et teneat ipsum quadraginta diebus aliis.	Then, when he wishes to get up after forty days, apply a properly made bandage, and he should wear it for another forty days.
Et minoretur a labore, et repletione cibi et potus, et uocibus uehementibus.	And he should avoid labor, overeating and drinking, and loud voices.
Nam quando utitur hoc regimine, ita sanatur sanatione integra.	For when he follows this regimen, he will be healed completely.
Et ego dicam curationem Rupturarum cum incisione in capitulo suo.	And I will describe the treatment of ruptures with incision in its own chapter.
Quando autem Rupturae accidunt in reliquo uentre, et sunt incipientes, et uis ut non addantur, tunc cauteriza Rupturam eius cauterio rotundo secundum quantitatem eius: et sit illud quod aduritur ex tunc sicut tertia eius.	But when ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen, and are in the early stages, and you wish to prevent their growth, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let the area burned be about a third of it.
Deinde cura ipsum, cum eo quod diximus: et non addetur.	Then treat it with what we have mentioned, and it will not grow further.
Et iam dixerunt quidam primi: ut cauterizetur Ruptura cum cauterio triangulato, secundum hanc formam.	And some of the ancients have said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, in this shape.
Postquam signatur cum encaustro, et ponitur linea quae est per latitudinem in latere superiori Rupturae, et linea altera ad inferius.	After marking it with ink, a line is drawn transversely on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below.
Et depone manum tuam in medio cum cauterio clauili.	And place your hand in the middle with a key-shaped cautery.
Sed cauterium primum est facilius et melius.	But the first cautery is easier and better.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in doloribus propter casum, aut percussionem.	On the method of cauterizing for pains caused by a fall or blow.
Caput XLVIII.	Chapter 48.
Quando accidit in quibusdam membris a casu, aut percussione dolor: et perseuerat ille dolor tempore longo, et non confert in eo curatio cum medicinis: tunc oportet ut cauterizetur cum cauterio Puncti.	When pain occurs in certain limbs from a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines is ineffective: then it should be cauterized with a pointed cautery.
Et sit cauterium omnis membri cauterium secundum magnitudinem eius, et ipsius paruitatem, et debilitatem eius, et ipsius uirtutem, et locationem torsionis, et doloris ex eo.	And the cautery for each limb should be sized according to its size, and its delicacy, weakness, strength, and the location of the twist and pain from it.
Si ergo sanatur ex cauterio primo, est bene.	If it heals from the first cauterization, it is well.
Si non: tunc itera super ipsum cauterium.	If not, then repeat the cauterization.
Quoniam de consuetudine horum dolorum est, ut permutentur ex membro ad illud quod appropinquat ei.	Because it is customary with these pains that they shift from one limb to another nearby.
Quare oportet ut consequaris eos cum cauterio, donec sanetur infirmus.	Therefore you should pursue them with cauterization until the patient is healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Lepra.	On the method of cauterizing for leprosy.
Caput XLIX.	Chapter 49.
Leprosi autem quandoque iuvantur cauterio iuvamento maximo.	Leprosy patients are sometimes greatly aided by cauterization.
Et praecipue species Leprae, quae fit propter putrefactionem phlegmatis et melancholiae: cum ergo vis cauterizare ipsam considera.	Especially the type of leprosy that arises due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy; when you decide to cauterize, consider this.
Si ergo Lepra est incipiens, et curasti eam cum eo, quod diximus in divisione, et non descendit, neque stat: et times super infirmum, quod comprehendat corruptio super totam complexionem eius: tunc cauteriza eum super caput quinque cauteriis: uno in medio capitis noto, et secundo inferius eo versus frontem apud finem capillorum, et duobus super duo cornua, et uno posterius super nucea cervicis.	If the leprosy is in the early stages, and you have treated it as we described in the section, but it does not spread or subside, and you fear it might affect the entire body, then cauterize him with five cauteries on the head: one in the center of the head at a marked point, a second lower towards the forehead at the hairline, two on either side of the temples, and one at the nape of the neck.
Et ultima manum tuam cum cauterio parumper, donec imprimat in os impressionem parvam, et dislocentur ex eo cortices: ut allevietur expiratio vaporibus grossorum ex eo, et cauteriza cauterio etiam super ipsum splenem, secundum quod praecessit.	Hold your hand with the cautery for a brief moment, until it leaves a small mark on the bone and the scabs peel off, to ease the release of thick vapors from there; also cauterize over the spleen, as previously mentioned.
Sin autem Lepra iam sparsa est super infirmum, et apparet manifeste: tunc oportet ut cauterizes cum istis cauteriis, quae diximus in capite, et cauterio super extremitatem nasi, et duobus cauteriis super duas maxillas, et duobus cauteriis super spondiles colli, et sex super spondiles dorsi, et uno magno super alhahosos apud gran caudae et uno supra ipsum, in ipso almeidati: et duobus super anchas: scilicet super omnem ancham uno, et duobus super genua: uno super omne genu, et duobus super humeros, et duobus super cubitos, et duobus super teneritudines pectoris sui: et cauteriza ipsum super omnem iuncturam, ex iuncturis digitorum manuum suarum, et pedum suorum: et cauteriza super omnem calcaneum pedum suorum, et focilia manuum suarum.	However, if leprosy has spread over the patient and is clearly visible, then apply the cauteries as we described on the head, one on the tip of the nose, two on each cheek, two on the vertebrae of the neck, six on the vertebrae of the back, a large one on the sacrum at the base of the spine, one just above it, two on the hips (one on each hip), two on the knees (one on each knee), two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the softer parts of the chest; cauterize every joint, including the joints of the fingers of both hands and feet; also cauterize on every heel and the backs of the hands.
Et cave tibi a nervis qui sunt super postremum calcanei, ut non comburas eos.	Be cautious of the nerves located at the back of the heel, so as not to burn them.
Et quandoque cauterizatur cauterio super os pectinis, et alio super os stomachi, et alio super epar.	Sometimes, cauterize over the pubic bone, another over the stomach, and another over the liver.
Et scias, quod quanto plus addis cauterium, est magis iuvamentum, et magis conferens.	Know that the more cautery you apply, the more it will aid and contribute to healing.
Et scias, quod infirmus non invenit in cauterio dolorem, sicut inveniunt ipsum sani: propterea, quod corpus eius iam stupefactum est.	And know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because his body is already numbed.
Et oportet ut sint cauteria ex magnitudine, et parvitate secundum membra et iuncturas: secundum quod praecessit ex speciebus ferramentorum.	The cauteries should be sized according to the limbs and joints, as was previously mentioned regarding the types of instruments.
Deinde cura cauterium ex farina herbi cum melle, et reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	Then treat the cauterized area with an herbal flour mixed with honey and follow the remaining treatment until it heals.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Stupore.	On the method of cauterizing for numbness.
Caput L.	Chapter 50.
Quando stupet aliquod membrum, et curatur cum medicinis, et oleis, et emplastris, et non sanatur, tunc cauteriza ipsum membrum stupefactum cauteriis, secundum quod meretur magnitudo membri, aut parvitas eius.	When a limb is numb and has been treated with medicines, oils, and poultices without healing, then cauterize the numb limb with cauteries according to its size, whether large or small.
Et sit cauterium tuum intrans in spissitudinem cutis parumper.	Let your cautery penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento, donec sanetur.	Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et quandoque cauterizatur ad quiddam stuporis, qui accidit manui, et pedi, in spondilibus dorsi apud exitum nervorum, qui movent illud membrum: et removetur stupor.	Sometimes numbness in the hand or foot is treated by cauterizing at the vertebrae of the back, near the exit points of the nerves that control that limb, and the numbness is relieved.
Verum non praesumat super illud, nisi qui est sapiens in anatomia membrorum, et egressione nervorum moventium corpus.	However, only those who are knowledgeable in the anatomy of the body and the pathways of nerves controlling movement should attempt this.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Albaras.	On the method of cauterizing for vitiligo (white patches).
Caput LI.	Chapter 51.
Quando antiquatur Albaras, et non confert in eo aliquid ex ingeniis medicinae: tunc cauteriza super ipsam cauterio profundo parumper, secundum quantitatem spissitudinis cutis, donec removeatur albedo, et mutetur color eius.	When vitiligo has persisted and no medical treatments have been effective, then cauterize the area with a slightly deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and the color changes.
Deinde cura ipsum cum farina herbi, et lentis cum oleo rosa, et foliis arnoglossae, et sanguine columbae, et sanguine hirundinis: de unoquoque sit pars una: misceantur haec omnia, et liniantur super pannum, et adhaereant loco, donec sanetur.	Then treat it with an ointment made from herbal flour, lentils with rose oil, plantain leaves, dove's blood, and swallow's blood; take an equal part of each, mix them together, spread them on a cloth, and apply it to the area until it heals.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Cancro.	On the method of cauterizing for cancer.
Caput LII.	Chapter 52.
Quando Cancer est incipiens, et vis ipsum sistere: tunc cauteriza ipsum cum cauterio circuli in circuitu eius, sicuti revolvitur.	When cancer is beginning, and you want to halt it, then cauterize around it with a circular cautery, following its circumference.
Sapientes autem dixerunt, ut cauterizetur cauterio ultimo in medio.	The wise have said that it should be cauterized with a final cautery in the center.
Mihi autem non videtur illud: quoniam timeo quod ulceretur: et ego iam vidi illud aliquotiens.	However, this does not seem advisable to me, as I fear it may ulcerate, and I have seen this happen several times.
Et rectius est, ut cauterizetur in circumitu eius cum circulo, sicut diximus: aut cauteriis multis.	It is better to cauterize around it with a circular cautery as we mentioned, or with multiple cauteries.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Adubelati.	On the method of cauterizing an abscess or boil.
Caput LIII.	Chapter 53.
Quando aliquis habet Adubelati, et tardatur in maturatione, aut propter superfluitatem facientem eam, aut propter aetatem infirmi, quando est decrepitus pauci sanguinis, aut propter tempus, et vis festinare in maturatione Adubelati, tunc cauteriza in circumitu eius cum cauteriis parvis multis punctando.	When someone has an abscess (Adubelati) that is slow to mature, either due to excess humor causing it, the patient's advanced age and low blood volume, or the season, and you wish to hasten its maturation, then apply multiple small cauterizations around its circumference by making tiny pricks.
Deinde dimitte eam.	Then leave it as it is.
Nam ipsa festinabit cum maturatione.	This will cause it to mature more quickly.
Si autem vis perforationem eius cum cauterio, tunc igni cauterium, cuius haec est forma.	If you wish to lance it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, shaped as described.
Et depone ipsum in medio Adubelati, donec penetret cutem: et sit cauterium ab eo quod sequitur infirmus, ut allevietur cursus puris.	Apply it in the center of the abscess until it pierces the skin, and it should be done in a way that allows the pus to drain, relieving the patient.
Deinde cura ipsum donec sanetur.	Then treat the area until it heals.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in malo corrodente.	On the method of cauterizing a corroding sore or ulcer.
Caput LIIII.	Chapter 54.
Corrodens non est nisi corruptio in membro ambulans, et corrodit ipsum: sicut ignis comedit ligna sicca.	A corroding sore is essentially decay spreading through the flesh, eating it away like fire devours dry wood.
Si ergo vides corrodentem in loco qui toleret cauterium cum igne, tunc igni cauteria multa, clavilia parva et magna, secundum quod conveniet illi loco in quo est corrodens.	If you see a corroding sore in an area that can tolerate fire cautery, then apply several cauteries, both small and large, depending on the area affected by the sore.
Deinde cauteriza ipsum ab omni parte donec eradices corruptionem totam, et non remaneat ex ea aliquid penitus.	Then cauterize it thoroughly from all sides until all the decayed tissue is eradicated, leaving no trace of it whatsoever.
Deinde dimitte ipsum tribus diebus, et pone super loca cauterizata sulphur tritum cum oleo, donec eradicentur escharae omnes, et omnis corruptio.	Leave the area for three days, and apply powdered sulfur mixed with oil over the cauterized spots, until all the scabs and decay are removed.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguentis generantibus carnem.	Afterward, treat the area with ointments that promote new flesh growth.
Si ergo vides, quod post tres dies caro nascitur nativitate sana, in qua non est corruptio, est bonum.	If, after three days, you see healthy new flesh growing without any decay, it is a good sign.
Et si non: tunc itera cauterium super illud quod remansit ex locis corruptis.	If not, then repeat the cauterization on any remaining decayed areas.
Et corrodens medicatur quandoque cum medicina acuta.	Sometimes, corroding sores are treated with strong medicines instead of cauterization.
Ipsa namque surgit loco cauterii.	Such a treatment acts in place of cautery.
Verumtamen cauterium cum igne est velocioris iuvamenti: et ego quidem iam dixi cauterizationem eius cum medicina acuta in divisione: accipe ergo eam illic quando ea indiges.	However, fire cautery provides faster relief; I have already described the use of strong medicines in another section. Refer to it when you need that information.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Clavis, et Verucis.	On the method of cauterizing corns and warts.
Caput LV.	Chapter 55.
Multotiens accidit in inferioribus partibus pedum haec aegritudo: et est res grossa, filtrata, quae laedit pedem.	This condition often affects the lower parts of the feet and consists of thick, hardened growths that harm the foot.
Et cauterium quidem in eis est secundum duos modos: cauterium cum igne, et cauterium cum aqua calida.	There are two methods for treating them: cauterization with fire or with hot water.
Quantum autem cum igne est, ut ignias cauterium concavum simile pennae vulturis: quod fiat ex ferro, secundum quantitatem quod contineat clavum ab omni parte: et sit subtilium marginum.	For fire cauterization, use a hollow cautery resembling a vulture's feather, made of iron, and sized to fit around the corn on all sides, with fine edges.
Deinde depone ipsum ignitum super clavum.	Then place the heated cautery over the corn.
Deinde revolve manum cum cauterio in circumitu clavi, donec perveniat cauterium ad profunditatem clavi: et dimitte ipsum tribus diebus, donec incipiat emittere pus.	Rotate the cautery around the corn, allowing it to penetrate deeply; leave it for three days until it begins to discharge pus.
Deinde emplastra ipsum cum malvis sylvestribus, contritis cum sale: et dimitte emplastrum super ipsum in nocte.	Then apply a poultice of wild mallow crushed with salt and leave it on overnight.
Ipse enim eradicabitur ex radicibus suis.	This will cause it to be uprooted from its roots.
Deinde cura locum unguento generativo carnis, donec sanetur.	Afterward, treat the area with an ointment that encourages flesh growth until it heals.
Quod si sunt non conuersi, et multotiens accidunt in superficie corporis, praecipue in manibus et pedibus: tunc administres in eis cauterium cum aqua calida: et est, ut accipias cannulam ex aere, aut ferro, aut ex penna uulturis: et depone eam super clauum, aut althelul.	If the corns or warts are not recessed and occur on the body’s surface, particularly on the hands and feet, then apply cauterization with hot water. Use a metal tube made of bronze, iron, or a vulture’s feather, and place it over the corn or wart.
Deinde proiice in cannulam ex aqua calida quantitatem paucam: retine manum tuam, et tu revolve eam cum compressione manus tuae parumper, ut imprimatur margo cannulae in radice clavi, et inveniatur aqua calida viam ad profundum, ad radicem clavi. Et expectet infirmus parumper super mordicationem aquae calidae hora una.	Pour a small amount of hot water into the tube, press it down and turn it slightly so that the tube’s edge presses into the root of the corn, allowing the hot water to reach the corn’s depth. Let the patient bear the hot water’s sensation for about an hour.
Deinde dimitte ipsum, nam clavis eradicatur cum radicibus suis.	Afterward, release it, as the corn will be uprooted from its roots.
Ita fac cum eis uno post unum, donec venias super omnes qui ex eis sunt in corpore.	Proceed in this way, one by one, until you treat all the corns on the body.
Deinde cura eos postquam eradicantur, cum eo quod generat carnem ex unguentis.	Then, once removed, treat the areas with an ointment that promotes flesh growth.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Tremore.	On the method of cauterizing for tremor.
Caput LVI.	Chapter 56.
Quando accidit alicui Tremor ex frigore in nervo, aut ex febre quartana, aut alio: tunc oportet ut cauterizes ipsum quatuor cauteriis, aut quinque super spondiles dorsi, et inter omnem spondilem cauterio, et in pectore eius cauterio, et super stomachum eius cauterio.	When someone experiences tremor due to cold affecting the nerves, quartan fever, or another cause, then apply four or five cauteries along the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra, one on the chest, and one on the stomach.
Tremor enim quiescit cum cauterio olivari, et festinat sanitas aegritudinis frigidae.	Tremor is calmed by olive oil cauterization, and recovery from the cold illness is hastened.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Albathir.	On the method of cauterizing pustules or boils known as Albathir.
Caput LVII.	Chapter 57.
Quandoque expelluntur in corpore Albathir foedae, id est, pustulae, quae fiunt a materiis grossis corruptis.	Sometimes foul pustules, known as Albathir, appear on the body, caused by corrupted, thick humors.
Oportet ergo in primis cum apparent, ut cauterizentur super omne caput pustulae cauterio subtili cum ligno myrti, cuius extremitas accensa est cum igne.	It is necessary, when they first appear, to cauterize the top of each pustule with a fine cautery, such as a myrtle twig with a fire-heated tip.
Aut cum radice aristolochiae longae.	Alternatively, use the root of long Aristolochia (birthwort).
Aut cum cauterio lenticulari.	Or, you may use a lenticular-shaped cautery.
Et quandoque cauterizantur ademenul, in principio expulsionis suae secundum hunc modum: et non augentur: et disrumpitur superfluitas faciens eos, et sanatur ex eis.	Sometimes, early cauterization of these pustules, following this method, prevents them from enlarging, breaks up the excess humor causing them, and brings about healing.
Verumtamen oportet ut fiat illud post evacuationem cum phlebotomia.	However, this procedure should be carried out after purging through bloodletting.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in fluxu sanguinis ex arteria in vulnere.	On the method of cauterizing arterial bleeding from a wound.
Caput LVIII.	Chapter 58.
Multotiens accidit fluxus sanguinis ex arteria, quae incisa est apud vulnus, quod accidit extrinsecus, aut apud incisionem apostematis, aut cauterium membri, et similia eis: et fit difficile abscindere eum.	Arterial bleeding often occurs from an artery cut by an external wound, the incision of an abscess, a limb cauterization, or similar injuries; stopping it can be very difficult.
Cum ergo accidit alicui illud, tunc propera cum manu tua ad orificium arteriae, et pone super ipsum digitum tuum indicem: et stringe eum multum, donec obsessus sit sanguis sub digito tuo, et non egrediatur ex eo aliquid.	When this happens, quickly place your index finger over the artery’s opening, press down firmly, and hold to stop blood from escaping.
Deinde pone in ignem cauteria olivaria parva, et magna numero plura: et suffla super ea, donec fiant ignita valde.	Then place several olive-sized cauteries, both small and large, in the fire and fan them until they are extremely hot.
Deinde accipe ex eis unum, aut parvum, aut magnum, secundum vulnus et locum, in quo disrupta est arteria, et depone cauterium super ipsam venam, post quam tu removes digitum tuum festinanter: et tene cauterium, donec abscindatur sanguis.	Choose a cautery that suits the size and location of the wound, place it over the artery after quickly lifting your finger, and hold it in place until the bleeding stops.
Quod si expellatur cum elevas digitum ab orificio arteriae, et extinguis cauterium, tunc accipe cauterium aliud festinanter, ex cauteriis quae in igne sunt praeparata.	If bleeding resumes when you lift your finger or extinguish the cautery, immediately use another cautery from those prepared in the fire.
Non ergo cesses facere illud cum uno post aliud, donec abscindatur sanguis.	Continue using cauteries one after another until the bleeding is stopped.
Et cave, ne comburas nervum qui est illic, et accidat super infirmum malicia alia.	Take care not to burn any nearby nerve, as this could cause additional harm to the patient.
Et scias, quod quando ex arteria fluit sanguis, tunc non est possibile abscindere ipsum: praecipue quando arteria est magna, nisi cum uno quatuor modorum.	Know that arterial bleeding, especially from a large artery, cannot be controlled except by one of four methods:
Aut cum cauterio, sicut diximus.	With cautery, as described.
Aut cum extractione, quando non est extracta.	By extraction, if it has not yet been removed.
Nam quando extrahitur, contrahuntur extremitates eius, et abscinditur sanguis.	When it is extracted, the ends contract, stopping the bleeding.
Aut ligetur cum filo ligatione forti.	Or by tightly tying it with a thread.
Aut ponantur super ipsum medicinae de proprietate, quarum est abscindere sanguinem, et stringatur cum pulvinar constrictione decenti.	Or apply medicines with properties to halt bleeding, combined with firm compression using a suitable cushion.
Qui autem administrat abscisionem eius cum ligamento, et strictura cum panno, aut positione rerum comburentium, et similium, non confert ei penitus, nisi raro.	Using ligatures, cloth pressure, or applying burning substances seldom offers lasting relief and may not be effective.
Si autem accidat alicui illud, et non sit ei praesens medicus, neque medicina: tunc incipiat cum positione digiti indicis super orificium venae ipsius, sicut narrauimus, et constrictione eius valde, donec obsessus sit sanguis a superiori parte vulneris, et super arteriam.	If a person is alone without a physician or medical supplies, they should place their index finger over the artery’s opening, pressing firmly to prevent blood flow from the wound above and the artery itself, as previously described.
Et digitus non removeatur, desuper ipsum cum aqua frigida vehementis frigoris semper, donec congeletur sanguis, et ingrossetur, et abscindatur.	Do not remove the finger, but continuously pour very cold water over the area to thicken and freeze the blood, stopping the bleeding.
Et interim consideret in eo, quid indiget ex cauterio, aut ex medicina.	During this process, assess whether further treatment with cautery or medicine is needed.
¶ Partis Primae Finis.	End of the First Part.
Liber Chirurgici Albucasis Pars II.	The Surgical Book of Albucasis, Part II.
¶ De Incisione, Perforatione, et Phlebotomia in uulneribus, et his similibus.	On Incision, Perforation, and Bloodletting in wounds, and such matters.
Iam Diximus in Capitulo Primo, omnem aegritudinem in qua conueniens est cum igne cauterium et medicina comburente, et occasiones eius, ipsius caussas, et instrumenta eius, et formas cauteriorum.	We have already discussed in the First Chapter, every condition in which cautery with fire and burning medicine is suitable, and its reasons, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries.
Et posui illic capitula a uertice usque ad pedem.	And I arranged there the chapters from head to foot.
Et ego procedam in hoc capitulo illa eadem uia: ut alleuietur super quaerentem quaesitum eius.	And I will proceed in this chapter by the same method: so that the inquiry may be made easier for the seeker.
Et antequam incipiam illud, oportet ut addiscatis o filii, quod in hoc capitulo est ex terrore illud quod est in capitulo primo de cauterizatione.	And before I begin it, it is necessary for you to learn, my sons, that in this chapter there is as much terror as there is in the first chapter on cauterization.
Et propter illud oportet, ut sit cautela in eo uehementior, quoniam in operatione quae est in hoc capitulo, multotiens cadit euacuatio cum sanguine, cum quo stat uita apud apertionem uenae, aut incisionem super apostema, aut apertionem exiturae, aut curationem uulneris, aut extractionem sagittae, aut incisionem super lapidem, et illis similia: ex quibus omnibus associatur tremor, et timor, et cadit in pluribus eorum mors.	And because of this, caution must be greater in it, since in the operation described in this chapter, there often occurs an evacuation with blood, upon which life depends in the opening of a vein, or the incision over a swelling, or the opening of an abscess, or the treatment of a wound, or the extraction of an arrow, or the incision over a stone, and similar actions: from all of which are associated tremor, fear, and in many cases, death.
Et ego moneo uos, ne cadat super uos illud in quo est haesitatio, nam quandoque cadunt ad uos in hac arte modi hominum cum modis infirmitatum.	And I advise you, lest that which involves hesitation fall upon you, for sometimes types of people come to you in this art with various kinds of sicknesses.
Ex eis enim est qui irascitur cum aegritudine sua, et est leuis apud eum mors: propter uehementiam eius quod inuenit ex infirmitate sua et longitudine eius maliciei.	For among them is one who becomes angry with his illness, and death seems of little concern to him, due to the severity of what he experiences from his sickness and its prolonged malice.
Et cum aegritudine est ex timore quod significat mortem.	And with sickness, there is a fear which signifies death.
