However, in cleansing with a claw, the instrument may slip and spoil your procedure: and indeed, the skin of a boy is naturally short, and many are born such that they do not need cleansing, as I have already observed.
Mundificationis autem cum forficibus, et ligamento cum filo, bonum experimentum detexit mihi: quoniam forfices sunt proportionalis incisionis: propterea, quod acuitas quae est superius, est sicut acuitas quae est inferius.	But the cleansing with scissors and thread binding has shown me good results: for the scissors are proportionate in their incision; therefore, the sharpness that is above is like the sharpness that is below.
Cum ergo premis manum tuam, proportionantur duae acuitates, et incidunt secundum operationem unam in tempore uno: et fit compressio simili figura, continens cutem uirgae ab omni parte, cum qua non cadit error omnino.	Thus, when you press your hand, the two sharp edges are aligned and cut as a single action in one moment; and a similar shape of compression occurs, holding the skin of the penis from all sides, with which no error occurs at all.
Et modus operationis propriae est, ut facias extimare, puerum praecipue, si est ex eis qui intelligunt parumper, quod tu non facis, nisi quod ligas filum in uirga sua tantum: et dimittas ipsum usque ad diem alium.	And the proper procedure is to make the boy believe, especially if he is one who understands a little, that you are only tying thread around his penis; and you leave it until the next day.
Deinde fac eum gaudere et laetari omnimodo quo possibile est tibi illud, ex eo quod recipit intelligentia sua.	Then make him happy and delighted in every way possible, given what his understanding can receive.
Deinde fac eum stare inter manus tuas praeparatae staturae, et non sit sedens: et occulta forfices in manica tua, aut sub pede tuo, ne uideat eos puer omnino, neque aliquid ex instrumentis.	Then have him stand with his height adjusted between your hands, and not be sitting; and hide the scissors in your sleeve, or under your foot, so that the boy does not see them at all, nor any of the instruments.
Deinde intromitte manum tuam ad uirgam eius, et suffla in cutem, et trahe eam sursum, donec egrediatur caput uirgae.	Then place your hand on his penis, blow on the skin, and pull it upward until the head of the penis emerges.
Deinde mundifica ipsam ex eo quod aggregatur in ea sordicie.	Then cleanse it of any dirt that has gathered on it.
Deinde liga locum signatum cum filo duplo.	Then tie the marked spot with double thread.
Postea liga inferius eo parumper ligamentum secundum.	Afterward, tie a second ligature slightly below it.
Deinde tene cum indice tuo, et pollice locum ligamenti inferioris retentione bona, et incide inter duo ligamenta.	Then hold the place of the lower ligature firmly with your index finger and thumb, and cut between the two ligatures.
Deinde eleua cutem sursum uelociter, et extrahe caput uirgae.	Then lift the skin upward quickly and expose the head of the penis.
Deinde dimitte sanguinem currere paulatim (est enim melius) et pone puluerem desuper: et super puluerem pannum in quo expansus est uitellus oui decocti in aqua rosata, concussum cum oleo ros recenti bono: et dimitte eum super ipsum usque ad diem alium: et cura ipsum reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	Then let the blood flow gradually (for it is better), and apply powder on top; and over the powder, place a cloth spread with egg yolk cooked in rose water, shaken with fresh good rose oil: and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with the remaining remedies until it heals.
Forma autem forficis ad mundificationem haec est.	Now, the form of the scissors for cleansing is as follows.
Sint hebetes duae extremitates, et sint incidentes: ne egrediatur in eis ramus claui: et sit longitudo duarum acuitatum, sicut longitudo duorum manubriorum aequaliter.	The two ends should be blunt and cutting; let there be no branching pin between them, and the length of the two blades should be the same as the length of the two handles.
Error uero cadens in mundificatione est: quoniam fortasse effugit cutis intrinseca tota, aut pars eius apud incisionem.	The error that occurs in cleansing is this: that perhaps the inner skin may entirely escape, or part of it at the incision.
Ergo oportet, ut extendas eam ex hora tua cum ungue tuo ante apostemationem loci: et incidas eam secundum aequalitatem.	Therefore, it is necessary to stretch it immediately with your nail before the formation of an abscess in the area, and cut it evenly.
Quod si non potes tenere eam cum ungue tuo, tunc extrahe eam cum uncino, et incide eam.	If you cannot hold it with your nail, then draw it out with a hook and cut it.
Si autem praeterierint ei tres dies, et remanet quod est sub uirga inflatum, apostematum: tunc dimitte illud, donec sedetur apostema calidum, et excoria illud cum facilitate, et incide illud secundum quod praeparatur tibi: et caue tibi a capite uirgae.	But if three days have passed, and what is beneath the penis remains swollen, forming an abscess: then leave it until the warm abscess settles, and scrape it gently, and cut it according to what you have prepared for yourself; and take care around the head of the penis.
Non enim nocebit ei illud.	For that will not harm him.
Cura ergo illud cum eo quod consolidat uulnus ex pulueribus, quos narrauimus in tractatu de pulueribus: et si inciditur ex cute supra mensuram, et euadit ad superiora, non nocet ei illud etiam.	Therefore, treat it with something that heals the wound using powders, which we have described in the treatise on powders; and if the cut goes beyond the skin or extends upward, that also will not harm him.
Cura ergo illud cum eo quod diximus, donec sanetur.	Therefore, treat it with what we have said, until it heals.
¶ De extractione Vrinae retentae in uesica.	On the extraction of urine retained in the bladder.
Caput LVIII.	Chapter 58.
Urinae retentio in uesica, fit ab opilatione facta ex lapide, aut sanguine congelato, aut pus, aut carne nata, et similibus illis ex eis quae diximus ex modis curationis in diuisione.	Retention of urine in the bladder occurs due to obstruction caused by a stone, congealed blood, pus, flesh growth, and similar conditions among those we have discussed in the methods of treatment in this section.
Et si non soluitur Vrina, et uides retentionem eius esse propter Lapidem, qui iam est in collo uesicae: tunc oportet ut sit infirmus super genua sua curuatus.	And if the urine is not released, and you see that its retention is due to a stone lodged in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over on their knees.
Deinde componantur pedes eius super dorsum eius, et extendat uentrem suum ex superiori parte dorsi eius, et stringat infirmus anhelitum suum quantum possibile est ei.	Then position his feet upon his back, and let him stretch his belly above his back, and let the patient hold his breath as much as he can.
Cogitur ergo cum collo uesicae ad expulsionem Lapidis ad posteriora: quare absoluitur Vrina.	Thus, pressure is applied on the neck of the bladder to force the stone backward, and the urine is released.
Quod si non soluitur cum eo quod diximus, et uehemens sit res super infirmum: tunc oportet ut administres extractionem eius cum instrumento, quod nominatur siringa, cuius haec est forma. Sit ex argento, et sit subtile, lene, concauum sicut cannula pennae auis in subtilitate radii, longum in similitudine palmi unius et medii: cui sit cannula subtilis in capite eius.	But if this method does not work, and the condition is severe for the patient, then extraction must be administered using an instrument called a syringe, the design of which is as follows. It should be made of silver, and be slender, smooth, and hollow like the quill of a bird's feather in thinness, and about one and a half palms in length, with a thin tube at its tip.
Et modus exitus Vrinae per ipsum est, ut accipias filum duplicatum, et liges in extremitate eius lanam, aut cotum, ligatura bona: et intromittas extremitatem fili in inferiori parte Siringae: et incide cum forficibus si superfluit aliquid ex lana, uerum intromitte in cannulam cum uehementia, sicut alzer.	The method for releasing urine through this instrument is to take a doubled thread, tie wool or cotton securely to its end, and insert the thread’s end into the lower part of the syringe; and if there is excess wool, trim it with scissors, then insert it into the tube with firmness, like an insertion tool.
Deinde inunge siringam cum oleo, aut cum butyro, et albugine oui: et fac sedere infirmum super sedem, et embroca uesicam, et ipsius uirgam cum oleis humidis, et oleo oliuae, et aqua tepida.	Then anoint the syringe with oil, or with butter, and egg white; and make the patient sit upon a seat, apply warm oils to the bladder and his penis, with olive oil and warm water.
Deinde intromitte siringam in uirgam cum facilitate, donec perueniat ad radicem uirgae.	Then insert the syringe into the penis gently, until it reaches the base of the penis.
Deinde dupla ipsam superius a parte umbilici.	Then bend it above towards the direction of the navel.
Deinde impelle siringam intra ipsam, donec perueniat ad Vesicam, et sentiat eam infirmus iam peruenisse ad rem uacuam: et non fit hoc secundum hunc ordinem, nisi quoniam meatus, in quo uadit, est in quo est tortuositas.	Then push the syringe further in until it reaches the bladder, and the patient will feel that it has reached an empty space: this is done in this manner only because the passage it travels through has a curve.
Deinde extende filum cum lana paulatim.	Then gradually draw out the thread with the wool.
Vrina enim sequetur lanam.	For the urine will follow the wool.
Deinde extrahe eam, et fac currere Vrinam per uiam urinae: et itera siringam, et non cesses facere illud, donec euacuetur uesica, et inueniat infirmus alleuiationem.	Then remove it, and allow the urine to flow through the urinary passage; repeat the use of the syringe, and continue doing this until the bladder is emptied and the patient finds relief.
¶ De qualitate clisterizationis uesicae cum Clepshydra.	On the nature of the irrigation of the bladder with the clepsydra.
Caput LIX.	Chapter 59.
Quando accidit in uesica ulcus, aut sanguis in ea congelatur, aut coartatur in ea pus, et uis distillare in eam aquas et medicinas: tunc fiat cum instrumento quod nominatur Clepshydra, et haec est forma eius.	When an ulcer occurs in the bladder, or blood congeals in it, or pus gathers there, and you wish to instill water and medicines into it, this should be done with an instrument called a clepsydra, and this is its design.
Est enim surda, id est, clausa.	It is deaf, that is, closed.
Et in eo sunt tria foramina, duo ex parte una, et unum ex parte altera, sicut uides.	And it has three openings, two on one side, and one on the other, as you see.
Et locus concauus, in quo est illud quod impellit, sit secundum quantitatem quod opilet ipsum sine additione, donec quando trahitur cum eo aliquid, ex humiditatibus attrahatur: et quando impellitur, cum eo expellatur ad longinquum: secundum quod facit clepshydra, qua proiicitur naphta, id est, ignis graecus in praeliis martis.	And the hollow chamber, where the plunger is, should be of a size that fits without excess, so that when it is drawn, moisture is sucked in; and when pushed, it expels to a distance, as with the clepsydra used to project naphtha, or "Greek fire," in battles of Mars.
Cum ergo uis proiicere humiditates in uesicam, intromitte extremitatem clepshydrae in humiditatem, et trahe cum eo quod impellit ad superiora, humiditas enim trahitur in concauitatem clepshydrae.	So when you wish to project moisture into the bladder, insert the end of the clepsydra into the moisture, and draw up with the plunger; the moisture is drawn into the hollow chamber of the clepsydra.
Deinde intromitte extremitatem eius in uirgam, secundum quod narrauimus in siringa.	Then insert its end into the penis, as we described with the syringe.
Deinde impelle humiditatem cum eo quod impellit illa namque humiditas peruenit ad uesicam statim, ita quod sentit eam infirmus.	Then push the moisture with the plunger, so that this moisture reaches the bladder immediately, and the patient feels it.
Forma clisteris subtilis quo clisterizatur uesica.	The form of the slender irrigator by which the bladder is irrigated.
Fiat ex argento, aut auricalco: cuius caput altius sit simile alcama paruo, et sub eo sinus inter quem cadat ligamentum.	It should be made of silver or brass, with its head slightly raised like a small bowl, and beneath it, a hollow where a ligature may rest.
Deinde accipe uesicam arietis, et pone in ea humiditatem, qua uis clisterizare uesicam.	Then take a ram’s bladder, and place in it the moisture you wish to use for irrigating the bladder.
Deinde liga eam inter duos sinus ligatura forti cum filo duplo: et calefac illam humiditatem parumper super ignem.	Then tie it between the two hollows with a strong ligature using double thread, and warm that moisture slightly over a fire.
Deinde intromitte extremitatem clisteris in uirgam, postea stringe manum tuam super uesicam cum humiditate strictura decenti, donec sentiat infirmus, quod illa humiditas iam peruenit ad uesicam.	Then insert the end of the irrigator into the penis, and press your hand on the bladder containing the moisture with moderate pressure, until the patient feels that the moisture has now reached the bladder.
Si autem non est tibi praesens uesica, tunc accipe frustum pergameni, et fac ex eo circulum, et perfora ipsum ab omni rotunditate sua.	But if you do not have a bladder at hand, then take a piece of parchment, make a circle from it, and perforate it all around its circumference.
Deinde intromitte filum forte in illis foraminibus, sicut reuoluuntur.	Then insert a strong thread into those holes, as they go around.
Deinde aggrega circulum, sicut aggregatur alsofratu: postquam tu ponis in eo illud quod uis ex humiditatibus, et oleis, et aquis.	Then join the circle, as the "alsofrat" is joined: after you place in it whatever you want from moistures, oils, and waters.
Deinde liga ipsum in instrumento: et fac cum eo sicut fecisti cum uesica ex expressione cum manu tua, donec perueniat humiditas ad uesicam.	Then bind it to the instrument: and use it as you did with the bladder, by squeezing it with your hand, until the moisture reaches the bladder.
¶ De extractione Lapidis.	On the extraction of the stone.
Caput LX.	Chapter 60.
Iam diximus in diuisione species Lapidis, et curationem eius cum medicinis: et dixi differentiam inter Lapidem generatum in renibus, et uesica, et signa illius totius: et dixi Lapidem in quo cadit operatio cum manu et sectio: et est Lapis generatus in uesica proprie: et ille qui figitur in uirga: et ego sum narrans illud cum expositione manifesta et abbreuiatione.	I have already spoken in detail of the types of stones and their treatment with medicines: and I have explained the difference between a stone formed in the kidneys and one in the bladder, and all its signs: and I have mentioned the stone upon which surgery and incision fall: it is the stone specifically formed in the bladder, and also that which is lodged in the penis: and I am narrating this with a clear explanation and in a concise manner.
Dico ergo, quod Lapis generatus in uesica, plurimum accidit pueris.	I say, therefore, that a stone formed in the bladder occurs mostly in boys.
Et ex signis eius est, quod urina egreditur ex uesica similis aquae in subtilitate sua: et apparet in ea harena alba, et fricat infirmus uirgam suam, et laborat cum ea, et multotiens pendet.	And one of its signs is that the urine flows out from the bladder, similar to water in its thinness: white sand appears in it, and the patient rubs his penis, struggles with it, and often it becomes erect.
Deinde erigitur, et egreditur cum eo anus in multis eorum.	Then it rises, and the anus protrudes with it in many of them.
Et est facilis sanatio puerorum, ex eo usquequo consequuntur quatuordecim annos.	And healing is easy in children, up to the time when they reach fourteen years.
Et est difficilis in senibus.	And it is difficult in the elderly.
In iuuenibus autem est media, in eo quod est inter illud: et eius cuius Lapis est maior, curatio facilior: et si paruus, est econuerso illius cura.	In young people, it is intermediate, between the two: and for the one whose stone is larger, treatment is easier; and if it is small, it is the opposite in treatment.
Cum ergo peruenimus ad curationem, oportet in primis, ut mundificemus infirmum cum clisteri, quod extrahat totum stercus quod est in intestinis suis: ipsum enim quandoque prohibet inuentionem Lapidis apud inquisitionem.	Therefore, when we proceed to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, which will remove all the feces in his intestines: for sometimes this obstructs the detection of the stone during the examination.
Deinde accipiatur infirmus cum pedibus suis, et concutiatur, et moueatur ad inferiora: ut descendat Lapis ad profundum uesicae, aut saliat de loco alto aliquotiens.	Then the patient should be taken by his feet, shaken, and moved downwards: so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, or jumps from a high place at times.
Deinde fac eum sedere inter manus tuas praeparatum, et manus eius sint sub coxis ipsius, ut fiat uesica tota decliuis ad inferiora.	Then make him sit, positioned between your hands, with his hands under his hips, so that the entire bladder is inclined downwards.
Deinde perquire eum, et tange eum extrinsecus.	Then examine him, and touch him externally.
Si ergo sentis Lapidem in spacio, tunc propera statim cum sectione super ipsum.	If then you feel the stone in the space, proceed immediately with the incision upon it.
Quod si non cadat sub tactu tuo omnino, tunc oportet ut abstergas digitum indicem cum oleo manus sinistrae, si infirmus est puer: aut digitum medium si est iuuenis completus: et intromittas ipsum in anum suum, et perquire de Lapide, donec stat sub digito tuo: et conuerte eum paulatim ad collum uesicae.	But if it does not fall entirely under your touch, then you should anoint the index finger of your left hand with oil if the patient is a boy, or the middle finger if he is a grown youth: and insert it into his anus, and search for the stone, until it is under your finger: and gradually move it towards the neck of the bladder.
Deinde preme super ipsum cum digito tuo, et impelle ipsum ad exteriora aduersus locus, cuius sectionem uis: et praecipe ministro, ut premat uesicam manu sua, et praecipe alii ministro, ut extendat testiculos manu sua dextra ad superiora: et alia manu sua, ut remoueat cutem, quae est sub testiculis in parte a loco in quo est sectio.	Then press on it with your finger, and push it outward toward the area where you wish to make the incision: instruct an assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct another assistant to extend the testicles upwards with his right hand, and with his other hand to pull back the skin below the testicles in the area away from where the incision will be made.
Deinde intromitte Spatumile incidens, cuius forma haec est.	Then introduce the cutting Spatumile, which has this shape.
Et finde in eo quod est inter anum et testiculos, et non in medio, ad latus natis sinistrae: et sit sectio super ipsum lapidem, et digitus tuus sit in ano: et fiat sectio transuersa, ut sit sectio exterius ampla, et interius stricta, secundum quantitatem quod sit possibile egressio Lapidis ex ea non maior.	And make the incision in the area between the anus and the testicles, not in the middle, but to the left side of the buttocks: and let the incision be upon the stone itself, with your finger in the anus: and make a transverse incision, so that the outer part is wide and the inner part is narrow, according to a size that allows the stone to pass through, but no larger.
Fortasse enim comprimit digitus, qui est in ano Lapidem apud sectionem, et egreditur absque difficultate.	For sometimes the finger, which is in the anus, compresses the stone at the incision, and it exits without difficulty.
Et scias, quod ex Lapide est cui sunt anguli et margines, quare fit difficilis exitus eius propter illud.	And know that some stones have corners and edges, which makes their passage difficult for this reason.
Et ex eo est lenis, similis glandulae, et rotundus: et fit facilis egressus eius.	And some stones are smooth, similar to a gland, and round: and their passage is easy.
Ei ergo cui sunt anguli, et margines, adde in fissura.	For the one with corners and edges, enlarge the cut.
Quod si non egreditur ita, tunc oportet ut ingenies super ipsum: aut stringas super eum cum gesti decenter, cuius extremitas sit sicut Luna, quae stringat super Lapidem, et non euadat ab ea: aut ut intromittas sub eo instrumentum subtile, curuatae extremitatis.	But if it does not exit this way, then you must use ingenuity on it: either press on it appropriately with a tool whose end is shaped like the moon, to grip the stone, so that it does not escape from it; or insert beneath it a slender instrument with a curved end.
Si autem non potes super cum, tunc amplifica foramen parumper.	But if you are still unable to reach it, then enlarge the opening a little.
Quod si uincit te aliquid ex sanguine, abscinde ipsum cum zegi.	But if some bleeding overwhelms you, cut it with a zegi.
Si uero lapis est plus quam unus, tunc impelle in primis magnum ad os uesicae.	But if there is more than one stone, then first push the larger one towards the mouth of the bladder.
Deinde incide super ipsum.	Then cut over it.
Postea impelle paruum post illud: et similiter fac si sunt plures duobus.	Afterwards, push the smaller one after it: and do the same if there are more than two.
Quod si magnus est ualde, tunc ignorantia est ut seces super ipsum sectione magna.	But if it is very large, it is unwise to cut over it with a large incision.
Quoniam accidit infirmo una duarum rerum, aut ut moriatur, aut accidit ei distillatio urinae assidua: proptera, quia non consolidatur locus omnino.	For one of two things happens to the patient: either he dies, or he suffers from a constant dribbling of urine, because the place does not heal completely.
Verum administra expulsionem eius, donec egrediatur: aut ingenia in fractura eius cum forficibus, donec extrahas eum frustatim.	Rather, aid its expulsion until it exits: or use ingenuity in breaking it with forceps, until you extract it piece by piece.
Cum ergo compleueris operationem tuam, tunc imple uulnus thure, et aloe, et sanguine draconis: et stringe ipsum, et pone super ipsum pannum infusum oleo et uino, aut oleo rosato, et aqua frigida: ut sedetur apostema calidum.	When you have completed your operation, then fill the wound with frankincense, aloe, and dragon’s blood: bind it, and place over it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in rose oil and cold water, to calm the warm swelling.
Deinde resupina infirmum super collum suum, et non soluas ligamentum, usque ad diem tertium.	Then lay the patient back on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Cum ergo solueris ipsum, embroca locum cum aqua, et oleo multo.	When you loosen it, then wash the area with water and plenty of oil.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento dyafinicon, et unguento basilicon, donec sanetur.	Then treat it with dyafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it heals.
Si autem accidit in uulnere apostema calidum additum, et corrosi, et illi similia: sicut si congeletur sanguis in uesica, et prohibeatur ex eo urina: et cognoscitur illud ex egressione sanguinis cum urina.	If, however, a hot swelling occurs in the wound, along with corrosion and similar issues: such as when blood clots in the bladder and obstructs the urine: and this is recognized by the passage of blood with the urine.
Intromitte ergo digitum tuum in uulnus, et extrahe illum sanguinem.	Then insert your finger into the wound, and extract that blood.
Nam si remanet, prouocat ad corruptionem uesicae, et putrefactionem eius.	For if it remains, it causes the bladder to decay and rot.
Deinde ablue uulnus cum aceto, et aqua, et sale: et oppone omni speciei cum eo quod conuenit ex curatione, usquequo sanetur.	Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt: and apply every kind of treatment suitable until it is healed.
Et oportet in horis curationis totius, ut liges duas coxas, et aggreges, caussa medicinarum quae ponuntur super locum.	And during all treatment times, you must bind the two thighs and bring them together, to keep the medicines in place over the area.
Quod si lapis est paruus, et sit in meatu uirgae, et figitur in eo, et prohibetur urinae exitus: tunc cura ipsum cum eo quod narro antequam peruenias ad sectionem.	If the stone is small, lodged in the urethra, and blocks the exit of urine, then treat it with what I am telling you before you resort to incision.
Multotiens enim a sectione excusaris per hanc curationem, iam enim probaui illud.	Many times you can avoid incision by using this treatment, as I have already proven.
Et est, ut accipias Perforatorium ex ferro alferico, cuius haec est forma, triangulatae extremitatis, acutum, fixum in ligno.	And it involves taking a perforator made of iron from alfaric, in this form, with a triangular, sharp end fixed in wood.
Deinde accipe filum, et liga cum eo uirgam sub lapide ut non redeat ad uesicam.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so it does not return to the bladder.
Deinde intromitte ferrum perforans in uirgam cum facilitate, donec perueniat Perforatorium ad ipsum lapidem: et reuolue Perforatorium manu tua in ipso lapide paulatim: et coneris perforationem eius, donec facias ipsum penetrare a parte altera.	Then insert the perforating iron into the penis gently, until the perforator reaches the stone itself: and slowly rotate the perforator on the stone with your hand: and try to perforate it, until you make it pass through to the other side.
Urina namque absoluitur statim.	Then the urine flows out immediately.
Deinde preme manum tuam super illud quod remansit ex lapide ab exteriori parte uirgae.	Then press your hand over what remains of the stone on the outer part of the penis.
Ipse enim frangitur, et egreditur cum urina, et sanatur infirmus.	For it breaks, exits with the urine, and the patient is healed.
Si autem non praeparatur tibi haec curatio, propter aliquid quod prohibet ab illo: tunc liga filum sub lapide, et filum aliud supra lapidem.	But if this treatment cannot be prepared for you due to some obstruction, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it.
Deinde seca super lapidem in ipsa uirga inter duas ligaturas.	Then cut over the stone in the penis itself, between the two ties.
Deinde extrahe ipsum.	Then extract it.
Postea solue ligamentum, et mundifica sanguinem congelatum, qui fit in uulnere.	Afterwards, untie the binding and clean the clotted blood that has formed in the wound.
Et non est necessarium ligamentum fili sub lapide, nisi ut non redeat ad uesicam: et ligamentum aliud desuper, nisi ut quando soluitur filum post egressionem lapidis, redeat cutis ad locum suum, et cooperiat uulnus: et propter illud necesse est tibi illud quando ligas filum superius, ut eleues cutem ad superiora, ut redeat apud complementum tuum, et cooperiat uulnus, sicut diximus.	And the thread binding below the stone is only necessary to prevent it from returning to the bladder, and the upper thread binding is only necessary so that when the thread is loosened after the stone’s removal, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound: and for this, it is necessary when you tie the upper thread to lift the skin upward, so that it returns in its completion and covers the wound, as we have said.
¶ De extractione Lapidis mulierum.	On the extraction of the stone in women.
Caput LXI.	Chapter 61.
Parum generatur Lapis in mulieribus.	A stone rarely forms in women.
Si autem accidat alicui earum lapis, tunc difficilis est curatio, et prohibetur propter modos multos.	But if one of them develops a stone, the treatment is difficult and is hindered for several reasons.
Vnus eorum est: quod mulier fortasse est uirgo.	One of these is that the woman may be a virgin.
Et secundus est, quia tu non inuenis mulierem quae detegat seipsam medico, quando est casta, aut ex habentibus maritos.	The second is that you may not find a woman willing to expose herself to a doctor if she is chaste or married.
Tertius est, quia tu non inuenis mulierem bene scientem hanc artem, praecipue operationem cum manu.	The third is that you may not find a woman well-versed in this art, especially in manual procedures.
Et quartus est longinquitas a loco lapidis: quare indiget sectione profunda, et in illo est timor.	And the fourth is the distance from the location of the stone, which requires a deep incision, and this carries risks.
Quod si necessitas prouocat ad illud, tunc oportet ut accipias mulierem medicam, bene scientem: et parum inuenitur.	If necessity calls for it, then you should find a female doctor who is skilled, though such are rare.
Si uero priuaris ea, tunc quaere medicum castum, subtilem, et praesenta mulierem obstetricem bene doctam in re mulierum, aut mulierem quae in hac arte innuit partem artis: fac ergo eam praesentem, et praecipue ei, ut faciat totum quod praecipis ei ex inquisitione super lapidem.	If you cannot find her, then seek a chaste, skilled doctor, and bring along a midwife well-versed in women's matters, or a woman familiar with this part of the art; make her present and instruct her to follow all your directions in examining the stone.
In primis quod est, ut aspiciat si mulier est uirgo: tunc oportet ut intromittat digitum in anum eius, et quaerat lapidem.	First, she should determine if the woman is a virgin: if so, she must insert her finger into the anus and search for the stone.
Si ergo inuenit ipsum, coartet eum sub digito suo, et tunc praecipe obstetrici, ut intromittat digitum suum in uuluam infirmae, et inquirat super lapidem, postquam ponit manum suam sinistram super uesicam, et comprimit eam compressione bona.	If she finds it, she should press it beneath her finger, and then instruct the midwife to insert her finger into the patient’s vulva and examine the stone, after placing her left hand over the bladder and applying firm pressure.
Si ergo inuenit lapidem, tunc oportet ut gradatim moueat eum ab orificio uesicae ad inferiora cum summa uirtutis suae, donec perueniat cum eo ad radicem coxae.	If she finds the stone, she should then gradually move it from the opening of the bladder downward with all her strength, until it reaches the base of the thigh.
Deinde secet super eum apud oppositionem medietatis uuluae apud radicem coxae, ex quacunque parte praeparatur ei, et sentit lapidem in illa parte: et digitus eius non remoueatur a lapide, coartans sub eo: et sit sectio parua in primis.	Then make an incision over it at the midpoint of the vulva near the base of the thigh, on whichever side it is positioned and where she feels the stone: her finger should not move from the stone, pressing under it, and the initial incision should be small.
Deinde intromittat radium super illam sectionem.	Then she should insert the probe into that incision.
Si ergo sentit lapidem, tunc addat in sectionem secundum quantitatem proportionatam quod lapis egreditur ab ea.	If she feels the stone, then enlarge the incision by a proportionate amount so that the stone can pass through it.
Et scias, quod species lapidis sunt multae.	And know that there are many types of stones.
Ex his enim est paruus, et magnus, lenis et asper, longus, et rotundus habens ramos.	Among them are small and large, smooth and rough, long, and round ones with branches.
Scias ergo species eius, ut significetur tibi per hoc super illud quod uis.	Therefore, know its type, so that you are better informed on what to expect.
Si ergo uincit te sanguis, tunc adde in loco zegi tritum, et tene ipsum hora una, donec abscindatur sanguis.	If bleeding overwhelms you, then apply powdered zegi to the area, and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops.
Deinde redi ad operationem tuam, donec egrediatur lapis: et fac, ut praepares tecum ex instrumentis, quae dixi in extractione lapidis in uiris, ut adiuueris per ea in operatione tua.	Then return to your operation until the stone is extracted: and make sure you have with you the instruments I mentioned for extracting stones in men, so they may aid you in your operation.
Quod si uincit te fluxus sanguinis, et scis quod expulsio sanguinis est ex arteria quae incisa est: tunc pone puluerem super locum, et stringe eum cum puluillis strictura decenti: et non mutes illud: et dimitte lapidem, et non extrahas ipsum.	But if bleeding overcomes you and you know that the bleeding is from a severed artery, then apply powder to the area, compress it with pads of appropriate tightness, and do not change it: and leave the stone alone, do not extract it.
Fortasse enim morietur mulier infirma.	For the sick woman might die.
Deinde cura uulnus.	Then treat the wound.
Cum ergo sedatur acuitas sanguinis post dies, et putrefit locus, tune redi ad operationem tuam, donec egrediatur lapis.	When the intensity of the bleeding subsides after a few days, and the area has softened, then return to your operation until the stone exits.
¶ De sectione super Herniam aquosam.	On the incision for a watery hernia.
Caput LXII.	Chapter 62.
Ramex aquosa non est, nisi aggregatio humiditatis in sifac albo, quod est sub cute testiculi continente ouum: et nominatur sifac.	A watery swelling is nothing but an accumulation of moisture in the white membrane, which is under the skin of the testicle containing the egg, and it is called "sifac."
Et quandoque est in panniculo proprio sibi, quem praeparauit ei natura in parte oui, donec putetur: quod est ouum aliud, et est cutis testiculi inter sifac album, quod diximus: et non fit illud nisi raro.	And sometimes it is in its own membrane, which nature has prepared for it in part of the egg, until it ripens; this is another egg, and the skin of the testicle is between it and the white membrane we mentioned, though this is rare.
Et generatio quidem huius ramicis, est ex debilitate quae accidit testiculis: quare effunditur ad eos haec materia.	And indeed the generation of this swelling comes from a weakness that happens to the testicles, wherefore this matter is discharged to them.
Et quandoque accidit ex percussione super testiculos.	And sometimes it happens from a blow to the testicles.
Et haec humiditas est habens colores multos.	And this moisture has many colors.
Aut enim est color eius decliuis ad citrinitatem, aut est sanguineus rubeus, aut faeculentus, niger, aut est aquosus albus, et est illud quod est plus.	For its color is either inclined to yellowness, or it is blood-red, or it is muddy black, or it is watery white, and this is the most common.
Et signa quibus scitur ubi sit aggregatio aquae, sunt ista.	And the signs by which the location of the water accumulation is known are as follows.
Nam si est in sifac albo quod diximus, tunc apostema est rotundum ad longitudinem parumper sicut figura oui: et non apparet testiculus, quoniam humiditas continet eum ab omni parte.	For if it is in the white membrane we mentioned, then the swelling is round and somewhat elongated like the shape of an egg, and the testicle does not appear, because the moisture surrounds it on all sides.
Et si est humiditas in panniculo proprio sibi, tunc apostema est rotundum cum parte oui, et propter hoc extimat homo quia est ouum aliud.	And if the moisture is in its own membrane, then the swelling is round with part of the egg, and for this reason a person thinks it is another egg.
Et si humiditas est inter cutem testiculorum et sifac album, tunc cadit sub sensu.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, then it falls under sensation.
Quando ergo uis cognitionem coloris humiditatis, tunc experire colorem humiditatis in apostemate cum Intromisso quadrato, cuius forma praecessit.	Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, then test the color of the moisture in the swelling with a square introducer, the form of which was previously described.
Secundum illud ergo quod egreditur in uestigio Intromissi, iudica de illo quod est inter ipsum.	Thus, according to what appears in the track of the introducer, judge concerning that which is within it.
Cum ergo uenimus ad curationem cum ferro, tunc oportet ut praecipias infirmo, ut phlebotometur si possibile est ei illud, et uides corpus eius plenum.	Therefore, when we come to the cure with the knife, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to be bled if possible for him, and you observe that his body is full.
Deinde resupinetur super dorsum suum super rem altam parum, et pone sub eo pannos multos.	Then he should be laid on his back on a somewhat elevated surface, and place many cloths under him.
Deinde sede tu super sinistram eius, et praecipe ministro, ut sedeat a dextra eius, qui extendat uirgam eius ad unum duorum laterum cutis testiculorum, et ad partem mirach uentris.	Then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right side, who will stretch his member to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles, and towards the part of the abdomen.
Deinde accipe spatumile latum, et seca cutem testiculorum ex medio per longitudinem, usque prope pectinem: et fiat sectio secundum rectitudinem aequedistantis lineae quae diuidit cutem testiculorum, donec perueniat ad sifac album comprehendens: et excoria ipsum et obserua, uel caue ex hoc, ut seces ipsum: et sit excoriatio tua qua ipsum excorias, ex parte quae suspenditur cum ouo plus: et subtiliter scrutare cum excoriatione secundum quantitatem quod tibi possibile est.	Then take a wide spatula and cut the skin of the testicles from the middle along the length, up to near the pubic hair; and let the incision be made in the straight line that divides the skin of the testicles, until it reaches the white membrane encompassing it; and flay it and observe, or take care lest you cut it; and let the flaying by which you strip it be from the part that is more suspended with the egg; and carefully examine with the stripping to the extent that is possible for you.
Deinde perfora sifac plenum aqua perforatione ampla, et extrahe totam aquam.	Then pierce the white membrane full of water with a wide perforation, and draw out all the water.
Deinde separa inter duo labia sectionis cum uncinis, et extende sifac ad superiora, et non tangas cutem testiculorum comprehendentem: et incide sifac qualitercunque est possibile tibi incidere ipsum, aut cum totalitate sua, aut frustatim, praecipue latus eius subtile.	Then separate the two lips of the incision with hooks, and stretch the white membrane upwards, and do not touch the skin enclosing the testicles; and cut the white membrane however it is possible for you to cut it, either in its entirety, or in pieces, especially its thinner side.
Nam si tu non exquisite perscrutaris, in incisione eius non fit securitas, quin aqua redeat.	For if you do not examine closely, security is not achieved in its incision, lest the water returns.
Si autem procedit ouum exterius a cute sua in hora operationis tuae: tunc quando compleueris sectionem sifac, reduc ipsum.	However, if the egg protrudes outward from its skin at the time of your operation, then when you complete the incision of the white membrane, return it.
Deinde aggrega duo labia cutis testiculorum cum sutura.	Then join the two lips of the skin of the testicles with a suture.
Deinde cura ipsum sicut reliqua uulnera, donec sanetur.	Then care for it as with other wounds, until it heals.
Quod si inuenis ouum corruptum ex nigredine alia, tunc oportet ut liges uasa, quae sunt suspensorium, timens fluxum sanguinis.	But if you find the egg corrupted by some blackness, then you must tie the vessels, which are the suspensory structures, fearing the flow of blood.
Deinde abscinde testiculum cum suspensorio, et extrahe ouum: postea cura illud cum eo quod diximus.	Then cut off the testicle with the suspensory, and extract the egg; afterwards treat it with what we have mentioned.
Si uero aqua est aggregata in duabus partibus, tunc scias quia sunt duae ramices: seca ergo partem aliam secundum quod fecisti in altera aequaliter.	But if the water is accumulated in two parts, then know that there are two swellings; therefore cut the other part as you did the first one, equally.
Et si aequatur tibi, ut sit operatio una, tunc fac: deinde absterge sanguinem.	And if it is manageable for you to make it one operation, then do it; then wipe away the blood.
Et intromitte in sectiones lanam submersam in oleo, aut in oleo rosato: et pone deforis lanam aliam quam submersisti in uino et oleo, et expande eam super duos testiculos, et mirach uentris: et pone desuper pannos duplicatos, et sunt puluilli: et liga eos desuper cum ligamento, quod est habens sex secundum hanc formam.	And insert into the incisions wool soaked in oil or in rose oil; and on the outside, place other wool soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over both testicles and the lower abdomen; and place doubled cloths on top, which are cushions; and bind them above with a bandage, which has six according to this pattern.
Deinde sumantur duo panni, et suantur, et impleantur lana carminata, secundum hanc similitudinem: et fiant extremitates quibus premitur ex coto, aut lana humida: et aggregentur cum strictura in lumbari bracharum: et una extremitatum accipiat super anum usque ad dorsum, et secunda accipiat ad partem pectinis: et duae extremitates super duas coxas inferius, et duae extremitates aliae super duo inguina, et aggregetur strictura tota in lumbari bracharum.	Then take two cloths, and sew them, and fill them with carded wool, according to this model: and make ends with which it is pressed with cotton or wet wool; and gather them with tightness in the waistband of the trousers; and one end reaches over the anus to the back, and the second reaches to the area of the groin; and two ends over the two thighs below, and the other two ends over the two groins, and the whole tightness is gathered in the waistband of the trousers.
Et, quandoque artificialiter medicatur haec ramex cum cauterio loco sectionis cum ferro: et est, ut accipias cauterium cultellare subtile, et seces cum eo cutem testiculorum: et est ignitum, secundum quod narrauimus: donec quando detegitur sifac album continens aquam: tunc accipe cauterium, secundum hanc formam.	And, sometimes this swelling is treated artificially with cautery instead of incision with a knife: and it is done by taking a thin knife-like cautery, and cutting the skin of the testicles with it; and it is heated, as we have described: until when the white membrane containing water is exposed; then take the cautery, in this shape.
Assimilatur literae graecae.	It resembles a Greek letter.
Deinde perfora cum eo illud sifac, et est ignitum, donec egrediatur humiditas tota.	Then pierce that white membrane with it while it is heated, until all the moisture exits.
Deinde extende sifac cum uncinis, et excoria cum cauterio subtili ignito, et incide ipsum secundum quod possibile est tibi, donec eradices totum eius.	Then stretch the white membrane with hooks, and strip it with a fine heated cautery, and cut it as much as is possible for you, until you eradicate it entirely.
Et caue ex ouo, ne tangat ipsum ignis.	And be careful of the egg, so that the fire does not touch it.
Et scias, quod haec operatio est saluior, et longinquior a fluxu sanguinis, et melior quam operatio cum sectione.	And know that this operation is safer, and further from blood flow, and better than the operation with incision.
Si uero contrarietatem tibi facit in hora sectionis, aut in hora cauterii apostema calidum, aut fluxus sanguinis, aut aliquid aliud: tunc oportet ut cures quod contrarietatem tibi facit ex illo cum curatione quae conuenit ei, secundum quod praemissum est.	But if any resistance occurs at the time of incision, or at the time of cautery, a hot swelling, or blood flow, or something else, then it is necessary to treat what resists you with the treatment that is appropriate for it, as was previously mentioned.
Si autem infirmus est timidus, et non expectat super hanc operationem, propter horribilitatem suam: tunc administra perforationem secundum quod ego narro illud: et est.	But if the patient is fearful, and cannot endure this operation because of its terrifying nature, then perform the puncture as I describe it: and it is.
Quando certificatur tibi apud te per illud quod diximus de significationibus, quod ramex est aquosa: tunc oportet quod facias sedere infirmum super sedem eleuatam.	When it is confirmed to you by what we have said about the signs, that the swelling is watery, then it is necessary to make the patient sit on an elevated seat.
Deinde perfora apostema in inferiori parte sui cum spatumili lato: et pone perforationem secundum longitudinem corporis, et sit apertio ampla, donec currat aqua tota.	Then pierce the swelling at its lower part with a wide spatula: and make the puncture along the length of the body, and let the opening be wide, until all the water flows out.
Deinde pone super locum cotum, et liga ipsum, et dimitte ipsum ut currat residuum aquae: deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur uulnus.	Then place cotton on the area, and bind it, and leave it so that the remaining water flows out: then treat it, until the wound heals.
Si autem contrarietas sit egressioni aquae in hora qua perforas ipsam: et non sit illud nisi propterea, quia panniculus albus contrarietatem facit in orificio uulneris, et prohibet exitum aquae: tunc oportet ut intromittas pennam in uulnus, aut instrumentum cum quo extrahitur aqua hydropicorum, cuius forma praecessit: aut adde in operatione uulneris parumper.	But if there is resistance to the flow of water at the time when you pierce it, and this is only because the white membrane causes resistance in the wound opening, and prevents the water from exiting, then you must insert a feather into the wound, or an instrument by which water is extracted from dropsical patients, the shape of which was previously described; or modify the wound operation slightly.
Et scias, quod aqua redit, et aggregatur post sex menses, aut circiter eos.	And know that the water returns, and accumulates after six months, or around that time.
Cum ergo aggregatur, tunc pertoretur secundum eundem modum, et pertransibit infirmus dies suos.	When it accumulates again, then it should be pierced in the same way, and the patient will pass his days.
¶ De cura Ramicis carnosae.	On the treatment of fleshy swelling.
Caput LXIII.	Chapter 63.
Scias, quod in sectione super hanc Ramicem, est ex timore perducente ad perniciem in pluribus dispositionibus.	Know that in cutting for this swelling, there is danger that leads to harm in many cases.
Quapropter uidetur mihi eius dimissio saluari ex ea.	Therefore, it seems to me that leaving it alone is safer for it.
Et ego sum rememorans operationem in ea, et species apostematis.	And I am recalling the operation for it, and the types of swelling.
Dico ergo, quod accidunt apostemata multa in corporibus, ex quibus componuntur testiculi: et fit illud ex caussis multis, scilicet.	I say, therefore, that many swellings occur in the bodies that make up the testicles, and it happens from many causes, namely.
Aut ex superfluitate acuta, uel acri, quae effunditur ad testiculos.	Either from an acute or sharp excess, which flows to the testicles.
Aut ex percussione.	Or from a blow.
Et est color apostematis secundum colorem corporis, et non inuenitur ei dolor: et est apostema graue.	And the color of the swelling is like the color of the body, and it is not painful: and it is a hard swelling.
Et fortasse est apostema lapideum, cuius color est fuscus, et non est sensus ei.	And perhaps it is a stone-like swelling, whose color is dark, and it has no sensation.
Et quandoque fit ex nodatione arteriarum, et inflatione earum: sicut iam praecessit eius rememoratio: aut ex inflatione uenarum.	And sometimes it arises from the twisting of the arteries and their swelling, as has already been mentioned, or from the swelling of the veins.
Quod ergo est ex eis ex inflatione arteriarum, cognoscitur per dispositionem apostematis, quando comprimis ipsum digitis tuis.	Therefore, what comes from the swelling of the arteries is recognized by the appearance of the swelling when you press it with your fingers.
Et non oportet ut tangas ipsum prorsus.	And it is not necessary that you touch it at all.
Illud uero quod fit ex inflatione uenarum, non dispergitur ex eo aliquid apud compressionem cum digitis.	But that which arises from the swelling of the veins does not disperse at all when compressed with the fingers.
Et iam possibile est, quod super hanc speciem fiat sectio, et super reliquas carnes: et est, ut seces cutem testiculorum.	And now it is possible that an incision be made on this type and on the surrounding flesh: and so, you must cut the skin of the testicles.
Deinde extende ouum ad sursum, et extrahe ipsum cum sifach albo: et libera suspensorium ex uasis, et liga uasa: et incide suspensorium postquam tu liberas ipsum ab omni parte ex partibus oui.	Then, pull the testicle upwards and remove it with a white cloth; free the suspensory ligament from the vessels, tie the vessels, and cut the suspensory ligament after you have freed it from every part of the testicle.
Si ergo ouum consolidatum est cum illis carnibus natis, tunc oportet ut attrahas ouum, et incidas ipsum.	If, therefore, the testicle is joined with those growing tissues, then it is necessary to draw out the testicle and cut it.
Et si adhaerentia est inter aliquid ex siphaket, aut in eo quod est inter uasa: tunc oportet ut liberes totam illam adhaerentiam, et incidas eam incisione rotunda.	And if there is an adhesion between any part of the membrane or between the vessels, then you must free all that adhesion and cut it with a circular incision.
Si autem est natiuitas carnis in loco adhaerentiae quae est retro: tunc oportet ut incidas totum eius, et extrahas ouum, sicut diximus.	But if there is a growth of flesh at the site of adhesion behind it, then you must cut all of it and remove the testicle as we have described.
Cum ergo completur operatio tua, tnnc imple uulnus in lana infusa in oleo rosato, et uino: deinde cura ipsum cum reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	When your operation is complete, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine; then treat it with the remaining care until it heals.
¶ De cura Ramicis, quae est cum Vite.	On the treatment of Varicocele, which occurs with a swelling.
Caput LXIIII.	Chapter 64.
Uitis est apostema inuolutum quadam inuolutione, simile botro, cum mollificatione testiculorum: et fit difficilis super infirmum motus et exercitium, et deambulatio.	The swelling is an abscess enveloped in a certain layer, resembling a cluster of grapes, along with the softening of the testicles, and it makes movement, exercise, and walking difficult for the patient.
Et in curatione huius aegritudinis est ex timore, propter illud cuius praecessit rememoratio.	And in the treatment of this condition, there is a need for caution due to what has been previously mentioned.
Verum oportet, ut dicamus operationem in ea secundum quod fecerunt primi.	But it is necessary that we describe the operation as the ancients performed it.
Dico ergo, quod oportet ut facias sedere infirmum super sedem eleuatam.	I say, therefore, that you must make the patient sit on an elevated seat.
Deinde impelle suspensorium testiculorum ad inferiora.	Then, push the suspensory ligament of the testicles downward.
Deinde tene cutem testiculorum cum digitis tuis, cum uasis quae sunt propinqua uirgae: et teneat ea minister alius, et extendat ea extensione uehementi.	Then, hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, along with the vessels near the penis; and another assistant should hold and stretch them with a strong extension.
Deinde incide cum spatumili lato acuto sectione transuersa in directo uasorum, donec detegantur uasa.	Then cut with a broad, sharp blade, making a transverse incision in line with the vessels until the vessels are exposed.
Deinde excoria ab omni parte, sicut diximus tibi in extractione Arteriarum quae sunt in timporibus.	Then strip away from every part, as we described to you in the extraction of the arteries in the temples.
Postea fige in eis acum in qua sit filum duplum, et liga ipsum in primo locorum quibus accidunt Vites: et liga ipsum iterum in ultimo eorum.	Afterwards, insert a needle with a doubled thread into them, and tie it at the first place where the swellings occur, and tie it again at the end of these locations.
Deinde seca ea in media sectione recta secundum longitudinem corporis, et extrahe quod aggregatur ex humiditatibus faeculentis corruptis.	Then cut them in the middle with a straight incision along the body's length and extract the accumulated foul and corrupted fluids.
Deinde cura uulnus cum curatione reliquorum uulnerum, in quibus uis generari saniem, ut cadant uasa quae nutriunt unum testiculorum.	Then treat the wound with the same treatment as for other wounds where you wish to produce suppuration so that the vessels which nourish one of the testicles are severed.
Non est enim malum per illud.	For it is not harmful because of this.
Si autem accidat Vitis omnibus uasis, tunc oportet ut extrahantur propter hoc testiculi cum uasis: ut non priuetur ouum nutrimento, propter incisionem, et tabescat, uel arescat, et non sit iuuamentum cum eis.	But if the swelling affects all the vessels, then it is necessary to remove the testicles along with the vessels, so that the testicle is not deprived of nourishment, which would cause it to waste away, or dry up, and there would be no benefit in keeping them.
¶ De cura Ramicis intestinalis.	On the treatment of intestinal rupture.
Caput LXV.	Chapter 65.
Euentus huius Ramicis est ex sectione, quae accidit in sifach extenso super uentrem in parte inguinum ex mirach uentris.	The occurrence of this rupture is from a cut, which happens in the membrane stretched over the abdomen in the area of the groin from the lower abdomen.
Quare descendunt intestina ex illa Ruptura ad unum testiculorum.	Therefore, the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles.
Et haec Ruptura est aut ex sifach, aut extensione eius.	And this rupture is either from the membrane or its extension.
Et accidunt istae duae species ex caussis multis: aut ex percussione, aut saltu, aut clamore, aut eleuatione rei grauis, et similibus.	And these two types happen for many reasons: either from a blow, a jump, a shout, lifting a heavy object, and similar causes.
Et signum, quando est ex extensione sifach.	And the sign, when it is from the extension of the membrane.
Est quod accidit paulatim in tempore longo, et non accidit subito: et est apostema aequale uersus profundum: propterea, quod sifach comprimit intestinum.	Is that it happens gradually over a long time, and does not happen suddenly: and it is a swelling equally towards the depth, because the membrane compresses the intestine.
Et signum eius quando est ex sectione sifach, quia facit accidere ex principio sui dolorem uehementem subito: et est apostema diuersum, apparens sub cute propinque: et illud est propter exitum intestini, et cursus eius ad exteriora sifach.	And the sign of it when it is from a cut in the membrane is that it causes intense pain suddenly from its beginning: and it is a swelling, irregular, appearing close under the skin: and this is due to the exit of the intestine, and its movement to the exterior of the membrane.
Et quandoque egreditur cum intestino zirbum: et nominatur haec Ramex intestinalis, et zirbia: et quandoque fit cum uentositate.	And sometimes a zirbum comes out with the intestine: and this is called an intestinal rupture and zirbia: and sometimes it occurs with wind.
Et quandoque currit in intestinum stercus, et retinetur illic: et est cum eo pernicies infirmi: quoniam facit accidere dolorem prauum, et praecipue quando premitur.	And sometimes feces move into the intestine and are retained there: and with this is harm to the patient, since it causes severe pain, especially when pressed.
Et in curatione specierum aegritudinis huius cum ferro est timor: quare oportet ut caueatur casus in ea.	And in the treatment of this type of illness with surgery, there is danger; therefore, it is necessary to be cautious of complications in it.
Et modus operationis est, ut praecipias infirmo, ut reducat intestinum manu sua ad interiora concauitatis suae, si obedit reditui.	And the method of operation is that you instruct the patient to return the intestine with his hand to the interior of its cavity, if it will respond to being returned.
Deinde resupinetur super collum suum inter manus tuas: et eleua crura eius.	Then he is to be laid back on his neck between your hands, and his legs are lifted.
Deinde extende cutem quae sequitur cutem ad superiora, et seca cutem testiculorum totam per longitudinem.	Then stretch the skin that follows the skin upwards, and cut the entire skin of the testicles along its length.
Deinde fige in duobus labiis sectionis uncinos, secundum quod indiges ad aperiendum sectionem cum eis: et sectio sit secundum quantitatem, quod sit possibile, ut egrediatur ex ea ouum.	Then fix hooks into the two lips of the incision, as you need to open the incision with them; and let the incision be to such a size that it is possible for an egg to come out of it.
Deinde excoria siphak, et quae sunt sub cute testiculorum, donec quando detegitur sifach album, durum ab omni parte: tunc intromitte digitum tuum indicem in eo quod sequitur testiculum, in eo quod est inter siphach album, quod est sub cute oui, et inter sifach secundum, et absolue cum eo adhaerentiam quae est in posteriori parte oui.	Then scrape away the membrane, and what is under the skin of the testicles, until the white membrane is revealed, hard on all sides; then insert your index finger into the area that follows the testicle, in that which is between the white membrane under the skin of the egg and the second membrane, and release with it the adhesion which is on the back part of the egg.
Deinde moue cum manu dextra ad interiora cutem testiculorum: et cum hoc extende sifach album ad sursum, cum manu sinistra: et eleua ouum cum sifach ad partem sectionis: et praecipe ministro, ut extendat ouum ad sursum: et tu solue adhaerentiam, quae est retro solutione completa.	Then move with your right hand the skin of the testicles inward; and with this, extend the white membrane upward with your left hand: and lift the egg with the membrane toward the side of the incision: and instruct your assistant to extend the egg upward: and you release the adhesion, which is at the back, with complete separation.
Et quaere digitis tuis, ut non sit aliquid illic ex intestino inuoluto in sifach albo duro.	And check with your fingers that there is nothing there from the intestine wrapped in the hard white membrane.
Si autem inuenis ex eo aliquid: tunc impelle ipsum ad uentrem inferius.	If, however, you find anything of it, then push it back towards the lower abdomen.
Deinde accipe acum, in qua sit filum grossum, factum licinium ex decem filis: et intromitte ipsam apud postremum sifach, id est, tunicae, quod est sub cute testiculorum quae sequitur sectionem: deinde incide extremitates quae eminent ex filo, donec sint quatuor fila.	Then take a needle, in which there is a thick thread, made of linen from ten threads: and insert it at the base of the membrane, that is, the tunic which is under the skin of the testicles that follows the incision: then cut the ends that extend from the thread, until there are four threads.
Deinde compone quaedam eorum super quaedam cum figura quae sit in modo crucis: et liga cum eis alsifach, de quo diximus, quia est sub cute testiculorum ligamento uehementi, donec non possit aliquod ex uasis, quae nutriunt eos mittere ad eos aliquid: ut non accidat inde apostema calidum.	Then arrange some of them over others in a shape like a cross: and tie the membrane, of which we spoke, that is under the skin of the testicles with a strong ligature, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can send anything to them, so that a warm swelling does not occur from there.
Et pone iterum ligamentum secundum extra ligamentum primum, longinquum ab eo minus duobus digitis.	And again place a second ligature outside the first ligature, two fingers away from it.
Et post ista duo ligamenta dimitte ex sifach, quod est sub cute testiculorum, quantitatem magnitudinis digiti: et incide reliquum totum secundum rotunditatem, et aufer ex eo ouum.	And after these two ligatures, leave a portion of the membrane under the skin of the testicles, the size of a finger’s breadth, and cut the rest completely around, and remove the egg from it.
Deinde seca in inferiori parte cutis testiculorum sectione, ex qua currit sanguis, et sanies: sicut narrauimus in eo quod praemissum est.	Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles at the incision, from which blood and serum flow, as we described in what was previously stated.
Deinde administra lanam submersam in oleo, et pone in uulnus: et administra ligamentum quod narrauimus.	Then apply wool soaked in oil, and place it on the wound: and apply the bandage which we described.
Et quandoque cauterizatur sifach album quod diximus, post incisionem eius timendo de fluxu sanguinis.	And sometimes the white membrane, as we said, is cauterized after its incision to prevent blood flow.
Multotiens enim accidit illud.	For it often happens.
Et dimitte ligamentum, donec cadat per se.	And leave the bandage until it falls off on its own.
Si autem tardatur casus eius, tunc embrocetur cum aqua calida: et pone super ipsum illud quod diximus, donec cadat.	If it takes too long to fall off, then bathe it with warm water: and place on it what we said, until it falls.
Deinde cura uulnus cum reliqua curatione uulnerum, donec curetur.	Then treat the wound with the remaining treatment for wounds, until it is healed.
¶ De Ramice uentosa.	On a windy rupture.
Caput LXVI.	Chapter 66.
IN Hac Ramice non uidi aliquem qui ausus fuerit super curationem eius cum ferro.	In this rupture, I have not seen anyone who dared to treat it with surgery.
Et primi quidem dixerunt, quod fit sicut narrauimus in Ramice quae est cum Vite.	And the first ones indeed said that it is done as we described in the rupture that involves the scrotum.
Quod est, ut liges uasa post sectionem super ea cum facilitate inferius: deinde seca in medio, et cura postremo cum eo quod aperit ipsum, donec cadant uasa: et cura uulnus, secundum quod diximus, donec sanetur.	That is, to tie the vessels below the section with ease: then cut in the middle, and finally treat it with what opens it until the vessels fall away: and treat the wound, as we said, until it is healed.
¶ De disruptione quae fit in inguinibus.	On the rupture that occurs in the groin.
Caput LXVII.	Chapter 67.
Quando accidit Ruptura in inguinibus, sicut diximus, et eminet locus, et non descendit ad testiculos aliquid ex intestinis: et si descendit, est illud parum, et redit in omnibus horis: uerum si prolongatur cum ea tempus, additur fissura in sifach, donec descendunt intestina in sifach.	When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we said, and the area swells, and nothing of the intestines descends to the testicles; and if something descends, it is little, and it returns every hour. But if time is prolonged with it, a tear is added in the membrane, until the intestines descend into the membrane.
Et accidit illud ex extensione sifach, quod est in inguinibus, sicut diximus.	And this happens from the extension of the membrane, which is in the groin, as we said.
Quod est, quia extenditur sifach: deinde mollificatur, et apostematur locus, et eminet.	That is, because the membrane is stretched: then it softens, the area swells, and it protrudes.
Et cura eius est cum cauterio, sicut praecessit eius narratio.	And its treatment is with cautery, as previously narrated.
Et quandoque curatur cum ferro, secundum hunc modum: et est, ut iaceat infirmus super dorsum suum inter manus tuas.	And sometimes it is treated with surgery, in the following way: that the patient should lie on his back between your hands.
Deinde seca locum Rupturae apostematum et eminentem, sectione per latitudinem, secundum quantitatem trium digitorum.	Then cut the swollen and protruding rupture site, with an incision across it the width of three fingers.
Deinde stringe alsifak et, quae sunt sub cute, donec quando detegitur sifach album, quod est sub cute quae sequitur ipsum.	Then tie the membrane and what is under the skin, until the white membrane, which is under the skin that follows it, is revealed.
Tunc accipe radium, et pone ipsum super locum eminentem ex sifach, et preme ipsum ad profundum uentris.	Then take a rod, and place it on the protruding area of the membrane, and press it to the depth of the abdomen.
Deinde sue duo loca eminentia super extremitatem radii ex sifach, et annecte cum sutura unum eorum cum altero: deinde extrahe extremitatem radii.	Then sew the two protruding places over the end of the rod from the membrane, and connect one of them with the other using a suture: then withdraw the end of the rod.
Et non incidas alsifach omnino, neque tendas ouum, neque aliud, sicut feci te scire in curatione ramicis intestinalis.	And do not cut the membrane entirely, nor extend the testicle, nor anything else, as I explained to you in the treatment of intestinal ruptures.
Deinde cura illud curatione uulnerum.	Then treat it with wound care.
Cum ergo incidis fila, mundifica illud, et restaura uulnus, donec consolidetur.	So when you cut the threads, clean it, and restore the wound until it is healed.
Sisach enim contrahitur, et non additur eminentia Rupturae.	For the membrane contracts, and the protrusion of the rupture does not increase.
Et cauterium est melius in hoc loco: quoniam est propinquius ad salutem.	And cautery is better in this location because it is closer to healing.
¶ De mollificatione cutis testiculorum.	On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
Caput LXVIII.	Chapter 68.
Multotiens mollificatur cutis testiculorum in quibusdam hominibus, propter quod mollificantur carnes quae sunt inter ea, et foedatur aspectus eius.	Often the skin of the testicles becomes softened in some men, whereby the flesh between them is softened, and its appearance is disfigured.
Ergo necesse est ei qui rogatur in curatione eius, ut faciat iacere infirmum super dorsum suum, et incidat totam cutem quae mollificata est super cutem naturalem.	Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked to treat it, to have the patient lie on his back, and to cut all the softened skin above the natural skin.
Deinde aggreget duo labia cum sutura: et si uis, sue in primis superfluitatem cutis mollificatae tribus suturis, aut quatuor, et firma suturam.	Then join the two edges with suturing: and if you wish, sew the excess of the softened skin at first with three or four stitches, and secure the suture.
Deinde incide inter sututuras.	Then cut between the sutures.
Deinde cura curatione reliquorum uulnerum, usquequo sanetur, et cadant fila.	Then treat it with the care for other wounds, until it is healed and the threads fall out.
¶ De Castratione.	On Castration.
Caput LXIX.	Chapter 69.
Scias, quod Castratio in lege nostra excommunicata est: et propter illud liceret mihi, ut non rememorarer eius in libro meo isto: et non est necessaria rememoratio eius, nisi propter duos modos.	Know that castration is condemned in our law: and because of that, it would be permissible for me to not mention it in this book of mine: and mentioning it is not necessary, except for two reasons.
Quorum unus est, ut sit illud in scientia medici quando interrogatur de ea: et ut sciat curationem eius cui accidit.	One of which is so that it is in the knowledge of the physician when he is asked about it: and so that he knows the treatment of one to whom it happens.
Et modus alter est, quod nos multotiens indigemus castratione quorundam animalium, propter iuuamenta nostra per illud, sicut arietum, hyrcorum, et gattorum, et similium ex animalibus.	And the other reason is that we often need to castrate certain animals for our benefit through it, such as rams, goats, cats, and similar animals.
Dico ergo, quod Castratio fit secundum duos modos.	I say, therefore, that castration is done in two ways.
Aut per attritionem.	Either by rubbing.
Aut per fissuram, et sectionem.	Or by splitting and cutting.
In illa autem quae fit per attritionem, uia operationis est: quod nos faciamus sedere animal in aqua calida, donec mollificentur testiculi eius, et leniantur, et pendeant: deinde attere eos manu tua, donec resoluantur et non appareant sub tactu.	In that which is done by rubbing, the method of operation is: that we make the animal sit in warm water, until its testicles are softened, relaxed, and hang down: then rub them with your hand, until they are dissolved and do not appear under touch.
In castratione autem per fissuram et sectionem, oportet ut teneas animal, et premas cutem testiculorum eius cum manu sinistra.	In castration by splitting and cutting, however, it is necessary to restrain the animal, and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Deinde liga suspensorium, et seca super omne ouum sectione una, donec quando procedunt duo oua: tunc incide ea postquam excoriaueris utrumque, et non dimittas super ea ex sifaket aliquid praeter sifac subtile, quod est super uasa.	Then tie a suspensory band, and make one cut over each testicle until both testicles come out: then cut them after you have stripped each one, and leave nothing from the membrane except the thin layer, which is above the vessels.
Et iste modus castrationis est melior eo qui fit per attritonem: quoniam attritio fortasse relinquit aliquid ex testiculis, quare desiderat animal coitum.	And this method of castration is better than the one done by rubbing: because rubbing may perhaps leave something of the testicles, which causes the animal to desire mating.
Deinde cura uulnus, donec sanetur.	Then treat the wound until it is healed.
¶ De cura Hermafroditae duorum modorum.	On the treatment of two types of hermaphroditism.
Caput LXX.	Chapter 70.
Hermafrodita ex uiris est secundum duos modos.	Hermaphroditism among males occurs in two forms.
Vnus eorum est, quia apparet in eo quod sequitur spacium, aut in cute testiculorum, in eo quod est inter duos testiculos, figura quasi uulua mulieris, in qua sunt pili: et quandoque currit urina ex eo quod est in cute testiculorum.	One form appears as a space or in the skin of the testicles, between the two testicles, resembling the shape of a woman’s vulva, with hair present; and sometimes urine flows from the area in the skin of the testicles.
In mulieribus autem est species una, et est uulua mulieris super pectinem sicut testiculi uiri parui omnino, eminentes ad exteriora: quorum unus est sicut priapus uiri, et duo sicut duo testiculi.	In women, there is one form where the vulva is located on the pubic area, resembling the small testicles of a male, slightly protruding outward: one part resembles a male penis, and two parts resemble two testicles.
Et curatio trium specierum, duarum ex uiris, et speciei unius ex mulieribus, est: quia oportet ut incidas carnes additas, donec effugiat impressio earum.	The treatment for these three types—two forms in males and one form in females—is to cut away the excess flesh until its impression disappears.
Deinde cura eas curatione reliquorum uulnerum.	Then, treat them with the usual wound care until healed.
In specie autem secunda uirorum, ex qua egreditur urina, quae est in cute testiculorum, non est operatio, neque est eius curatio omnino.	For the second type in men, where urine flows from the skin of the testicles, there is no operation or treatment whatsoever.
¶ De incisione Tentiginis, et carnis eminentis in uuluis mulierum.	On the excision of swelling and protruding flesh in the vulvas of women.
Caput LXXI.	Chapter 71.
Tentigo fortasse additur super rem naturalem, donec foedatur et turpis fit aspectus eius: et quandoque magnificatur in quibusdam mulieribus adeo, donec expanditur sicut in uiris, et peruenit usque ad coitum.	Swelling sometimes enlarges beyond the natural state, becoming disfigured and unsightly; in some women, it may grow to the extent that it expands like a male organ and becomes capable of sexual intercourse.
Oportet ergo ut teneas superfluitatem Tentiginis manu, aut cum uncino, et incidas: et non ultimes in incisione, praecipue in profundo radicis: ut non accidat fluxus sanguinis.	Therefore, you should hold the excessive swelling with your hand or with a hook and cut it away; however, do not go too deep with the incision, especially at the base, to avoid bleeding.
Deinde cura ipsam curatione uulnerum, donec sanetur.	Then treat the area with regular wound care until it heals.
Caro autem orta, est caro quae nascitur in orificio matricis, donec impleat ipsum: et fortasse egreditur ad exteriora secundum similitudinem caudae: et propter illud quidam primi nominant aegritudinem caudatam.	Overgrown flesh may grow within the opening of the uterus until it fills the space; it may even protrude outward in a tail-like manner. Because of this, some early scholars called this ailment "caudate illness."
Oportet ergo ut incidamus eam sicut incidimus Tentiginem, et curemus eam, donec sanetur.	Thus, we should excise it as we do for swelling, and treat it until it is healed.
¶ De cura Alratica, quae est uulua mulieris non perforata.	On the treatment of Alratica, the condition of an imperforate vulva in women.
Caput LXXII.	Chapter 72.
Alratica est, ut sit uulua mulieris non perforata, aut sit foramen paruum.	Alratica is a condition where a woman’s vulva is either imperforate or has a very small opening.
Et est aut naturalis, aut accidentalis.	It is either congenital or acquired.
Accidentalis est ex aegritudine quae praecessit: et ipsa quidem fit aut ex carne nata addita, aut sifach subtili, aut spisso: et fit aut in profundo matricis, aut in lateribus eius, aut in superiore ipsius, aut inferiori eius: et prohibet a coitu et impregnatione, et partu, et fortasse prohibet menstrua.	The acquired form results from a previous ailment and may occur due to excess flesh growth or a membrane that is thin or thick; it may occur deep within the womb, on its sides, at its upper part, or lower part, and it obstructs intercourse, impregnation, and childbirth, and sometimes even menstruation.
Et cognitio illius fit per aspectum obstetricis, si opilatio est apparens propinqua.	Diagnosis is made by a midwife’s examination if the obstruction is visible and close.
Si autem non est apparens, tunc quaere eam digitis tuis, aut cum radio.	If it is not visible, then seek it out with your fingers or with a probe.
Si autem opilatio est ex sifach subtili, et est propinqua duobus labiis: tunc propera, et disrumpe ipsam.	If the obstruction is due to a thin membrane and is close to the labia, then proceed quickly and rupture it.
Et est, ut ponas super duo labia puluillos.	This is done by placing small cushions on both labia.
Deinde pone indices tuos duarum manuum simul, et mulier sit super dorsum suum expansis cruribus suis.	Then place the index fingers of both hands together, while the woman lies on her back with her legs spread.
Deinde extende duo labia cum fortitudine, donec disrumpatur sifach subtile, et aperiatur opilatio.	Then extend the two labia firmly until the thin membrane is ruptured and the obstruction is opened.
Deinde accipe lanam, et imbibe eam in oleo, et pone ipsam super locum: et coeat mulier omni die, ut non consolidetur locus uice alia.	Next, take some wool, soak it in oil, and place it on the area; let the woman have intercourse daily to prevent the site from sealing again.
Si autem sifach est grossum, spissum: tunc oportet ut seces ipsum cum spatumili lato simili folio myrti.	If the membrane is thick and dense, then you must cut it with a broad spatula shaped like a myrtle leaf.
Si autem opilatio est ex carne nata, tunc suspende eam cum uncinis, et incide eam: et sint tecum medicinae quae fluxum sedant sanguinis absque mordicatione, sicut acacia, et sanguis draconis, et thus aggregatum cum albugine oui.	If the obstruction is due to excess flesh growth, suspend it with hooks and cut it away, and have on hand medicines that stop bleeding without causing irritation, such as acacia, dragon’s blood, and frankincense mixed with egg white.
Deinde administra cannulam ex plumbo amplam, ut non consolidetur uulnus uelociter, teneat eam diebus aliquot: et administra licinium ex lino sicco, deinde curetur reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	Then insert a broad lead tube to prevent the wound from closing too quickly, leaving it in place for a few days; apply a wick made from dry linen, then proceed with usual wound care until it heals.
Et quandoque nasciur in matrice natiuitas carnium aliarum: oportet ergo ut incidantur secundum hunc modum: dum non est apostema cancerosum apostemati enim canceroso quod est in matrice, non fiat contrarietas cum ferro omnino.	Sometimes, new flesh growths arise in the womb. These must be excised as described here, provided there is no cancerous abscess; for a cancerous abscess in the womb, surgery with iron should not be performed at all.
¶ De cura hemorroidarum, Athehelil, et Bothor rubeae in uuluis mulierum.	On the treatment of hemorrhoids, athehelil, and red bothor in the vulvae of women.
Caput LXXIII.	Chapter 73.
Hemorroides quidem sunt apertio orificiorum uenarum, donec currit ex eis sanguis multus assidue.	Hemorrhoids are indeed the opening of the orifices of veins, until much blood flows continually from them.
Cum ergo antiquantur hemorroides, fiunt thelil: et iam dixi in diuisione species earum, et signa ipsarum: et dicam hic quae ex eis recipiunt curationem, et quae non.	When hemorrhoids persist, they become thelil; and I have already explained the types of these, and their signs; and I will say here which of them receive treatment, and which do not.
Dico ergo, quod hemorroides quae sunt in orificio matricis, et non apparent sensui: tunc non est ei curatio cum ferro.	Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids that are in the orifice of the uterus and are not apparent to the senses: then they are not treated with a surgical instrument.
Quae autem ex eis sunt in orificio matricis super quas cadit sensus, sunt quae curantur.	However, those that are in the orifice of the uterus and are perceived by touch are the ones that are treated.
Oportet ergo ut intromittas mulierem in domum frigidam.	Therefore, it is necessary to place the woman in a cool room.
Deinde extende athehelil cum forficibus, aut cum panno aspero, et incide eas ex radicibus suis.	Then stretch out the athehelil with scissors, or with a rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Deinde pulueriza super eas apud fluxum sanguinis ex uno puluerum incisiuorum absque mordificatione: sicut acacia, et sanguis draconis, et thus, et similia eis.	Then sprinkle over them, where the blood flows, some powders of incision that do not cause stinging: such as acacia, dragon’s blood, frankincense, and similar substances.
Deinde impellat pedes eius ad parietem hora una.	Then have her press her feet against the wall for one hour.
Postea depone eam in aquam frigidam.	Afterwards, place her in cold water.
