Quod si perseuerat fluxus sanguinis: tunc fac eam sedere in decoctione sumach, et corticum granatorum, et gallarum, et similium.	If the blood flow persists, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, galls, and similar ingredients.
Deinde accipe farinam hordei, et confice eam cum melle et aceto, et fac emplastrum cum eo super dorsum eius.	Then take barley flour, mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it to place on her back.
Si ergo abscinditur sanguis cum eo, bonum est: et si non, fac adhaerere dorso uentosas, et mammillis, absque scarificatione.	If the bleeding stops with this, it is good; if not, apply suction cups to her back and breasts, without cutting the skin.
Deinde accipe lanam, et submerge in succo tarathit, aut succo arnoglossae, aut succo ramorum alaulat, id est, aglanter, uino pontico, et fac adhaerere loeo.	Then take wool, and soak it in the juice of tarathit, or the juice of plantain, or the juice of alaulat branches, that is, wild rose, with Pontic wine, and apply it to the area.
Cum ergo quiescit apostema, tunc cura locum cum unguentis, donec sanetur.	When the swelling subsides, then treat the area with ointments until it heals.
Albarth uero rubeum est simile capitibus alhaasse, et est asperi aspectus.	The red albarth is similar to the heads of alhaasse and has a rough appearance.
Oportet ergo ut incidas quod apparet ex eo, secundum quod dixi in thelil aequaliter: et cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	Therefore, it is necessary to cut away what appears of it, as I have explained with the thelil, and treat it until it heals.
¶ De perforatione Exiturae quae accidit in matrice.	On perforation of an ulcer occurring in the uterus.
Caput LXXIIII.	Chapter 74.
Accidunt in matrice species multae apostematum, sicut cancer, et apostema lapideum, et ulcera, et adubelati, et alekilati, id est, herpes, aestiomemus, et fistulae, et hemorroides, et ragadiae, et thelil, et apostema calidum.	Many types of swellings occur in the uterus, such as cancer, stone-like swellings, ulcers, adubelati, alekilati, that is, herpes, aestiomemus, fistulas, hemorrhoids, fissures, thelil, and hot swellings.
Et ego quidem iam dixi omnes has aegritudines et species earum, et signa ipsarum, et earum curationes in diuisione: necesse est ut dicam in hoc tractatu apostema calidum quod accidit in matrice, quando est ex apostematibus quae colligunt saniem, et uis scire qualiter fit eius apertio cum ferro.	And indeed, I have already discussed all these afflictions, their types, their signs, and their treatments in the division; but it is necessary in this treatise to speak of the hot swelling that occurs in the uterus, when it is one of the swellings that collects pus, and you want to know how its opening is made with a surgical instrument.
Oportet ergo ut consideres.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to observe.
Tunc si dolor apostematis in incaeptione sua est acutus cum percussione sua, et flamma, et febre: et uides ipsum rubere: si cadit super ipsum sensus, tunc non properes cum perforatione eius: et cura ipsum cum eo eo quod iuuat super maturationem, donec quando quiescat acuitas accidentium.	Then, if the pain of the swelling is sharp at its beginning, with throbbing, heat, and fever, and you see it redden, and if it is sensitive to the touch, then do not rush to perforate it; treat it with what helps bring it to maturation until the sharpness of the symptoms subsides.
Tunc oportet ut facias sedere mulierem super sedem quae labeat duo sedilia, et reclinetur, uel appodietur super dorsum suum, et aggreget pedes suos ad partem inferiorem uentris: et sint coxae eius expansae, et ponat brachia sua sub genibus suis, et liget utraque ligamento conueniente ad illud.	Then it is necessary to make the woman sit on a seat with two benches, and have her lean back or support herself on her back, bringing her feet toward the lower part of her abdomen; her hips should be spread, her arms placed under her knees, and each tied with a suitable binding for this.
Deinde sedeat obstetrix a latere dextro, et administra instrumentum quo aperitur orificium matricis.	Then the midwife sits on her right side and uses the instrument that opens the orifice of the uterus.
Cuius forma uenit in eis quae sunt post.	The form of this instrument is shown in the following illustrations.
Et oportet quando uis administrare hoc instrumentum, ut figas cum Radio profundum matricis mulieris: ut non sit illud quod ingreditur ex instrumento plus, quam profundum matricis, et laedat infirmam.	And when you wish to use this instrument, you must affix the end of the probe in the depth of the woman’s uterus, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than the depth of the uterus and harm the patient.
Si autem fuerit instrumentum magis quam profundum, tunc oportet ut ponas puluillos super tecturam profundi matricis: ut prohibeatur introitus instrumenti totius in profundum matricis: et oportet ut ponat uertiginem, quae currit in instrumento, ex latere superiore: et ut teneat instrumentum, et ut reuoluat minister uertiginem, donec aperiatur profundum matricis.	If, however, the instrument is longer than necessary, you must place cushions over the covering of the depth of the uterus, to prevent the instrument from entering fully into the depth of the uterus; and the turning screw, which runs in the instrument, should be on the upper side, so the assistant holds the instrument and turns the screw until the depth of the uterus is opened.
Cum ergo apparet Exitura, et tangitur manu, et est lenis et mollis: tunc oportet ut seces ipsam apud caput suum cum spatumili lato.	When the ulcer appears, can be touched by hand, and is smooth and soft, it is necessary to cut it at its head with a broad spatula.
Cum ergo euacuatur sanies, tunc oportet ut ponas in uulnus licinium submersum in oleo rosaceo: aut oleo uiridi, in quo sit quaedam stipticitas: et pone licinium, et extrahe sectionem in profundo matricis.	When the pus is thus evacuated, you must place in the wound a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or green oil with a certain astringency; place the linen cloth and draw the section into the depth of the uterus.
Et pone exterius super matricem, et super pectinem lanam mundam submersam in aqua, in qua bullitae sunt maluae.	Then place on the outside over the uterus and pubic area clean wool soaked in water in which mallows have been boiled.
Deinde curetur post duos dies cum unguento quod conuenit ad illud, donec sanetur.	Then, after two days, treat it with an ointment suited to this purpose, until it heals.
Et quandoque abluitur matrix et uulnus, ita quod clisterizatur cum aqua et melle: deinde cum aqua in qua bullita est radix lilii, aut aristolochia longa: deinde redeat ad unguentum.	And at times the uterus and the wound are washed, so that it is rinsed with water and honey; then with water in which lily root or long aristolochia has been boiled; then return to using the ointment.
Quod si uulnus absconditum fuerit interius in matrice, tunc oportet ut prohibearis ex curatione eius cum ferro, imo cura ipsum cum eo quod diximus in diuisione.	If the wound is hidden within the uterus, then you must refrain from treating it with an instrument; rather, treat it with what we have discussed in the division.
¶ Doctrinae Obstetricum, qualiter medicentur embriones uiui, secundum figuram non naturalem egressi.	Teachings for Midwives, on how to treat live embryos, when they emerge in an unnatural position.
Caput Lxxu.	Chapter 75.
Necesse est Obstetrici, ut cognoscat in primis figuram partus naturalis.	It is necessary for the midwife first to know the form of natural birth.
Ex signis ergo eius est, quod quando uides mulierem comprimi ad inferiora, et desiderat odorare aerem, et alleuiatur super eam quod super ipsam est de partu, et festinat exitus embrionis: tunc scias quod iste partus est secundum figuram naturalem, et est exitus eius super caput suum, et secundina cum eo: aut suspensa, uel pendens ex umbilico.	Among the signs of this is that when you see the woman bearing down, and she desires to smell fresh air, and the pressure from labor lessens over her, and the embryo's exit hastens, then you know that this birth is according to the natural form, and its exit is head-first with the afterbirth, either attached or hanging from the umbilical cord.
Cum ergo uides haec signa, tunc oportet ut comprimatur uenter eius, ut descendat embrio uelociter.	When you see these signs, it is then necessary to press on her abdomen so that the embryo descends quickly.
Nam quando descendit super caput suum, descendit secundina cum eo, et mundatur ex illis superfluitatibus mundificatione bona.	For when it descends head-first, the afterbirth descends with it, and it is cleansed of these impurities with good purification.
Qui autem est praeter hunc partum, est innaturalis, illaudabilis.	But any other birth than this is unnatural and unfavorable.
Quoniam quandoque egreditur foetus super pedes suos, et egreditur corpus eius ante caput ipsius, et pedes eius, et manus eius una, aut pes eius unus: aut egreditur caput eius et manus eius: aut egreditur uentrinus: et fortasse conuertitur super collum suum, et similia ex figuris illaudabilibus.	For sometimes the fetus emerges feet-first, or its body exits before its head, with one foot or hand, or one foot alone; or its head and hand emerge; or its abdomen appears; and perhaps it turns on its neck, and other such unfavorable presentations.
Necesse est ergo Obstetrici, ut sit prudens, subtilis in istis rebus omnibus, et caueat sibi ab errore et decaeptione: et ego sum ostendens omnem figuram ex eis, et qualiter est ingenium in ea, et significetur per illud, et stetur super ipsum.	Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise, precise in all these matters, and cautious of error and deception; and I am showing every one of these forms and how to manage each, and it shall be explained and demonstrated.
Quando egreditur foetus super caput suum egressione sua naturali, et uehemens fit illud super mulierem, et difficilis fit ei partus, et uides uirtutem eius iam debilitatam: tunc fac eam sedere super sedem, aut mulieres teneant eam: et uapora uuluam eius cum foenugraeco decocto, et cum oleis humidis.	When the fetus emerges head-first in its natural exit, and this becomes intense for the woman, and the birth becomes difficult for her, and you see her strength already weakened: then have her sit on a seat, or have other women hold her, and steam her vulva with a fenugreek decoction and moist oils.
Deinde intromittat Obstetrix inter digitos suos Spatumile paruum, et findat cum eo secundinam, et secet eam ungue suo, donec currat quod est in ea ex humiditate: et preme uentrem mulieris, donec descendat foetus.	Then let the midwife insert between her fingers a small spatula and split the afterbirth with it, cutting it with her fingernail until the moisture contained within flows out; and press the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.
Si autem non descendit, tunc oportet ut clisterizetur mulier ex mucillagine foenugraeci, cum oleo sisamino.	If it does not descend, then the woman must be given an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil.
Deinde praecipe ei post clistere, ut comprimatur: et fac eam sternutare cum condisi, et tene os eius et nasum ipsius hora una.	Then instruct her after the enema to bear down; and make her sneeze with condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour.
Foetus enim egredietur statim.	The fetus will then emerge immediately.
Quod si egrediantur duae manus foetus in primis, iunc oportet ut reducas eas cum facilitate paulatim.	But if the two hands of the fetus emerge first, then it is necessary to gently and gradually push them back.
Si autem non obedit in introitu, tunc pone mulierem super sedem, et eleua pedes eius sursum: deinde concute sedem super terram: et mulier teneatur, ut non cadat apud concussionem.	If it does not go back easily, then place the woman on a seat and lift her feet upwards; then shake the seat over the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the shaking.
Si ergo non egrediuntur manus, et moritur foetus: tunc incide eas, et extrahe residuum foetus: et liga manum eius cum panno, et extrahe ipsum cum aequalitate: nam ipse egredietur.	If, however, the hands do not come out and the fetus dies, then cut them off and extract the rest of the fetus; bind its hand with cloth and draw it out steadily, and it will emerge.
### Exitus Embrionis Super Pedes Suos	_When the fetus emerges feet-first_
Quando egreditur foetus super pedes suos, tunc oportet ut impellat eos sursum: deinde conuertat foetum paulatim: postea aequet ipsum.	When the fetus emerges feet-first, it is necessary to push the feet upward, then gradually turn the fetus, and then adjust its position.
Deinde accipiat unum pedum eius, et extendat eum paulatim.	Then take one of its feet and extend it gradually.
Cum ergo egrediuntur usque ad coxas, tunc praecipe ei, ut comprimatur, et fac eam sternutare cum condisi: egredietur enim, si Deus uoluerit.	When the fetus emerges up to the hips, instruct the woman to bear down, and make her sneeze with a condiment; then the fetus will emerge, God willing.
Et si non egreditur cum eo quod narrauimus, tunc reduc foetum paulatim, donec ponas eum secundum figuram naturalem.	If the fetus does not emerge with this approach, then gradually push it back until it is in the natural position.
Nam ipse egredietur tunc egressu facili.	Then it will emerge easily.
Quod si prohibeatur cum eo toto quod narrauimus: tunc accipe ex mucillagine alteae, et oleo sisamino, et gummi soluto: et percute totum in mortario percussione bona: deinde line cum eo uuluam mulieris, et inferius uentris eius.	But if it is still prevented from emerging with all that we have described, then take marshmallow mucilage, sesame oil, and dissolved gum; pound everything thoroughly in a mortar, then apply it to the woman’s vulva and lower abdomen.
Deinde fac eam sedere in aqua tepida, donec consequatur hypocundria.	Next, have her sit in warm water until her lower abdomen relaxes.
Cum ergo uides quod iam calefacta sunt inferiora eius, tunc fac ei sief de myrrha: et suppone ipsum.	When you see that her lower parts are now warmed, then prepare a suppository of myrrh and place it.
Quando ergo tenet sief hora una, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem.	When she has held the suppository for an hour, then have her sit on a seat.
Deinde fac eam sternutare: et stringe ipsius os et nasum: et preme inferiorem partem uentris compressione facili.	Next, make her sneeze, and gently press her mouth and nose, and apply gentle pressure on her lower abdomen.
Nam foetus egredietur statim.	The fetus will then emerge immediately.
### Exitus Foetus Super Genua et Manus	_When the fetus emerges on its knees and hands_
Quando egreditur secundum hanc formam, tunc ingeniet in intromittendo manus suas paulatim.	When the fetus emerges in this way, she must carefully insert her hands gradually.
Deinde resupinetur mulier super collum suum, et pendeant pedes eius ad inferiora: et ipsa sit iacens super lectum, et complicet manus suas.	Then the woman should be laid back on her neck, with her legs hanging down, lying on the bed with her hands folded.
Deinde preme supra uentrem eius paulatim.	Then gently press on her abdomen.
Deinde extrahe quod est sub pedibus eius ex puluinaribus, donec sit praeparata in inferiori parte.	Then remove what is beneath her feet from the cushions, so that she is prepared at the lower part.
Quod si non egreditur foetus, tunc accipe pedes eius, et moue eos motu uehementi.	If the fetus does not emerge, take its feet and shake them with firm motion.
Deinde preme quod est supra hypocundria paulatim, donec ascendat foetus ad superiora.	Next, press gradually above the lower abdomen until the fetus moves upward.
Deinde intromittat manus suas, et aequet foetum paulatim: et praecipe mulieri, ut comprimatur, donec egrediatur foetus.	Then insert her hands, gradually aligning the fetus, and instruct the woman to bear down until the fetus emerges.
### Exitus Foetus Latitudinaliter Pendens Ex Manibus	_When the fetus is hanging laterally by its arms_
Ingenietur in reductione manus eius.	Carefully attempt to reposition its hand.
Si autem non potest reducere eam, tunc eleua mulierem, et fac eam ambulare.	If this is not possible, then lift the woman and have her walk.
Si uero ambulare non potest, tunc fac eam iacere super lectum: et concute crura eius concussione uehementi.	If she cannot walk, then lay her on the bed and shake her legs firmly.
Deinde administra linimentum quod praeparasti ex mucillaginibus.	Next, apply the liniment prepared from mucilage.
Quod si accipit eam partus, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem.	If labor seizes her, then have her sit on a seat.
Deinde stude in reductione manus, et aequa foetum secundum figuram naturalem: et fac sternutare mulierem, et praecipe ei, ut comprimat se, donec egrediatur.	Then work on repositioning its hand and align the fetus in the natural position, and make the woman sneeze, instructing her to bear down until the fetus emerges.
### Exitus Foetus Super Collum Suum, Expansis Manibus, et Est Facies Eius ad Dorsum Matris Suae	_When the fetus emerges head-down, with arms extended, and its face toward the mother's back_
Oportet ut teneat Obstetrix manum foetus, deinde reuoluat eum paulatim, et aequet eum cum facilitate.	The midwife must hold the fetus’s hand, then turn it gently and adjust it with ease.
Cum ergo aequatur, tunc pone super uuluam eius quod narrauimus ex oleo et mucillaginibus.	When it is properly aligned, then apply the mixture of oil and mucilage on her vulva as we described.
Deinde praecipe ei, ut moueatur paulatim.	Then instruct her to move gradually.
Cum ergo feceris illud, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem, et praecipe ei ut inclinetur ad latus dextrum.	When you have done this, have her sit on a seat and instruct her to lean to her right side.
Deinde praecipe ei, ut comprimatur: et fac eam sternutare cum condisi.	Then instruct her to bear down and make her sneeze with condiments.
### Exitus Foetus Praeparati Super Latus	_When the fetus is positioned sideways_
Quando descendit ad orificium matricis secundum hunc modum cum secundina, tunc scinde secundinam cum ungue tuo, donec euacuetur ex humiditate.	When the fetus descends to the mouth of the uterus in this manner with the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your fingernail until the moisture is released.
Si ergo suspenditur super faciem foetus, et collum eius, tunc incide eam ex umbilico: ut non retineatur, et moriatur.	If it then hangs over the face and neck of the fetus, cut it from the umbilical cord, so it does not hold it back and cause death.
Deinde impelle foetum ad interiora, donec ponas eum secundum quod oportet: et praecipe mulieri, ut comprimat se aliquotiens: ipse enim egredietur exitu leui.	Then push the fetus back inward until it is in the appropriate position, and instruct the woman to bear down several times; then it will emerge with ease.
¶ Exitus Geminorum, aut foetuum multorum.	The exit of twins, or of many fetuses.
Scias, quod Gemini multotiens nascuntur: et quandoque nascuntur tres, et quatuor.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born.
Verumtamen illud extraneum est, et raro contingit.	However, that is unusual and rarely happens.
Quinque uero est res extra naturam, et non uiuunt penitus: et continet eos, quamuis multiplicentur, secundina una: et separantur per sifach, distinguens inter eos ligatum in umbilico cuiusque eorum.	But five is something unnatural, and they do not survive at all; even if they are multiple, they are contained in one membrane, and are separated by a membrane, distinguishing between them a ligament in each of their umbilici.
Et quandoque egrediuntur sicut egreditur foetus unus exitu naturali, facili: et egrediuntur exitu illaudabili, sicut narrauimus.	And sometimes they emerge as one fetus does, with a natural, easy exit; and they emerge with a difficult exit, as we have described.
Quod si difficiles fuerint quidam eorum apud partum, et perueniunt ad illud quod diximus ex figuris innaturalibus, tunc cura eos sicut narrauimus: et sit ob stetrix subtilis, et faciat quod facit cum facilitate et tarditate, et ingenietur secundum omnem figuram cum eo quod praeparatur ei ex ingenio ducente ad salutem.	But if any of them are difficult at birth, and they come to the situation we mentioned with unnatural positions, then care for them as we have described, and let the midwife be skillful, and let her act with ease and patience, and use her ingenuity in every position with what is prepared for her, guided toward safety.
¶ Rememoratio eius quod formatur in matrice ex embrionibus, et abortiuntur.	Recollection of what is formed in the womb from embryos, and is aborted.
Quandoque formatur in matrice unus, et duo, et tres, et quatuor, et quinque, et sex, et septem, et plures decem: et iam uerificatum est apud me, quod mulier abortiendo emisit septem, et alia quindecim, omnes formatos.	Sometimes one is formed in the womb, or two, or three, or four, or five, or six, or seven, or more, up to ten; and it has been verified by me that a woman in aborting expelled seven, and another fifteen, all fully formed.
Quod factum est mensuratione gloriosi sapientis.	Which was accomplished by the measurement of a glorious sage.
Hoc ergo totum oportet ut sit in scientia Obstetricis.	Therefore, all this must be in the knowledge of the midwife.
Fortasse enim perueniet ad eam simile illius: opponat ergo ei cum illo quod oportet.	For perhaps something similar to that may come to her; let her, therefore, apply to it whatever is necessary.
¶ De extractione foetus mortui.	On the extraction of a dead fetus.
Caput LXXVI.	Chapter 76.
Quando curas foetum mortuum cum eo quod dixi in diuisione ex medicatione, et non egreditur, et cogeris uti operatione cum manu, tunc oportet ut consideres.	When you treat a dead fetus with what I have discussed in the section on medication, and it does not emerge, and you are forced to use manual intervention, then you must consider.
Si ergo mulier est sanae uirtutis, et non est cum aliquo ex accidentibus, ex quibus timetur super eam perditio: tunc oportet ut resupinetur mulier super lectum, super dorsum suum, et sit caput eius inclinatum inferius, et crura eius eleuata: et ministra teneat eam a duabus partibus, aut ligetur ad lectum, ut non extrahatur corpus eius apud extractionem foetus.	If the woman is of sound strength and does not have any conditions that would threaten her life, then the woman should be laid on her back on a bed, with her head inclined downward and her legs elevated; an assistant should hold her from both sides, or she should be bound to the bed, so that her body is not pulled during the fetus's extraction.
Deinde humecta os matricis ex oleis humidis cum mucillagine alteae, et foenugraeci, et seminis lini.	Then moisten the mouth of the uterus with softening oils made with the mucilage of mallow, fenugreek, and flaxseed.
Deinde inungat Obstetrix manum suam cum istis oleis et mucillaginibus: deinde intromittat eam in matricem cum facilitate.	Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and mucilages, and then insert it into the uterus gently.
Deinde quaerat cum ea locum in quo figat uncinos ex foetu, et loca conuenientia ad illud.	Then she should look with her hand for a place where she can secure hooks into the fetus, and find suitable locations for this.
Considera ergo tunc, si foetus est praeparatus ut descendat super caput suum: tunc fige uncinos in oculos eius, aut in collo eius, aut in ore eius, aut in palato ipsius, aut sub barba eius, aut in furcula ipsius, aut in locis propinquis costis, et sub hypocundriis.	Therefore, if the fetus is positioned to descend head first, then place the hooks in its eyes, or its neck, or its mouth, or its palate, or under its chin, or its breastbone, or in locations near the ribs and under the hypochondria.
Si autem descensus est super pedes eius, tunc in pectine, et costis eius mediis.	If, however, it descends feet first, then in its groin and middle ribs.
Et oportet, ut teneat uncinum cum manu dextra: et ponat curuitatem eius in eo quod est inter digitos sinistrae manus: et intromittat cum manu cum facilitate, et figat uncinum in aliquo illorum locorum quae diximus, donec perueniat ad rem uacuam.	She should hold the hook with her right hand and place its curve between the fingers of her left hand; then insert it with ease and secure the hook in one of those locations mentioned, until she reaches an empty space.
Deinde figat in oppositione eius uncinum alium, aut tertium, si indiges: ut sit contractio aequalis, et non declinet ad partem.	Then she should fix another hook opposite it, or a third if needed, so that the pull is even and does not lean to one side.
Deinde extendatur extensione aequali, et non sit extensio secundum rectitudinem tantum, imo moueatur ad omnem partem, ut alleuietur exitus eius: sicut fit cum dente apud eradicationem eius.	Then pull with equal force, not only in a straight line, but move it in all directions, to ease its exit, as is done with a tooth during extraction.
Et oportet in eo quod est inter illud, ut mollificetur extensio.	And it is necessary that, in between these actions, the extension is softened.
Quod si retineatur ex eo pars, tunc oportet ut inungat Obstetrix quosdam digitos cum oleo, et intromittat eos ex parte, ut reuoluat cum eis quod retinetur.	If a part is held back, then the midwife should anoint some of her fingers with oil and insert them from the side, to rotate what is being held.
Si ergo egreditur pars foetus, tunc permutentur uncini ad locum alium qui sit altior: fac hoc donec egrediatur foetus totus.	If a part of the fetus emerges, then shift the hooks to a higher location; do this until the entire fetus exits.
Si ergo egreditur manus ante alia, et non est possibile reducere eam, propter coartationem eius: tunc oportet, ut inuoluatur super eam pannus.	If a hand emerges before the others, and it is impossible to push it back due to its restriction, then it should be wrapped in a cloth.
Deinde extrahe eam donec quando egreditur tota, incide eam aut in iunctura plantae, aut in cubito: et ita oportet ut facias in manu altera, et in duobus pedibus.	Then pull it until it fully exits, and cut it either at the wrist or elbow; do likewise with the other hand and both feet.
Si autem caput foetus est magnum, aut accidit ei coartatio in exitu, aut est in capite eius aqua aggregata: tunc oportet ut intromittat inter digitos Spatumile spinosum, et findat cum eo caput, et extrahat aquam: aut disrumpat ipsum cum instrumento quod nominatur Almisdac: cuius forma uenit cum formis reliquorum instrumentorum in capitulo quod est post hoc.	If, however, the fetus's head is large, or it is restricted in the exit, or there is fluid accumulated in its head, then it is necessary to insert between the fingers a thorny spatumile, and split the head with it to extract the fluid, or rupture it with an instrument called an Almisdac, the form of which appears with the other instrument forms in the chapter after this one.
Similiter faciat si foetus est magni capitis natura, tunc oportet ut seces algengematu: aut extrahas ipsum cum misdach, sicut diximus.	Similarly, if the fetus has a naturally large head, then it is necessary to cut it with the algengematu or extract it with the misdach, as we have described.
Deinde attrahas ossa cum forcipibus.	Then pull out the bones with forceps.
Quod si egrediatur caput, et coartetur apud furculam: tunc findatur, donec effundatur humiditas quae est in pectore.	If the head emerges but becomes restricted at the breastbone, then it should be split until the moisture in the chest is released.
Si autem non complicatur, neque obedit ad exitum: tunc incide caput frustatim, secundum quod possibile est tibi.	If it does not fold or permit exit, then cut the head into pieces as much as is possible for you.
Quod si inferius uentris est apostematum, aut est in eo hydropisis: tunc oportet ut perfores ipsum, donec currat humiditas ex eo.	If there is an abscess in the lower abdomen, or if there is dropsy in it, then it is necessary to pierce it until the fluid flows out.
Si uero foetus est super pedes suos, tunc attractio eius est facilis, et directio eius ad os matricis est leuis.	If the fetus is on its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its direction toward the mouth of the uterus is smooth.
Si autem coartatur apud uentrem, aut pectus: tunc oportet ut extrahas ipsum cum panno quem inuoluisti super manum tuam: et findat uentrem, aut pectus, donec currat quod est in eis.	If it becomes restricted at the abdomen or chest, then it is necessary to extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand, and split the abdomen or chest until the contents flow out.
Si autem auferuntur reliqua membra, et redit caput: tunc intromittat Obstetrix manum sinistram.	If the other limbs have been removed and the head remains, then the midwife should insert her left hand.
Si ergo os matricis est apertum, tunc intromittat manum in profundum matricis, et quaerat cum ea caput, et attrahat ipsum cum digitis usque ad os matricis: deinde intromittat in eo uncinum unum, aut uncinos duos, et attrahat ipsum cum eo.	If the mouth of the uterus is open, then she should insert her hand deep into the uterus, search for the head with it, and draw it toward the mouth of the uterus with her fingers; then insert one hook or two into it and pull it out with them.
Quod si os matricis coartatur, propter apostema calidum quod accidit ei: tunc non oportet ut laboretur super ipsum, imo oportet tunc administrare effusionem rerum humidarum, pinguium: et administra emplastra: et sedeat in aquis quae mollificant et humectant.	If the mouth of the uterus is restricted due to a warm abscess that has occurred, then it is not necessary to work on it; rather, it is necessary to apply moist, fatty substances, apply poultices, and have her sit in waters that soften and moisten.
Quod si foetus est super latus suum, tunc possibile est ut aequetur: tunc administretur quod diximus in foetu uiuo.	If the fetus is on its side, then it is possible to straighten it; then apply the same treatment that we discussed for a live fetus.
Quod si non est possibile illud, tunc incidatur frustatim, et extrahatur.	If that is not possible, then it should be cut into pieces and extracted.
Et oportet ut non dimittas aliquid ex secundina intus omnino.	And it is necessary not to leave any part of the afterbirth inside at all.
Cum ergo compleueris operationem tuam, tunc administra quod diximus in apostematibus calidis quae accidunt in matricibus.	When you have completed your operation, then administer what we mentioned regarding warm abscesses that occur in the uterus.
Quod si accidat fluxus sanguinis, tunc descendat in aquis stipticis, et administra reliquam curationem.	If bleeding occurs, then let her sit in astringent waters and administer the remaining treatment.
Et ego quidem iam uidi mulierem, in cuius uentre mortuus erat foetus: deinde impregnata est super ipsum uice alia, postea mortuus est foetus alius etiam.	I myself have seen a woman in whose womb a fetus had died; she then became pregnant again over it, and afterward that fetus also died.
Accidit ergo ei post tempus longum apostema in umbilico suo, et inflatum est, donec apertum est: et coepit emittere pus.	After a long time, an abscess developed in her navel, and it swelled until it opened and began to discharge pus.
Vocatus sum ergo ad curationem eius, et medicatus sum ei tempore longo: et non consolidatum est uulnus.	I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time, but the wound did not heal.
Posui ergo super ipsum ex quibusdam emplastris fortis attractionis: et exiuit ex loco os.	So I applied to it some poultices with strong drawing power, and a bone came out of the place.
Deinde praeterierunt ei dies aliquot, et exiuit os aliud.	Then, after a few days, another bone emerged.
Miratus sum ergo inde, cum in uentre non sit os.	I was amazed at this, since there are no bones in the womb.
Cogitaui ergo, quia erant ex ossibus foetus mortui.	So I thought that they were bones of the dead fetus.
Inquisiui ergo uulnus, et extraxi ossa multa, muliere existente in melioribus dispositionibus suis: et iam uixit taliter tempore longo, et mittit ex loco pus parum.	I therefore explored the wound and extracted many bones, the woman being in better health, and she continued to live in this condition for a long time, discharging a small amount of pus from the place.
Et ego non firmaui hic hoc extraneum, nisi quoniam in eo est scientia, et adiutorium ad illud, quod administrat medicus artifex cum manu ex curatione.	I record this unusual case here only because it contains knowledge and assistance for what the skillful physician accomplishes by hand in treatment.
¶ De formis Instrumentorum necessariorum in extractione foetus.	On the forms of instruments necessary for the extraction of the fetus.
Caput LXXVII.	Chapter 77.
Hic inferius est forma Strictorii, quo aequantur libri, cui aequaliter sunt duae uertigines in duabus extremitatibus duorum lignorum.	Below is the form of the press, by which books are aligned, having two equal pivots at the two ends of two wooden pieces.
Verumtamen haec Vertigo oportet ut sit subtilior strictorio: et ut fiat, aut ex ebano, aut ex ligno bussi.	However, this pivot should be finer than the press and should be made either of ebony or boxwood.
Et sit latitudo omnis ligni quasi duo digiti: et margo cuiusque amborum est quasi digitus unus, et longitudo cuiusque eorum est palmus et medietas: et in medio duorum lignorum sunt duo additamenta ex genere eiusdem ligni, quae iam firmata sunt in utrisque, quorum longitudo est medietas palmi et plus parum: et latitudo utriusque est quasi duo digiti, aut plus parum.	The width of each piece of wood should be about two fingers, with each side margin being about one finger, and the length of each piece is a palm and a half. In the middle of the two wooden pieces are two additional parts made of the same kind of wood, already fixed to each side, with a length of half a palm and slightly more, and the width of each is about two fingers, or a little more.
Et ista duo additamenta intromittuntur in os matricis, ut aperiatur cum eis quando tu reuoluis duas Vertigines.	These two additional parts are inserted into the mouth of the womb, to open it when you turn the two pivots.
Forma Vertiginis qua aperitur matrix.	The form of the pivot with which the womb is opened.
Forma alia ad simile illius, subtilior, et leuior.	Another form similar to it, finer and lighter.
Fiat ex ligno ebani, aut bussi, secundum similitudinem forcipum.	It should be made from ebony or boxwood, in the likeness of forceps.
Verumtamen in extremitate eius sint duo additamenta, sicut uides hic supra: et longitudo omnis additamenti ex eis est quasi palmus: et latitudo utriusque est, duo digiti.	However, at its end should be two additional parts, as you see above; the length of each part is about a palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
Cum ergo uis aperire matricem cum eo, tunc fac sedere mulierem super lectum, pendentibus pedibus eius, aperto quod est inter crura eius.	Therefore, when you wish to open the womb with it, have the woman sit on a bed with her feet hanging down and the area between her legs exposed.
Deinde intromitte ista duo additamenta coniuncta in matricem: et tu es tenens extremitatem instrumenti inferius inter coxas eius.	Then insert the two joined additional parts into the womb, holding the instrument's end below between her thighs.
Deinde aperi manum tuam cum instrumento, sicut facis cum forficibus, aequaliter secundum quantitatem quam uis ex apertione oris matricis, donec faciat Obstetrix quod uult.	Then open your hand with the instrument, as you would with scissors, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the womb, until the midwife achieves what she wants.
Forma Vertiginis alterius quam dixerunt antiqui Forma Impellentis quo impellitur foetus.	The form of another pivot which the ancients called the form of the pusher, with which the fetus is pushed.
Forma Almisdac, qua conteritur caput magnum: et assimilatur forcipi, cui sunt dentes in extremitate, sicut uides.	The form of the Almisdac, with which a large head is crushed; it resembles forceps with teeth at the end, as you see.
Et quandoque fit oblungum, sicut forcipes secundum hanc formam, sicut uides, cui sunt dentes sicut dentes serrae, quo inciditur et conteritur.	And it is sometimes made elongated, like forceps of this form, as you see, with teeth like those of a saw, with which it cuts and crushes.
Forma Almisdac quo conteritur caput paruum.	The form of the Almisdac with which a small head is crushed.
Forma Vncini habentis spinam unam.	The form of the hook with one spine.
Forma Vncini habentis spinas duas.	The form of the hook with two spines.
Forma forcipis cui sunt dentes serrae, cum quo conteritur caput foetus.	The form of forceps with serrated teeth, with which the head of the fetus is crushed.
Forma Spatumilis habentis duas extremitates ad abscindendum caput.	The form of the Spatumilis with two ends for cutting off the head.
Forma duorum Spatumilium etiam latorum.	The form of two wide Spatumilia.
Ista instrumenta omnia exercentur, et quanto plus multiplicantur species eorum, et praeparata sunt apud artificem, est uelocior ad operationem suam, et altior apud homines, propter quantitatem suam.	All these instruments are used, and the more their types are multiplied and prepared by the craftsman, the quicker they are for the operation and more esteemed by people, due to their quantity.
Non ergo despicies ex eis instrumentum, quin sit apud te praeparatum.	Therefore, do not disregard any of these instruments; have them prepared with you.
Inexcusabilis est enim necessitas eorum.	For their necessity is undeniable.
¶ De extractione Secundinae.	On the extraction of the afterbirth.
Caput LXXVIII.	Chapter 78.
Quando retinetur Secundina apud partum, tunc oportet ut praecipias infirmae, ut retineat anhelitum suum.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, then you should instruct the patient to hold her breath.
Deinde fac eam sternutare cum condisi: et stringe manum tuam super os eius, et nares ipsius.	Then make her sneeze with a condiment, and press your hand over her mouth and nose.
Si ergo egreditur per hoc, bonum est.	If it comes out as a result, it is good.
Si non: tunc accipe ollam, et perfora in coopertorio foramen: et pone in ea herbas aperientes os matricis, sicut calamentum, rutam, et anetum, et camomillam, et sseham, et cassiam ligneam, et centauream: accipe omnes istas herbas, aut quasdam earum, et submerge eas cum aqua, et pone eas super ignem.	If not, then take a pot and perforate a hole in the cover, and place in it herbs that open the mouth of the womb, like calamint, rue, dill, chamomile, sseha, cinnamon, and centaury; take all these herbs, or some of them, and submerge them in water, and place them on the fire.
Deinde pone embulam arundinis super foramen coopertorii ollae, et extremitatem aliam in os matricis: et teneat eam donec perueniat uapor ad concauitatem matricis.	Then place a reed tube over the hole in the cover of the pot, and place the other end in the mouth of the womb; let her hold it until the vapor reaches the cavity of the womb.
Deinde fac eam sternutare, sicut diximus.	Then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Secundina enim egredietur cum facilitate.	For the afterbirth will come out with ease.
Si autem remaneat post hanc curationem, et non egrediatur: tunc praecipe Obstetrici, ut submergat manum suam in oleo sisamino, aut mucillagine alteae.	If it remains after this treatment and does not come out, then instruct the midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil or marshmallow mucilage.
Deinde intromittat in uuluam, et quaerat cum ea Secundinam.	Then she should insert her hand into the vulva and search for the afterbirth with it.
Cum ergo inuenerit eam, tunc accipiat eam, et extendat ipsam paulatim.	When she finds it, then she should take hold of it and gently stretch it out little by little.
Si autem fuerit annexa in profundo matricis, tunc intromittat manum, secundum quod narrauimus, donec quando inuenerit Secundinam, et extrahat eam paulatim secundum rectitudinem, ut non cadat matrix apud attractionem uehementem: imo oportet, ut permutetur cum facilitate ad latera dextra et sinistra: deinde addatur in quantitatem attractionis.	But if it is attached deep within the womb, she should insert her hand, as we have described, until she finds the afterbirth, and pull it out gradually in a straight line, so the womb does not fall due to forceful traction; rather, it should be moved gently to the right and left sides, then more traction may be applied as needed.
Ipsa enim obedit tunc, et seruatur, et euadit ab adhaerentia.	Then it yields, is freed, and escapes from its adherence.
Quod si os matricis est coartatum, sicut nos iam narrauimus: cura eam cum sternutatione, et ex medicatione ollae cum herbis.	If the mouth of the womb is constricted, as we have already described, treat her with sneezing and the medication from the pot with herbs.
Si autem non egreditur cum omnibus quae narrauimus, tunc caue ne fatigeris super eam in iteratione extractionis.	If it does not come out with everything we have described, then be careful not to exhaust her with repeated extractions.
Verum oportet, ut quod egreditur ad os matricis ex ea, liges ad coxam mulieris.	Instead, it is proper to tie what comes out at the mouth of the womb to the woman's hip.
Deinde clisteriza eam cum unguento tetrapharmacon.	Then administer a clyster with tetrapharmacon ointment.
Ipsum enim putrefaciet eam post dies, et dissoluetur, et egredietur.	For this will cause it to decay over days, dissolve, and come out.
Verumtamen quando putrefit, eleuatur ex ea odor malus ad stomachum et caput, et laedit illud infirmam.	However, when it decays, a foul odor will rise from it to her stomach and head, harming the patient.
Oportet ergo ut administrentur suffumigationes conuenientes ad illud.	Therefore, suitable fumigations should be administered for this.
Quidam autem antiquorum iam experti sunt suffumigationem nasturtii, et ficuum siccarum.	Some of the ancients have tried fumigations with watercress and dried figs.
Forma instrumenti quo suffumigatur mulier apud retentionem Secundinae et menstruorum.	The form of the instrument with which a woman is fumigated for retention of the afterbirth and menstruation.
Fiat ex uitro simile alcama, aut ex zere: et ponatur extremitas ampla super ignem: et suffumigatio sit posita super prunas: teneat eam, donec consumatur illa suffumigatio: et itera aliam.	It should be made of glass similar to alcama, or from bronze; place the wide end over the fire, and the fumigation is placed on the embers; she should hold it until the fumigation is consumed, and repeat another.
¶ De curatione Ani non perforati.	On the treatment of an imperforate anus.
Caput LXXIX.	Chapter 79.
Nascuntur multi puerorum, et Ani eorum sunt non perforati, quos iam opilauit sifac subtile.	Many children are born with their anuses not perforated, which a delicate membrane has obstructed.
Oportet ergo, ut obstetrix perforet illud sifac digito suo: et si non, perforet ipsum cum Spatumili acuto: et caueat lacertum, ne tangat eum.	Therefore, the midwife should perforate that membrane with her finger; if not, she should perforate it with a sharp Spatumili and be careful not to touch the muscle.
Deinde pone super ipsum lanam infusam in uino et oleo.	Then place wool soaked in wine and oil over it.
Deinde cura ipsum cum ungentis, donec sanetur.	Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
Si autem times quod opiletur, tunc pone in foramine cannulam de plumbo diebus multis, et auferatur quando puer uult egerere.	If you fear it may become obstructed, place a lead tube in the opening for many days, and remove it when the child wants to evacuate.
Et iam accidit opilatio Ani etiam ex consolidatione uulneris, aut apostematis.	Sometimes obstruction of the anus also occurs due to wound healing or an abscess.
Oportet ergo ut secetur illa consolidatio, deinde curetur cum eo quod diximus ex curatione et plumbo.	Therefore, that hardened area should be cut, then treated as we described, with healing and lead.
¶ De curatione Fistularum quae accidunt in inferiori parte.	On the treatment of fistulas occurring in the lower part.
Caput LXXX.	Chapter 80.
Fistulae quae accidunt in inferiori, sunt Nodatio, et Grossitudo quae accidunt prope anum deforis: aut in spacio unius partium: et est Fistula una, aut plures.	Fistulas that occur in the lower area are knotted growths and thicknesses that appear near the outside of the anus or in the space of one of the parts, and there may be one fistula or several.
Cum ergo antiquatur illa Nodatio, aperitur, et currit ex ea humiditas aquosa alba, aut pus subtile.	When this knotty growth becomes old, it opens, and a watery white moisture or thin pus flows from it.
Et quandoque sunt ex istis Fistulis penetrantes.	And sometimes these fistulas are penetrating.
Ergo penetrantes cognoscuntur per illud quod egreditur ex egestione, et uentositate, quando utitur infirmus egestione: et fortasse egreditur ex eis uermis.	Penetrating fistulas are recognized by the matter that exits with stools and gas when the patient evacuates; sometimes worms may emerge from them.
Et sunt ex eis Fistulae quando sunt in spacio penetrantes usque ad uesicam, et usque ad meatum uirgae.	Some fistulas, when they are in a certain position, penetrate as far as the bladder and to the urethra.
Et sunt ex eis penetrantes usque ad iuncturam coxae, et usque ad nodum caudae.	Some penetrate as far as the hip joint and to the coccygeal junction.
Ex eo autem quo cognoscitur Fistula penetrans usque ad anum, etiam a non penetrante, est, ut intromittas digitum tuum indicem in anum: et intromittas tentam subtilem in Fistulam ex aere, aut ferro: quando non est tortuositas.	To determine if a fistula penetrates to the anus, as opposed to a non-penetrating one, insert your index finger into the anus and a thin probe of brass or iron into the fistula when it is not twisted.
Quod si in ea est tortuositas, tunc intromitte in eam tentam ex plumbo subtilem, aut pilum ex pilis equarum, donec sentias tentam, aut pilum in digito tuo.	If there is a twist in it, then insert a thin lead probe into it, or a strand of horsehair, until you feel the probe or hair with your finger.
Quod si non sentis ipsam penitus, neque procedit ex foramine aliquid ex egestione, neque uentositas, neque uermis sicut dixi: tunc scias, quia est non penetrans: propera ergo ad curationem.	If you do not feel it at all, nor does anything exit from the opening with stool, nor gas, nor worms as I mentioned, then know that it is non-penetrating; proceed, therefore, with the treatment.
Et quando Fistula est penetrans usque ad uesicam, aut ad meatum urinae: tunc significatio eius est exitus urinae ex ea, et prohibitio eius ab hoc ut consolidetur locus cum medicinis.	When the fistula penetrates to the bladder or the urinary tract, this is indicated by urine exiting from it, and it will resist healing with medication.
Si uero est penetrans usque ad iuncturam coxae, aut ad os coxae: tunc signum eius est, quod perueniat tenta usque illuc, si non est in ea tortuositas usque ad os: et inuentio doloris in circumitu partis, et quod egreditur pus ex ea semper: et quod non ualeat in ea medicatio, neque consolidatur cum unguento.	If, however, it penetrates as far as the hip joint or the hip bone, the sign is that the probe reaches there without twisting, pain is felt around the area, pus constantly discharges from it, and it does not respond to medication or heal with ointments.
Et in istis Fistulis omnibus penetrantibus non est curatio omnino: et curatio earum est labor et uanitas ei, ex stultis medicis, super quem formatur.	For all these penetrating fistulas, there is absolutely no cure, and treatment is merely labor and futility at the hands of foolish physicians who attempt it.
In illa autem quae non est penetrans, et non antiqua, speratur sanatio cum serro: secundum quod ego narro tibi, et ego iam probaui: et est, ut iaceat infirmus inter manus tuas super dorsum suum: et eleua crura eius usque supra coxas ipsius, et coxae eius sint inclinatae ad uentrem ipsius.	For a fistula that is non-penetrating and not old, healing may be hoped for with a cautery, as I describe to you, having tested it myself. The patient should lie in your arms on his back, with his legs raised above his hips, and his hips bent toward his abdomen.
Deinde intromittetentam plumbi, aut aeris, si est in Fistula tortuositas, donec scias ubi peruenit tenta.	Then, insert a lead or brass probe if there is twisting in the fistula, so you can determine how far the probe reaches.
Si autem sentit eam infirmus circa anum, tunc oportet ut intromittas digitum tuum indicem in anum.	If the patient feels it near the anus, then you should insert your index finger into the anus.
Si ergo sentis in digito tuo tentam iam penetrasse per seipsam detectam, praeter quod sentias inter digitum tuum, et inter ipsum sifac, aut carnem: tunc ergo scias certe, quia est penetrans: non ergo labores in ea, quoniam non est eius sanatio, sicut diximus.	If you feel the probe with your finger, penetrating by itself, but sense a membrane or flesh between your finger and it, then know for certain that it is penetrating. Therefore, do not waste effort on it, as there is no cure, as we have said.
Dixerunt tamen, quia sanatur in quibusdam hominibus caro, et ex medicatione qua ei speratur iuuamentum, est, ut ignias cauterium subtile secundum amplitudinem Fistulae, sicut praecessit, et intromittas ipsum ignitum in Fistulam, donec perueniat circa anum.	However, it has been said that, in some people, tissue may heal, and a helpful treatment would be to heat a thin cautery to fit the width of the fistula as previously described, and insert the heated cautery into the fistula until it reaches near the anus.
Deinde itera illud bis, aut ter, donec scias, quia iam adustae sunt omnes illae carnes additae filtratae, quae sunt similes cannulae pennae auis.	Then repeat this process two or three times until you know that all the added, fibrous tissues, which resemble a bird’s feather quill, have been burned.
Deinde cura illud cum liciniis inuolutis in butyro, donec egrediantur illae carnes, quae adustae sunt: deinde cura illud cum unguentis generantibus carnem et consolidantibus.	Then treat it with wicks soaked in butter until the burned tissues are expelled, then treat it with ointments that generate and consolidate new flesh.
Si ergo sanatur, bonum est.	If it heals, that is good.
Et si non, tunc non sanatur cum alia curatione unquam.	If it does not heal, then it will never heal with any other treatment.
Et si egreditur tenta, et non peruenerit usque ad digitum tuum, qui est in ano, et est inter ipsum et tentam uelamen spissum ex carne, aut sifac: et uides Fistulam in eo quod sequitur superficiem cutis, tunc seca cutem ab initio Fistulae, et tu uadis secando cum tenta quod est in fistula, donec perueniat secatio ubi peruenit tentae extremitas, et liberatur tenta et cadit.	If the probe exits but does not reach your finger in the anus, and there is a thick membrane of flesh or a membrane between the probe and your finger, and you see the fistula near the skin's surface, then cut the skin from the fistula's start, cutting alongside the probe in the fistula until the incision reaches the probe’s end, freeing it to fall.
Deinde mundifica illas carnes filtratas, quae assimilantur cannulae pennae auis, ut non remaneat ex eis aliquid.	Then clean out those fibrous tissues that resemble the hollow shaft of a bird’s feather so that nothing remains.
Si autem uincit te sanguis, et soluit inter te et inter operationem tuam ut seces illas carnes: tunc melius quod fit, et uelocioris iuuamenti, cauterizare eam cum igne, aut cum medicina acuta.	If blood overwhelms you and disrupts your operation to cut away these tissues, then it is better and faster to cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Quoniam cauterium cum igne aggregat habitudines bonas, adustionem illarum carnium additarum, et abscisionem sanguinis, et exiccationem humiditatum.	For cautery with fire gathers beneficial conditions: burning away the added tissues, stopping bleeding, and drying up moisture.
Deinde cura illud cum liciniis inuolutis in butyro, aut caulibus tritis, donec locus emittat pus, et egrediantur illae carnes adustae in pus.	Then treat it with wicks soaked in butter or mashed cabbage until the area discharges pus and the burned tissues are expelled as pus.
Deinde cura tunc uulnus cum unguentis consolidatiuis, generantibus carnem duram: et sunt medicinae in quibus sunt stipticitas et exiccatio.	Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments that generate firm flesh; these are medicines with astringency and drying properties.
Nam quando restaurantur, tunc iam sanatur: et non times iterationem.	For once they are restored, the wound is healed, and you need not fear recurrence.
Si autem Fistula iam peruenit usque ad profundum ani, et elongatur a superfluitate corporis: tunc intromitte digitum tuum in anum, et inquire cum eo.	If the fistula has already reached deep into the anus and extends far within the body, then insert your finger into the anus and examine with it.
Si ergo sentis tentam, et inter te, et inter eam est uelamen ex sifac, aut carne, et est propinqua penetrationi: tunc non est operatio in illo, nisi secundum uiam fiduciae et spei.	If you feel the probe, and there is a membrane or flesh between you and it, and it is close to penetration, then there is no further operation except to proceed with hope and trust.
Quod est, quia administratur in eo unus trium modorum: aut ut cauterizes ipsam, sicut diximus: aut seces eam, donec consequaris concauitatem eius, ut sit possibile tibi intromittere licinia, et curationem ex proximo.	This means that one of three methods can be applied: either cauterize it, as we have said; or cut it until you reach its cavity, making it possible for you to insert wicks and administer treatment closely.
Et non procedas multum cum sectione, ut non incidas lacertum continentem anum, et accidat super infirmum exitus egestionis absque uoluntate.	Do not proceed too far with the incision, so as not to cut the muscle that holds the anus, which could result in involuntary discharge for the patient.
Deinde cura illud cum eo quod diximus.	Then treat it with the methods we have described.
Fortasse enim sanabitur: aut elonges ipsum uelamen, et mundes ipsum postquam secas ipsum usque prope anum, sicut diximus, aut cum tenta, aut cum instrumento alio acutae extremitatis.	Perhaps it may heal, or you may cut away this membrane and clean it after making an incision near the anus, as we described, either with a probe or with another instrument with a sharp tip.
Deinde mundifica illas carnes filtratas quae sunt in sectione, usque ubi potes cum perscrutatione.	Then clean out those fibrous tissues that are in the incision, probing as far as you are able.
Deinde conare restaurationem uulneris totius cum sectione, et orificio superiore ubi consolidatur: et remanet Fistula aperta in interiore parte anus, et erit leuius super infirmum.	Next, attempt the restoration of the entire wound by keeping the incision and upper opening where it can consolidate, leaving the fistula open in the inner part of the anus, which will ease the burden on the patient.
Et quandoque suitur Fistula secundum hunc modum: et est, quando intromittis tentam in Fistulam: et est in latere ani circa superficiem corporis cum cute et margine ani: tunc accipe tentam perforatae extremitatis, quae est sicut acus aleskef, id est, praeparantium coria, secundum hanc formam.	Sometimes, the fistula is sutured according to this method: insert a probe into the fistula, which is located along the side of the anus near the body surface with skin and edge of the anus. Then take a probe with a perforated tip, similar to an awl used for leatherworking, shaped as described here.
Et intromitte in eam filum inuolutum ex quinque filis, et circiter ea.	Then insert into it a thread wrapped from five strands, and secure it around the probe.
Deinde intromitte tentam cum filo in Fistulam, donec consequatur concauitatem eius.	Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula until it reaches its cavity.
Si ergo est penetrans in margine ani interius prope, tunc extrahe filum ex illo foramine: ita ut intromittas digitum tuum in anum, et extrahas extremitatem fili, et aggreges duas extremitates simul: et stringe utramque, et dimitte illud die uno, aut duobus diebus: et quanto plus incidit filum in carne, stringe ipsum bene, donec incidantur illae carnes quae sunt inter duas extremitates fili, et cadant: deinde cura uulnus, donec consolidetur, et sanetur.	If the fistula penetrates close to the inner edge of the anus, then extract the thread from that opening by inserting your finger into the anus and pulling out the end of the thread. Tie the two ends together, tighten them, and leave it for one or two days. As the thread cuts further into the flesh, tighten it well until the tissue between the two ends of the thread is cut through and falls away. Then treat the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
Si autem orificium Fistulae non est penetrans: tunc fac ipsum penetrare quocunque modo praeparatur tibi, nisi sit in profundo multum.	If the fistula’s opening is not penetrating, then make it penetrate in any way available to you, unless it is very deep.
Non enim inest tibi, ut facias illud propter lacertum, ut non incidas ipsum.	If it reaches the muscle, you must take care not to cut into it.
Deinde fac cum ea sicut diximus, donec sanetur.	Then proceed as we have described until it is healed.
Forma Spatumilis spinosi quo finditur Fistula, cuius curuitas est acuta ualde, et pars altera est non acuta, ut non incidat illud quod non est necesse, sicut uides.	This is the form of the spined spatumilis used for splitting the fistula, with one end sharply curved, while the other end is blunt to avoid cutting unnecessarily, as you see.
¶ De sutura Hemorroidarum, ex quibus currit sanguis ex incisione earum: et cura fissurarum.	On the suture of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows after their incision: and on the treatment of fissures.
Caput LXXXI.	Chapter 81.
Sunt Hemorroides secundum duos modos.	Hemorrhoids exist in two forms.
Aut enim sunt intra anum, similes uesicis carbonum, uel prunarum: aut quasi ipsae sint grana uuae.	They are either inside the anus, resembling blisters of charcoal or embers, or as if they were like grapes.
Et ex eis sunt paruae, et magnae: et sanguis currit ex eis semper, et est una, et sunt multae.	And among them are small and large ones; blood flows from them constantly, and there is one, or there are many.
Et sunt extra anum, et in extremitatibus eius.	And they are outside the anus, and on its edges.
Verumtamen istae quae sunt extra anum, sunt secundum plurimum paucae humiditatis, ex quibus currit aqua citrina, aut parum sanguinis cursu assiduo: et sunt secundum colorem corporis.	However, those that are outside the anus usually have little moisture, from which yellowish fluid or a small amount of blood flows steadily, and they are the same color as the body.
Et curatio eius quae est intra anum, est, ut praecipias infirmo ut assellet: et exprimatur, donec egrediatur anus, et appareant athelil tibi.	And the treatment for those inside the anus is to instruct the patient to sit; then press, until the anus emerges, and the hemorrhoids appear to you.
Propterea ergo et suspende cum uncinis: aut tene eos cum ungue tuo.	Therefore, suspend them with hooks, or hold them with your fingernail.
Deinde incide eos apud radices suas.	Then cut them at their roots.
Si autem non retinentur in eis uncini, propter humiditatem eorum et ipsorum mollificationem: tunc cape eos cum panno aspero, aut cum coto ex diploide lanea, et extrahe eos cum digitis tuis.	If the hooks do not hold them, due to their moisture and softening, then grasp them with a rough cloth or woolen fabric, and extract them with your fingers.
Deinde incide eos, et pulueriza super eos post incisionem quosdam pulueres calidos, ut stent eis loco cauterii.	Then cut them, and sprinkle some warm powders on them after the incision, so they act as a substitute for cauterization.
Aut cauteriza eos secundum quod praecessit in capitulo cauterizandi.	Or cauterize them as described previously in the chapter on cauterization.
Deinde cura eos cum reliqua curatione, donec sanentur.	Then treat them with the remaining treatment until they heal.
Quod si non obedit anus egressioni, tunc clisteriza infirmum clisteri in quo sit mordicatio parua, ut lauetur cum eo quod est in ano, et obediat egressioni uelociter, quando exprimit se infirmus.	If the anus does not yield to egress, then administer an enema with a mild irritant to cleanse the anus, and so that it yields to egress quickly when the patient presses.
Si autem athelil sunt extrinseci ab ano, tunc res eorum est leuis, facilis: et est ut capias eos cum ungue tuo, aut capias eos cum uncino, et incidas eos.	If the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then their treatment is light, easy: just grasp them with your fingernail or a hook and cut them.
Deinde cura eos cum eo quod diximus, donec sanentur.	Then treat them as described, until they heal.
Et qui abhorret incisionem cum ferro, tunc oportet ut administres suturam eorum secundum hunc modum.	And if someone shuns incision with iron, then it is necessary to perform their suture according to this method.
Accipe filum inuolutum, et intromitte ipsum in acum.	Take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle.
Deinde extrahe athelil ad superiora, et fac ipsum penetrare cum acu in radice eius ex parte altera: et inuolue duas extremitates fili, in inferiori parte acus, et sint latitudinaliter: et stringe athelil strictura forti.	Then pull the hemorrhoid upwards, and make the needle penetrate at its root from the other side; wrap the two ends of the thread at the lower part of the needle, laying them crosswise, and tie the hemorrhoid tightly.
Deinde noda filum, et extrahe acum.	Then knot the thread and remove the needle.
Fac illud cum omnibus athelil, et dimitte ex eis unum: nec suas ipsum, ut currat ex eo superfluitas sanguinis.	Do this with all the hemorrhoids, but leave one unsutured so that excess blood may flow from it.
Deinde pone super anum pannum infusum in oleo rosato, aut caeroto, et pone ipsum super anum: et praecipe infirmo, ut quiescat.	Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or carrot oil on the anus, and instruct the patient to rest.
Deinde dimitte ipsum, donec cadat.	Then leave it alone until it falls off.
Cum ergo cadunt athelil, cura eos cum unguentis, et reliqua curatione, donec sanentur.	When the hemorrhoids fall off, treat them with ointments and the remaining care until they heal.
¶ De cura Fissurarum.	On the treatment of fissures.
Multotiens enim accidunt ex exiccatione stercoris, et constrictione naturae.	They often occur due to the drying of stool and the constriction of nature.
Cum ergo antiquantur, et non ualet in eis medicina: tunc oportet ut radas cum puncta Spatumilis, aut cum ungue tuo, donec fiant humidae, et auferatur ab eis cortex superior qui prohibet eas a consolidatione.	When they become chronic and medicine has no effect, it is necessary to scrape them with the point of a Spatumila, or with your fingernail, until they become moist, and the upper crust that prevents them from healing is removed.
Deinde cura eas, donec consolidentur secundum quod oportet.	Then treat them until they heal properly.
Si autem non consolidantur: tunc itera eas cum rasione uehementiori quam prima, donec sanguinentur multum, et excorientur deinde cura eas, donec sanentur.	If they do not heal, then repeat the scraping more vigorously than the first time until they bleed significantly and the surface is removed; then treat them until they heal.
¶ De curatione Almirmar inuersorum, et non inuersorum: et Athelil siccorum, et Formicae.	On the treatment of inward and outward Almirmar, and of dry Athelil, and of Formica.
Caput LXXXII.	Chapter 82.
Scias quod Almirmar non est nisi nodus rotundus secundum colorem corporis, similis capiti claui: et fit in toto corpore, praecipue in inferioribus partibus pedum, et digitis: et accidit ex eis dolor apud ambulationem.	Know that Almirmar is nothing but a round knot of the same color as the body, similar to the head of a nail; it appears on the entire body, especially on the lower parts of the feet and toes, and causes pain when walking.
Oportet ergo ut secetur quod est in circumitu claui, et teneatur cum forficibus, aut cum uncino, et eradicetur ex radice sua.	Therefore, it is necessary to cut around the nail, hold it with forceps or a hook, and remove it from its root.
Deinde cura illud: et si uis cauteriza illud secundum quod praecessit in capitulo suo.	Then treat it; and if you wish, cauterize it as was previously discussed in its chapter.
Ex athelil autem siccis unus est eminentia parua, aspera, filtrata, rotunda supra superficiem corporis.	As for dry Athelil, it is a small, rough, filtered, round prominence on the surface of the body.
Et multotiens accidunt in manibus puerorum.	And it often occurs on the hands of children.
Et curatio eius est, ut extendas athelil, et incidas ipsum: aut stringas ipsum cum filo de serico: aut cum pilo, donec cadat.	The treatment for it is to stretch the Athelil and cut it, or to tie it with a silk thread or hair until it falls off.
Et si uis, cauteriza ipsum secundum quod praemissum est cum igne, aut cum medicina acuta: et iam eradicantur athelil inuersi, et non inuersi cum instrumento quod ego dicam.	And if you wish, cauterize it as mentioned before, either with fire or with sharp medicine; and now both inward and outward Athelil are eradicated with the instrument I will describe.
Formica autem est etiam eminentia parua filtrata, grossa, super superficiem corporis, uadens in profundum ualde: et quando inuenit eam frigus, sentitur in ea simile mordicationi formicae, et fit in corpore toto: et plurimum eius fit in manibus.	Formica is also a small, thick, filtered prominence on the surface of the body, going very deep; and when cold reaches it, it feels like an ant's bite, appearing all over the body, especially on the hands.
Et curatio eius est, ut accipias cannulam ex penna anseris, aut penna uulturis forti: et pone illam cannulam super Formicam, donec contineat circulus cannulae ex partibus eius.	The treatment for it is to take a tube from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and place that tube over the Formica until the tube's circle encloses it.
Deinde reuolue manum tuam cum cannula, donec seces quod est in circumitu Formicae: et ponas eam in profundo carnis, et eradices Formicam ex radice eius.	Then twist your hand with the tube until you cut around the Formica; insert it deep into the flesh and remove the Formica from its root.
Et si uis, fac illud cum cannula aeris, aut ferri, secundum hanc formam.	And if you wish, do this with a tube of brass or iron, in this manner.
Sit superius cannulae ad sublimitatem trahens surdum inuolutum, ut alleuietur super digitum apprehensio eius et ipsius reuolutio.	Let the top of the tube have a raised and rounded cover so that handling and twisting it over the finger is eased.
Et si uis cauteriza Formicam secundum quod praemissum est in cauterizatione Athelil in capitulo de cauterio.	And if you wish, cauterize the Formica as previously discussed in the cauterization of Athelil in the chapter on cautery.
¶ De formis Instrumentorum quae administrantur ad Clisteria in aegritudinibus Ani, et solutionis uentris, et colicae.	On the forms of instruments used for enemas in illnesses of the anus, diarrhea, and colic.
Caput LXXXIII.	Chapter 83.
Quandoque Clistere fit ex argento, aut ex aurichalco, aut ex aere fuso, aut malleato.	Sometimes the enema device is made of silver, or brass, or cast or hammered bronze.
Et quandoque fit ex istis Instrumentis paruum, et magnum, secundum illos in quibus administrantur.	And sometimes these instruments are made small or large, depending on the patient for whom they are administered.
Illud ergo quod administratur in curatione puerorum paruorum, sit paruum: et quorum ani sunt debiles, aut dolorosi, sic et clisteria eorum.	Therefore, that which is administered in treating small children should be small, and for those whose anus is weak or painful, so should be their enema devices.
Clistere magnum.	Large enema.
Clistere paruum.	Small enema.
Canna eius, id est, caput superius in quo ligatur uter, sit amplum secundum hunc modum: et sit ei distinctio ut ligetur uter sicut uides, et extremitas eius inferior quae intromittitur in anum, sit surda, id est, non aperta, lenis, ualde, trahens ad subtilitatem: et in uno laterum eius sint duo foramina, et in latere altero foramen unum.	Its tube, that is, the upper part to which the reservoir is tied, should be wide in this way, with a separation so that the reservoir can be fastened as you see, and its lower end, which is inserted into the anus, should be blunt, that is, not open, very smooth, tapering to a thin point; and on one side, it should have two holes, and on the other side, one hole.
Et sit amplitudo foraminis secundum grossitudinem radiorum, et grossius parum, et sit uter in quo ponuntur medicinae ex uesica animalis: aut ex charta ouis, quae sit secundum formam asofrati paruae: cuius radix sit palmus unus.	The diameter of the holes should be about the thickness of spokes, and slightly thicker, and the reservoir in which the medicines are placed should be made from the bladder of an animal or from egg parchment, shaped like a small bag, with a base of one palm in length.
Et perforetur foraminibus multis sicut reuoluitur, et sit spacium quod est inter omne foramen grossitudo digiti.	And it should be pierced with many holes all around it, with the space between each hole about the width of a finger.
Deinde intromitte in illa foramina filum forte ex filo crudo, quod sit ex decem filis, aut circiter ea, et aggrega cum eo utrem sicut asofrati.	Then insert a strong thread of raw fiber, made of ten strands or so, into these holes, and tie it around the reservoir like a small bag.
Cum ergo ponitur in eo uter, stringatur in capite clisteris inter duo distinguentia constrictione forti.	When the reservoir is placed on it, tie it tightly at the top of the enema device between the two separations.
Deinde clisteriza cum eo.	Then administer the enema with it.
Et haec est forma circuli utris hic depicta, et foraminum.	And this is the form of the reservoir's circle and the holes depicted here.
Qualitas autem clisterizandi cum eo, est: ut impleas utrem, aut uesicam ex medicina, quae sit calefacta secundum quantitatem tolerantiae infirmi: et caue ne sit calida ualde, aut frigida ualde.	The method of administering the enema with it is to fill the reservoir or bladder with medicine, warmed to the tolerance level of the patient; and be careful that it is not too hot or too cold.
Deinde resupinetur infirmus super dorsum suum, et eleuet crura sua ad superiora: et pone sub eo inthaan, id est, corium super quod iacent homines, aut linteamen.	Then the patient should lie on their back and raise their legs upward, and place beneath them a pad, that is, leather on which people lie, or a cloth.
Deinde inunge extremitatem Clisteris cum oleo, aut cum albugine oui, aut cum mucillagine foenugraeci, aut similium.	Then anoint the end of the enema device with oil, egg white, fenugreek mucilage, or similar substances.
Deinde intromitte ipsum in anum cum facilitate.	Then gently insert it into the anus.
Deinde accipiat minister utrem cum duabus manibus suis simul, et exprimat ipsum cum uehementia, donec euacuet totum quod est in Clisteri in intestinum.	Then the assistant should take the reservoir with both hands and squeeze it forcefully until it empties everything from the device into the intestine.
Deinde extrahe Clistere, et eleuet infirmus crura sua ad parietem.	Then remove the enema device, and the patient should raise their legs against the wall.
Quod si medicina cogit eum ad exitum, tunc teneat quantum potest.	If the medicine urges him to expel, he should hold it as much as he can.
Et si dormit cum ea nocte tota, est magis ultimum in iuuamento.	And if he sleeps with it the entire night, it is most beneficial.
Si autem clisterizas eum in aegritudinibus solutionis uentris, et festinat exitus eius: tunc itera clistere, donec sanetur.	If you administer an enema for diarrhea, and he hurries to expel it, then repeat the enema until he is healed.
Quod si in ano sunt hemorroides, aut apostemata laedentia, tunc sit clistere subtile ualde, lene, ex clisteribus quibus clisterizantur pueri.	If there are hemorrhoids or painful abscesses in the anus, then use a very thin, gentle enema device, like those used for children.
Et haec sit forma clisteris subtilis super quod sit stricta cutis.	And this is the form of the thin enema device with a tightly wrapped covering.
¶ De curatione Vulnerum capitis sine fractura ossis.	On the treatment of head wounds without fracture of the bone.
Caput LXXXIIII.	Chapter 84.
Iam dixi in diuisione de curatione uulnerum quod conueniebat libro, et ego dicam hic curationem eorum cum manu, et cum medicinis secundum complementum.	I have already spoken in the section on wound treatment which pertains to the book, and here I will describe their treatment manually and with medicines in full.
Dico ergo, quod uulnera diuersificantur secundum illud quo fiunt uulnera, et secundum locum super quem cadit uulnus.	I say, therefore, that wounds vary depending on what causes them and the place where the wound occurs.
Res ergo quibus fiunt uulnera multotiens, sunt sicut iactus lapidis: aut incisio ensis, aut cultelli: aut percussio cum lancea, aut ligno, aut sagitta: et similibus illis ex rebus multis.	Thus, the objects that often cause wounds are things like the throw of a stone, the cut of a sword or knife, or a blow with a spear, wood, arrow, and similar objects.
Vulnera autem quae fiunt secundum loca corporis sunt, sicut uulnus quod cadit super caput, aut collum, aut pectus, aut uentrem, aut epar: et similia ex eis membris.	Wounds that occur in different parts of the body include wounds on the head, neck, chest, abdomen, liver, and similar parts.
Et ego sum narrans curationes quorundam uulnerum, ut ponam eam ratiocinationem et regulam super reliqua uulnera.	And I will narrate the treatments of certain wounds, to establish a rationale and rule for other wounds.
Et ego incipiam a uulneribus capitis simplicibus: quoniam rememoratio compositorum ueniet in principio capituli tertii.	And I will begin with simple head wounds, as the mention of complex wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Dico ergo.	I say, therefore.
Quando accidit in capite uulnus simplex, et non est fractura ossis: considera tunc, si est ex iactu lapidis, aut ei similibus, et iam fregit cutem tantum: et est uulnus magnum, et times super infirmum euentum apostematis calidi: tunc propera, et phlebotoma cephalicam statim: et non tardes illud: et extrahe ei ex sanguine secundum quantitatem uirtutis eius: si non fuerit prohibens aliquid a phlebotomia, praecipue si fuerit sanguis qui egreditur ex uulnere paucus.	When a simple head wound occurs and there is no fracture of the bone, consider then if it is from the throw of a stone or something similar, and it has only broken the skin: if the wound is large and you fear a hot abscess forming, then proceed quickly and perform a cephalic phlebotomy immediately; do not delay this, and extract blood according to the patient's strength, if there is no contraindication to phlebotomy, especially if there is little blood coming from the wound.
Et sit phlebotomia ex contrario partis uulneratae.	And let the phlebotomy be done on the side opposite to the wounded area.
Et caueat infirmus sibi a repletione, et uino, et cibis grossis.	And the patient should avoid overeating, wine, and heavy foods.
Si autem minutionem prohibet aliquid, tunc minoretur ex cibo, et non appropinquet carnibus, neque uinis.	If there is something preventing bloodletting, then reduce the food intake, and avoid meat and wine.
Et pone super uulnus si accidit ei apostema calidum, cotum infusum in oleo rosato solo, aut cum uino in quo est stipticitas.	And if a hot abscess forms on the wound, apply a cooked compress soaked in rose oil alone or with wine containing astringency.
Si autem securus fueris ab apostemate calido, tunc pone super uulnus, si est recens cum sanguine suo, et non mutauit ipsum aer, puluerem quem ego narrabo post paululum: et si iam mutauit ipsum aer, tunc pone super ipsum quaedam unguenta, donec sanetur.	If you are free from concern about a hot abscess, then apply to the wound, if it is fresh with its blood and has not yet been affected by the air, a powder I will describe shortly; if the air has already altered it, then apply certain ointments until it heals.
Si autem uulnus est magnum, aut est ex incisione ensis, et similium: et non aggregantur labia eius per puluillos, tunc aggrega ipsa cum sutura, secundum quod ego narrabo in uulneribus uentris de sutura eorum.	If the wound is large or caused by a sword cut or similar, and its edges do not come together with compresses, then bring them together with sutures, as I will describe in the treatment of abdominal wounds.
Si autem uulnus iam detectum est ab osse, et pendet, et non est retentio eius, nisi in suspensorio paruo: tunc incide ipsum.	If the wound is already exposed to the bone, is hanging, and only held in place by a small attachment, then cut it off.
Deinde cura uulnus cum medicinis, et restaura in eo carnem duram loco cutis, et praecipe infirmo, ut alatur cibis in quibus est grossitudo, sicut sunt capita, et triticum coctum, donec sit ut puls: et eis similia.	Then treat the wound with medicines and restore hard flesh in place of the skin, and instruct the patient to eat foods with substantial nourishment, such as heads and cooked wheat, until it is like porridge, and similar foods.
Quod si inuenis in cute putrefactionem, et non adhaeret ossi: tunc incide putrefactum totum, et proiice ipsum: deinde cura illud.	If you find putrefaction in the skin and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut off all the rotten part and remove it; then treat it.
Si autem in his uulneribus est arteria, aut uena ex qua fluit sanguis: et non abscinditur per medicinas, tunc inquire super arteriam.	If in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then locate the artery.
Si ergo inuenis eam non sectam, tunc seca eam cum Spatumili, aut liga eam.	If you find it unsevered, then cut it with a Spatumili or tie it.
Quod si necessitas prouocat quando non confert illud quod diximus, tunc cauteriza eam, donec abscindatur sanguis.	If necessity demands when what we mentioned does not work, then cauterize it until the bleeding stops.
Si autem uulnera ista sunt parua, simplicia, tunc res eorum est facilis, leuis: ita ut puluerizes super ea hunc puluerem: quoniam consolidat ea antequam mutet ea aer.	If these wounds are small and simple, then their treatment is easy and light: simply apply this powder over them, as it heals them before the air can affect them.
¶ Modus Pulueris incarnatiui.	The Method of the Healing Powder.
